**1. With reference to the evolution of the British administrative system in India, consider the following statements:**

1. The Charter Act of 1793 mandated the payment of a fixed annual sum to the British government from Indian revenues, a practice that continued until the Government of India Act, 1919.
2.  The Pitt's India Act established a dual system of governance, where the Governor-General held significant power while remaining accountable to the Board of Control in London.
3. The Charter Act of 1833 ended the East India Company's monopoly over trade with China and in tea, thereby opening these markets to other British entities.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. While the Charter Act of 1793 did indeed mandate an annual payment to the British government from Indian revenues, this practice was not continued until 1919.  The payment ceased much earlier. The Government of India Act, 1919, dealt with a different set of financial reforms, primarily focusing on the separation of central and provincial budgets.

Statement 2 is correct. The Pitt's India Act of 1784 did indeed establish a dual system of control over the East India Company's affairs in India.  The Board of Control in Britain oversaw the Company's activities, thereby establishing a system of checks and balances and limiting the Company's autonomy. The Governor-General, while exercising considerable power in India, was ultimately answerable to this British body.

Statement 3 is correct. The Charter Act of 1833 marked a significant shift in British policy toward India's trade.  It abolished the East India Company's monopoly on trade with China and in tea, opening these lucrative markets to private British traders and businesses. This act reflects the growing influence of laissez-faire economic principles in Britain and the desire to maximize economic benefits from India.  The other options are incorrect because they contain inaccuracies about the timelines and specifics of these crucial legislative acts.


**2. With reference to the Government of India Act 1919, consider the following statements:**

1.  The act introduced a bicameral legislature at the provincial level, consisting of a Council of State and a Legislative Assembly.
2. The Montagu-Chelmsford Reforms, which formed the basis of the 1919 Act, recommended granting voting rights to all women above the age of 21.
3.  The act introduced Dyarchy, dividing provincial subjects into "reserved" and "transferred," with the latter being administered by Indian ministers.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 3 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. The Government of India Act of 1919 introduced a bicameral legislature at the *central* level (Council of State and Legislative Assembly), not at the provincial level. Provincial legislatures remained unicameral under this act.

Statement 2 is incorrect. The Montagu-Chelmsford Reforms did not recommend granting voting rights to all women above 21. While the reforms did advocate for expanding the franchise,  universal female suffrage was not part of their recommendations.  The inclusion of women in the electorate happened gradually and through subsequent legislative acts.

Statement 3 is correct. The 1919 Act, based on the Montagu-Chelmsford Reforms, introduced the system of Dyarchy in the provinces.  This system divided administrative subjects into "reserved" (under the Governor's control) and "transferred" (under Indian ministers' control), representing a limited step towards self-governance.  The other options are incorrect due to the factual inaccuracies regarding the legislative structure and the scope of the Montagu-Chelmsford reforms concerning women's suffrage.


**3. With reference to the impact of the Charter Acts on the East India Company, consider the following statements:**

1. The Charter Act of 1833 led to the gradual phasing out of the East India Company's administrative functions, culminating in its dissolution in 1858.
2. The Charter Act of 1793 renewed the Company's trading privileges but also introduced stricter financial accountability to the British government.
3. The Charter Act of 1813 completely ended the Company's monopoly on trade within India, opening all markets to private enterprise.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 2 and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The Charter Act of 1833 started the process of diminishing the East India Company's administrative role. Though not immediately dissolved, the act significantly increased the power of the British Crown over India's governance, paving the way for the Company's eventual dissolution after the 1857 rebellion.

Statement 2 is correct. The Charter Act of 1793 indeed extended the East India Company's charter, thus renewing its trading rights.  However, it also introduced greater financial accountability, requiring the Company to pay a substantial sum to the British government from Indian revenues.  This marked a shift towards tighter British control over the Company's finances.

Statement 3 is incorrect. The Charter Act of 1813 did not completely end the Company's trade monopoly. While it did open up most of India's trade to private enterprise, the Company retained its exclusive rights to trade in tea and with China.  This partial liberalization of trade demonstrates the gradual nature of British policy changes concerning the East India Company's economic power.  Option (c) and (d) are incorrect because they include Statement 3 which is factually incorrect.


**4. Consider the following statements about the administrative reforms under Lord Cornwallis:**

1.  Cornwallis introduced the Permanent Settlement, granting proprietary rights to Zamindars in exchange for a fixed revenue payment to the British.
2.  He separated the functions of revenue collection and judicial administration, aiming to enhance efficiency and reduce corruption among District Collectors.
3.  Cornwallis's reforms resulted in the immediate and complete abolition of the Mahalwari system across British India.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 2 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct.  Lord Cornwallis's landmark administrative reform was the Permanent Settlement, a revenue system that granted Zamindars proprietary rights over their lands. In return, they were obligated to pay a fixed annual revenue to the British government. This system, while aiming to stabilize revenue collection, had significant long-term consequences for land ownership and agrarian relations.

Statement 2 is correct.  A key aspect of Cornwallis's reforms was the separation of revenue collection from judicial functions.  Previously, District Collectors held both responsibilities, leading to potential conflicts of interest and corruption. By separating these roles, Cornwallis aimed to improve the administration of justice and enhance the integrity of the revenue system.

Statement 3 is incorrect.  The Mahalwari system was not immediately and completely abolished by Cornwallis's reforms. This system, prevalent in certain parts of North India, continued to operate alongside the Permanent Settlement, which was primarily implemented in Bengal and some other regions. The Mahalwari system had its own evolution and modifications under subsequent British administrations.  Options (b), (c), and (d) are incorrect because they wrongly include Statement 3.


**5. With reference to the Indian Councils Act of 1861, consider the following statements:**

1. The Act established a bicameral legislature at the central level, granting significant legislative powers to the non-official members.
2. The Act granted legislative powers to the provincial governments of Bombay and Madras, which had been curtailed earlier.
3. The Act introduced a system of direct elections for non-official members of both the central and provincial legislative councils.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 2 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3
(d) 1 only


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. The Indian Councils Act of 1861 did not create a bicameral legislature at the central level. The central legislative council remained unicameral, and non-official members had limited legislative powers, primarily acting in an advisory capacity.  The Act expanded the council's size and included non-official members, but it did not fundamentally alter the power balance between the executive and legislature.

Statement 2 is correct.  A significant provision of the 1861 Act was the restoration of legislative powers to the provincial governments of Bombay and Madras. These powers had been restricted earlier, leading to greater centralization of power at the central level. The Act aimed to devolve some legislative authority back to the provinces.

Statement 3 is incorrect.  The 1861 Act did not introduce direct elections for non-official members of legislative councils.  Non-official members were nominated, mainly from elite sections of Indian society, not elected by the broader populace.  The principle of elected representation in Indian legislative bodies evolved gradually through subsequent legislative acts. Options (b), (c), and (d) are incorrect because they include either Statement 1 or Statement 3, or both, which are factually incorrect.

**1. Consider the following statements regarding 19th-century Indian social reform:**

1. Ishwar Chandra Vidyasagar's efforts primarily focused on promoting widow remarriage and opposing child marriage, while his involvement with the Brahmo Samaj was minimal.
2. Raja Ram Mohan Roy's reformist activities centered on advocating for monotheism and criticizing aspects of both Hinduism and Christianity,  but he played a minor role in the legalisation of widow remarriage.
3. Dayanand Saraswati's significant contribution was the establishment of the Arya Samaj,  and he had limited direct engagement in advocating for widow remarriage or opposing sati.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 3 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect.  While Ishwar Chandra Vidyasagar was indeed a key figure in the widow remarriage movement and a staunch opponent of child marriage, his association with the Brahmo Samaj was significant. He was a prominent member and actively participated in its reformist activities.  His work significantly overlapped with and contributed to the Brahmo Samaj's objectives.


Statement 2 is largely correct. Raja Ram Mohan Roy's primary focus was on religious reform, advocating for a monotheistic interpretation of Hinduism and critiquing certain practices within both Hinduism and Christianity.  Although he was a strong advocate for social reform, his direct involvement in the legalisation of widow remarriage was less prominent compared to Vidyasagar's direct action and advocacy.  His influence on the broader intellectual climate that fostered such reforms is undeniable, however.


Statement 3 is also largely correct. Dayanand Saraswati's main achievement was the founding of the Arya Samaj, a reformist movement that focused on a return to Vedic principles. While the Arya Samaj indirectly contributed to broader social reforms, Dayanand Saraswati's personal efforts were not directly focused on widow remarriage or the abolition of sati in the same way as Vidyasagar and Roy.  His focus was primarily religious and philosophical rather than directly legal and social, unlike Vidyasagar's concentrated efforts on legal and social change.  The Arya Samaj's later activities might have touched upon these issues, but Dayanand Saraswati's core work didn't center on them.

Therefore, only statement 2, albeit with nuances, presents the most accurate reflection of the individual's primary contributions within the context of 19th-century Indian social reform.


**2. With reference to the Vernacular Press Act (VPA) and its impact, consider the following statements:**

1. The VPA, enacted during Lord Lytton's tenure, was primarily aimed at suppressing the growing influence of vernacular newspapers critical of British policies.  Its repeal under Lord Ripon marked a significant step towards greater press freedom.
2.  The Som Prakash newspaper played a crucial role in highlighting the injustices of British rule and directly challenged the VPA's restrictions.  Its publication was instrumental in galvanizing public opinion against the act.
3. The VPA's impact was limited to the vernacular press in Bengal and did not significantly affect the English-language press or newspapers published in other regions of India.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct.  The Vernacular Press Act of 1878, passed under Lord Lytton, was a direct response to the growing criticism of British policies in the vernacular press.  The act imposed strict censorship and restrictions on the publication of content deemed seditious or critical of the government. Lord Ripon's subsequent repeal of the VPA in 1882 is widely seen as a move towards greater freedom of the press, though press freedom remained precarious throughout the colonial period.


Statement 2 is also largely correct. While pinpointing the specific role of *Som Prakash* in directly challenging the VPA might require further research, the fact remains that many vernacular newspapers actively voiced dissent against British rule and the VPA's restrictive measures.  These newspapers played a vital role in shaping public opinion and fueling resistance against the government.  The general impact of newspapers in this period is accurately reflected in the statement.


Statement 3 is incorrect. The VPA's impact extended beyond the vernacular press in Bengal and affected newspapers published in other regions of India and in other languages.  While the English-language press enjoyed more freedom, the VPA's restrictive spirit still cast a shadow over the entire journalistic landscape, impacting the freedom of expression across different linguistic and regional contexts.

Therefore, statements 1 and 2 accurately reflect significant aspects of the VPA, its impact, and the role of the vernacular press in challenging British policies.


**3. With reference to the early stages of British involvement in Indian governance, consider the following statements:**

1. The Regulating Act of 1773 established a Supreme Court in Calcutta with jurisdiction over all British subjects, regardless of their place of residence, but its jurisdiction over Indians was initially unclear and led to conflicts.
2. Warren Hastings, appointed Governor-General under the Regulating Act of 1773, effectively abolished the dual system of government, thus centralizing administrative power.
3. Pitt's India Act of 1784 strengthened British parliamentary control over the East India Company's affairs, creating a Board of Control to oversee the Company's actions in India, but ultimately it failed to curb the Company's aggressive expansionist policies.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The Regulating Act of 1773 did establish a Supreme Court in Calcutta, intending to provide a system of justice for British subjects.  However, the Act's wording regarding the court's jurisdiction over Indians was ambiguous, leading to significant jurisdictional conflicts between the Supreme Court and the Company's own courts and administrative structures.  This ambiguity created friction and legal complexities in the early years of British governance.


Statement 2 is incorrect.  Warren Hastings did not abolish the dual system of government. The dual system, characterized by a division of power between the Company and the Nawab, continued for several years after the Regulating Act.  Hastings' administrative reforms aimed at improving governance but did not fundamentally alter the structure of the dual system.  The system's abolition came later under different circumstances.


Statement 3 is correct. Pitt's India Act of 1784 did significantly increase British parliamentary oversight of the East India Company.  The Act created the Board of Control, giving the British government greater authority over the Company's affairs, including its financial matters and political actions in India. While the Act aimed to curb the Company's excesses, it did not completely prevent the Company's aggressive expansionist policies.  The Company's drive for territorial control and influence persisted even under the new regulatory framework.

Therefore, only statements 1 and 3 accurately reflect key aspects of the early British administrative reforms in India.



**4. With reference to the Government of India Act, 1935, consider the following statements:**

1. The Act completely abolished communal representation, establishing joint electorates for all communities.
2. The Act introduced provincial autonomy, granting significant self-governing powers to the provinces, but retained considerable control at the center.
3. The Act established a Federal Court, but its jurisdiction was limited, and the Privy Council in London remained the ultimate court of appeal for Indian matters.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. The Government of India Act, 1935, did *not* completely abolish communal representation. While it did make some provisions for joint electorates, it also continued the system of separate electorates for certain communities, particularly Muslims, which had been introduced earlier. The Act's failure to fully address the issue of communal representation contributed to the escalating tensions leading to the partition of India.


Statement 2 is correct. A major feature of the 1935 Act was the introduction of provincial autonomy. This involved granting significant self-governing powers to the provinces, including control over several legislative and administrative functions.  However, the central government retained considerable power and control over key areas, maintaining a degree of centralized authority.  The balance of power between the center and the provinces remained a point of contention.


Statement 3 is correct. The 1935 Act did establish a Federal Court in India. However, this court's jurisdiction was limited, and the Privy Council in London remained the ultimate court of appeal for Indian cases.  This preserved the ultimate judicial authority of the British Crown, even with the establishment of a more significant judicial body within India.

Therefore, statements 2 and 3 accurately represent key features of the Government of India Act, 1935.


**5. With reference to the evolution of the Indian Civil Service (ICS) under British rule, consider the following statements:**

1. The Charter Act of 1853 introduced open competitive examinations for recruitment to the ICS, ending the system of patronage, and immediately led to a significant increase in Indian representation within the service.
2.  The ICS examination was initially held only in England and in English, creating barriers for Indian candidates, while the age limit was gradually lowered, making it even more challenging for Indians to qualify.
3. The Lee Commission (1924) recommended a 50:50 parity between European and Indian recruits to the ICS within 15 years, a recommendation that was fully implemented, ensuring equitable representation.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 2 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. The Charter Act of 1853 did introduce open competitive examinations for the ICS, replacing the earlier system of patronage. However, this did *not* immediately lead to a significant increase in Indian representation.  The examinations were held in England, in English, and with age limits that disproportionately disadvantaged Indian candidates. The process of "Indianization" of the ICS was gradual and faced considerable resistance.


Statement 2 is correct. The ICS examinations were initially held exclusively in England and conducted in English, creating significant hurdles for Indian candidates.  Furthermore, the age limit for the examinations was gradually *lowered*, not raised, making it even more difficult for Indians to compete effectively against their British counterparts. This acted as a significant barrier to Indian participation in the higher echelons of the civil service.


Statement 3 is incorrect. The Lee Commission (1924) did recommend a 50:50 parity between European and Indian recruits to the ICS within 15 years. However, this recommendation was *not* fully implemented.  The process of Indianization continued, but it was slower and less complete than what the Lee Commission had envisioned.  The British government retained considerable control over the service, and full parity remained a distant goal throughout the colonial period.

Therefore, only statement 2 accurately reflects the challenges faced by Indian candidates seeking entry into the ICS during the British Raj.

**1. With reference to the Indian Councils Act of 1861, consider the following statements:**

1.  The Act established a bicameral legislature at the center, comprising a Council of State and a Legislative Assembly.
2.  The Act significantly expanded the Viceroy's Executive Council, increasing the number of members to at least twelve.
3.  The Act introduced direct elections for a portion of the non-official members in the Imperial Legislative Council.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (d) None

**Explanation:**

The Indian Councils Act of 1861 did not establish a bicameral legislature.  The legislative changes introduced by the act were limited to expanding the Governor-General's (later Viceroy's) Council for legislative purposes, creating the Imperial Legislative Council.  This Council was unicameral, not bicameral.  While the Act did allow for the addition of non-official members to the Governor-General's Legislative Council, the number was between six and twelve, not a fixed number of at least twelve as stated in statement 2.  Crucially, these non-official members were nominated, not directly elected, as statement 3 incorrectly claims. The Act laid the groundwork for increased Indian participation in the legislative process but did so through nomination, not election.  The introduction of elements of election would come later with subsequent acts. Therefore, none of the statements accurately reflect the provisions of the 1861 Act.  The options are designed to mislead by offering plausible but inaccurate interpretations of the Act's impact on the legislative structure and representation.


**2. With reference to the evolution of the Viceroy's authority, consider the following statements:**

1.  The title "Viceroy" formally replaced "Governor-General" under the Indian Councils Act of 1892, signifying enhanced power.
2.  The introduction of the "portfolio" system under Lord Curzon significantly strengthened the Viceroy's control over his executive council.
3.  The Government of India Act of 1858 explicitly limited the Viceroy's power to overrule decisions of his executive council.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 2 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (a) 2 only

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. The title "Viceroy," denoting the Crown's personal representative, was adopted following the Government of India Act, 1858, not the Indian Councils Act of 1892.  Statement 3 is also incorrect. The 1858 Act, while establishing the Executive Council, did not limit the Viceroy's ability to overrule council decisions. In fact, the opposite was true; the Viceroy's authority gradually increased over time.  Statement 2 is correct. The introduction of the portfolio system, where Executive Council members headed specific departments, streamlined administration and centralized power in the hands of the Viceroy. This system, while seemingly allowing for departmental autonomy, ultimately increased the Viceroy's overall control as he could now hold individual ministers accountable for their respective departments' performance.  The other options are designed as distractors, playing on common misconceptions regarding the evolution of the Viceroy's authority and the timing of key legislative changes.


**3. With reference to the Indian Councils Act, 1892, consider the following statements:**

1.  The Act significantly reduced the number of non-official members in both the Imperial and Provincial Legislative Councils.
2.  The Act introduced the principle of direct elections for all members of the Imperial Legislative Council.
3.  The Act allowed for the nomination of members to provincial councils by universities and chambers of commerce.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 3 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) 2 and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (b) 3 only

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. The 1892 Act actually *expanded* the number of non-official members in both the Imperial and Provincial Legislative Councils, not reduced it. This was a response to growing nationalist demands for greater Indian participation in the legislative process. Statement 2 is also incorrect. The Act did not introduce direct elections for *all* members. While it did introduce an element of indirect election for some non-official members, a substantial number were still nominated. This system of indirect election, involving recommendations from various bodies, was a step towards greater representation but fell short of full direct elections.  Statement 3 is correct. The Act did empower universities, district boards, municipalities, zamindars, trade bodies, and chambers of commerce to recommend members to provincial councils. This was a significant step towards broadening the representation within the councils and involved a form of indirect election. The other options are designed to create confusion by presenting plausible but incorrect assertions about the Act's impact on the composition and electoral processes of the legislative councils.


**4. Consider the following statements regarding the impact of the Government of India Act of 1858:**

1. The Act formally transferred the governance of India from the East India Company to the British Crown, ending the Company's rule.
2. The Act established a bicameral legislature in India, with an upper and lower house having equal powers.
3.  The Act mandated the appointment of an Indian as a member of the Viceroy's Executive Council.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (a) 1 only

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The Government of India Act of 1858 formally ended the East India Company's rule and transferred the governance of India to the British Crown. This marked a significant shift in the nature of British rule in India, although the practical implications took time to fully manifest. Statement 2 is incorrect. The Act did not establish a bicameral legislature.  The legislative reforms introduced later, particularly through the Indian Councils Acts, gradually expanded the legislative councils but did not create a full bicameral system with equal powers in the immediate aftermath of the 1858 Act.  Statement 3 is incorrect. The Act did not mandate the appointment of an Indian to the Viceroy's Executive Council. While the Act laid the foundation for increased Indian participation in the administration, the actual appointment of Indians to high office happened gradually over subsequent years through later legislative reforms and changes in administrative practices. The options function as distractors by blending accurate historical facts with inaccurate claims regarding the immediate consequences of the 1858 Act.  The question tests the examinee's understanding of the Act's immediate and long-term effects on the structure of governance and representation.


**5. With reference to the Permanent Settlement of 1793, consider the following statements:**

1. The settlement granted Zamindars permanent rights to collect land revenue, but not ownership of the land itself.
2. The settlement was implemented uniformly across all regions of British India, irrespective of local variations in land tenure.
3. The settlement led to the immediate elimination of intermediary landlords between the state and the actual cultivators.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (a) 1 only

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is largely correct. The Permanent Settlement of 1793 granted Zamindars the right to collect land revenue in perpetuity, but crucially, it did *not* grant them absolute ownership of the land.  The land technically remained under the ownership of the British crown, with the Zamindars acting as revenue collectors.  Statement 2 is incorrect. The Permanent Settlement was not implemented uniformly across all regions of British India.  Its application varied considerably depending on local conditions and land tenure systems.  Different systems, such as the Ryotwari system, were implemented in other areas. Statement 3 is incorrect. The Permanent Settlement did *not* eliminate intermediary landlords. In fact, it solidified the position of Zamindars as intermediaries between the state and the actual cultivators, often leading to exploitation of the latter. The other options are designed to test the examinee's understanding of the nuances of the Permanent Settlement and its uneven implementation.  The question emphasizes the importance of understanding the complexities of the land revenue system and its regional variations.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided text, adhering to all specified criteria.  The questions focus on different aspects of British rule in India, particularly revenue policies and social/political strategies.


**1. With reference to the British revenue policies in India, consider the following statements:**

1.  The Ryotwari system, implemented primarily in the Madras Presidency, aimed to collect revenue directly from individual cultivators, bypassing intermediaries like Zamindars.
2.  Under the Permanent Settlement, Zamindars were granted proprietary rights over their lands, leading to a system where the British received a fixed revenue, regardless of fluctuations in agricultural yield.
3. The Mahalwari system, prevalent in parts of North India, involved revenue settlements with village communities or groups of villages, with the village headman responsible for collection.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3
(d) 1 only


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

All three statements accurately reflect aspects of British revenue policies.  The Ryotwari system indeed aimed for direct revenue collection from cultivators, eliminating the Zamindari intermediary.  The Permanent Settlement did grant Zamindars proprietary rights and secured a fixed revenue for the British, regardless of agricultural output variations. This created a system of fixed revenue for the British East India Company, but often at the expense of the peasants.  Finally, the Mahalwari system, as described, focused on village communities or groups as the revenue collection unit, with the village headman playing a key role.  Therefore, option (c) is the correct answer.


**2. With reference to British administrative policies in India post-1857, consider the following statements:**

1.  Following the 1857 Revolt, the British administration actively promoted social reforms to appease the Indian population and foster goodwill.
2. The British sought alliances with conservative elements like Zamindars and princes to counter the growing nationalist movement, viewing them as a counterweight to nationalist-minded intellectuals.
3.  The British policy of "divide and rule" involved exploiting existing religious and caste divisions to weaken the unified opposition to their rule.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 only
(d) 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. Post-1857, the British largely abandoned their previous support for social reforms, fearing that these reforms had contributed to the revolt. They shifted towards supporting conservative elements instead. Statement 2 is correct.  The British actively cultivated relationships with Zamindars and princes, providing them with support and protection in exchange for loyalty. This strategy aimed to counter the growing influence of the nationalist movement. Statement 3 is also correct.  The "divide and rule" policy was a cornerstone of British administration, exploiting pre-existing social and religious divisions to prevent a unified nationalist front.  Thus, only statements 2 and 3 are correct, making (b) the correct option.


**3. With reference to the impact of British rule on Indian society, consider the following statements:**

1.  The British significantly invested in social services like education, sanitation, and public health during the 19th century, leading to significant improvements in these sectors.
2. The condition of factory workers in 19th-century India was characterized by long working hours, low wages, and hazardous working conditions, with initial labour legislation being inadequate.
3.  The British consistently supported the freedom of the Indian press throughout their rule, recognizing its importance in fostering public opinion and political discourse.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) 2 and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. While some progress was made in certain areas, the British significantly underinvested in social services compared to military and administrative expenditures.  Statement 2 is correct. The text clearly highlights the deplorable working conditions in factories, with long hours, low wages, and hazardous environments. Although some labour legislation was enacted, it was largely inadequate to address the widespread exploitation. Statement 3 is incorrect. While the press was initially relatively free, the British imposed restrictions, particularly through the Vernacular Press Act, whenever they felt the press was becoming too critical of their policies or fostering nationalist sentiment.  Therefore, only statement 2 is accurate, making (b) the correct option.


**4. Consider the following statements regarding the British attitude towards various groups in India post-1857:**

1. Educated Indians who advocated for greater Indian participation in administration were viewed by the British with suspicion and hostility.
2. The British consistently maintained a policy of non-interference in the internal affairs of princely states, respecting their sovereignty.
3.  The British actively supported social reformers who challenged traditional practices and advocated for changes in Indian society.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is accurate. The emergence of a middle-class nationalist leadership demanding participation in administration was seen as a direct challenge to British authority.  Statement 2 is incorrect. The British, while initially hesitant to annex more territories, increasingly interfered in the internal affairs of princely states through the doctrine of paramountcy, using them as a tool to maintain their overall control. Statement 3 is also incorrect.  Post-1857, the British largely withdrew support from social reformers, aligning themselves with conservative and orthodox elements in Indian society.  Therefore, only statement 1 is correct, making (a) the correct option.


**5. With reference to the impact of British land revenue policies on Indian agriculture, consider the following statements:**

1. The Permanent Settlement led to increased agricultural productivity and prosperity for the majority of cultivators.
2.  The Ryotwari and Mahalwari systems, while aiming for direct revenue collection, often resulted in overassessment and the impoverishment of cultivators.
3.  The introduction of private property in land, facilitated by British revenue policies, led to increased stability and continuity in traditional village structures.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 2 and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. While the Permanent Settlement aimed to increase productivity, it often resulted in the exploitation of peasants by Zamindars and did not necessarily lead to widespread prosperity.  Statement 2 is correct. Both the Ryotwari and Mahalwari systems, despite the intention of direct revenue collection, frequently led to overassessment of land revenue, pushing cultivators into debt and poverty.  Statement 3 is incorrect. The introduction of private property in land, while intended to incentivize improvements, disrupted traditional village structures and led to increased social and economic inequalities. Consequently, only statement 2 is correct, making (b) the correct option.

**1. With reference to the contributions of Dadabhai Naoroji, consider the following statements:**

1.  He served as the President of the Indian National Congress on three separate occasions.
2.  He founded the East India Association, a platform advocating for Indian self-governance in Britain.
3.  His book, "Poverty and Un-British Rule in India," primarily focused on the positive impacts of British economic policies on India's industrial development.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3


**Correct Answer:** (c) 1 and 2 only

**Explanation:**

Dadabhai Naoroji's legacy is deeply intertwined with the early phase of Indian nationalism.  Statement 1 is correct; he held the presidency of the Indian National Congress thrice, a testament to his leadership and influence within the organization.  Statement 2 is also accurate; he established the East India Association in London, serving as a crucial platform to articulate Indian grievances and advocate for self-rule before the British public and government.  This demonstrates his commitment to raising awareness about India's plight on the international stage.  However, statement 3 is incorrect.  "Poverty and Un-British Rule in India" was a powerful critique of British economic policies. Naoroji's "Drain Theory," a central theme of the book, argued that British rule systematically depleted India's wealth, transferring resources to Britain without adequate return.  The book highlighted the impoverishment of India under British rule, directly contradicting statement 3's assertion of positive impacts.  Therefore, only statements 1 and 2 are correct.  The distractor in statement 3 uses the plausible element of mentioning the book's title to create confusion, implying a positive portrayal of British rule when, in reality, the book was a scathing indictment.


**2. With reference to Sir Syed Ahmad Khan's contributions, consider the following statements:**

1.  He is primarily remembered for his advocacy of separate electorates for Muslims and Hindus in British India.
2.  He significantly contributed to the development of Urdu literature and education.
3.  The Aligarh Movement, which he spearheaded, primarily focused on promoting traditional Islamic scholarship.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (c) 1 and 2 only

**Explanation:**

Sir Syed Ahmad Khan was a complex and influential figure in 19th-century India. Statement 1 is correct; he played a key role in advocating for separate electorates for Muslims, a policy that later had profound and divisive consequences for Indian politics. This reflects his pragmatic approach to navigating the complexities of the colonial context.  Statement 2 is also accurate; he was a prolific writer and intellectual who made significant contributions to Urdu literature and education. He promoted the modernization of Muslim education, bridging the gap between traditional and modern learning. Statement 3, however, misrepresents the Aligarh Movement's objectives. While he sought to improve the educational prospects for Muslims, the Aligarh Movement was not solely focused on traditional Islamic scholarship.  It aimed to create a modern, Western-style education system for Muslims, enabling them to participate more effectively in the broader socio-political landscape. Thus, the movement was about modernization and integration, not a rigid adherence to traditional methods.  The distractor in statement 3 uses the truthful element of the Aligarh Movement to create confusion, associating it solely with traditional scholarship when, in fact, it was a forward-looking initiative.  Only statements 1 and 2 accurately capture key aspects of Sir Syed Ahmad Khan's influence.


**3.  With reference to the Charter Act of 1813, consider the following statements:**

1. The Act significantly increased the East India Company's trade monopoly in India.
2.  It allocated funds for the promotion of education in India, including the study of Oriental languages.
3.  The Act completely abolished the Company's administrative control over India.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (b) 2 only

**Explanation:**

The Charter Act of 1813 marked a turning point in British policy towards India. Statement 1 is incorrect.  While the Company retained its monopoly in certain areas like tea and trade with China, the Act *ended* its general trade monopoly in India, opening it to all British subjects.  This reflects the growing pressure from British manufacturers and free-trade advocates. Statement 2 is correct;  a significant provision of the Act was the allocation of funds for the promotion of education in India, including the study of Oriental languages (Sanskrit, Arabic, and Persian).  This is often seen as an early step towards the development of a modern education system in India. Statement 3 is also incorrect.  The Act did not abolish the Company's administrative control; it retained its governance over India, albeit under stricter parliamentary oversight.  The Company's administrative role would continue until the Government of India Act 1858. The distractors in statements 1 and 3 play on the potential misunderstanding of the Act's nuanced changes to the East India Company's powers, making them seem plausible despite being factually inaccurate. Only statement 2 accurately captures a key aspect of the Act's impact.


**4. With reference to the impact of British land revenue systems in India, consider the following statements:**

1. The Ryotwari system, implemented primarily in the South, resulted in widespread empowerment of village communities.
2. The Permanent Settlement, introduced in Bengal, led to the strengthening of the traditional zamindari system and its positive contribution to agricultural development.
3. The Mahalwari system, prevalent in North India, eliminated the role of intermediaries in revenue collection, leading to direct government-peasant interaction.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 3 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (d) None

**Explanation:**

The British land revenue systems in India had profound and largely negative consequences for the agrarian economy. Statement 1 is incorrect. The Ryotwari system, while aiming for direct revenue collection from peasants, often led to overassessment, exploitation, and the impoverishment of ryots. It did not empower village communities; rather, it weakened them by disrupting traditional structures. Statement 2 is incorrect. The Permanent Settlement, while granting proprietary rights to zamindars, led to the emergence of absentee landlordism, exploitation of tenants, and a lack of investment in agricultural improvement. It did not strengthen the traditional zamindari system in a positive way; instead, it transformed it into a system ripe for exploitation. Statement 3 is incorrect. The Mahalwari system, while aiming for village-level revenue collection, often involved inaccuracies in assessment, corruption, and the rise of intermediaries despite the intention of eliminating them.  It didn't result in direct government-peasant interaction; instead, it often involved multiple layers of intermediaries and exploitation. All three statements present a misleadingly positive portrayal of the British land revenue systems, which is directly contradicted by historical evidence. Therefore, none of the statements are correct.  The distractors in each statement utilize the truthful element of naming the system to create confusion, implying positive outcomes which are actually contrary to their historical effects.

**1. With reference to the impact of the Charter Act of 1813 on India, consider the following statements:**

1. The Act significantly boosted industrialization in India by providing substantial financial support to Indian industries.
2.  The Act completely abolished the East India Company's monopoly over trade with India, opening all trade routes to private British companies.
3. The Act allocated a substantial sum for the education of Indians, marking a crucial step in the westernization of the Indian education system.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 3 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The Charter Act of 1813 is indeed significant for its impact on Indian education.  Statement 3 accurately reflects a key provision of the Act:  it allocated one lakh rupees annually for the education of Indians. This marked a departure from the earlier policy of neglecting Indian education and laid the groundwork for the future expansion of Western-style education in India.  However, this funding was not substantial enough to cause widespread industrialization as suggested in statement 1. The Act did not completely abolish the East India Company's trade monopoly as stated in statement 2. While it did significantly curtail the Company's monopoly, it still retained control over the lucrative tea trade and trade with China. Therefore, only statement 3 is entirely correct. The other statements present plausible but inaccurate information, highlighting potential misconceptions around the Act's impact.  The Act's primary focus on education, rather than direct industrial support, is a critical aspect often overlooked, making this a challenging question for UPSC aspirants.


**2. With reference to Mahatma Gandhi's life and work, consider the following statements:**

1.  Gandhi's first major Satyagraha movement in India was the Ahmedabad Mill Strike of 1918, where he successfully negotiated a significant wage increase for textile workers.
2.  Mahatma Gandhi's  'Hind Swaraj' explicitly advocated for the adoption of English education system as crucial for India's progress and modernization.
3.  Gandhi's association with the newspaper 'Yugantar' played a vital role in disseminating his political views during the early stages of the Indian independence movement.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

All three statements contain inaccuracies. Statement 1 is incorrect because Gandhi's first major Satyagraha campaign in India was the Champaran Satyagraha (1917), not the Ahmedabad Mill Strike (1918). The Ahmedabad Mill Strike was a significant event, but it followed Champaran. Statement 2 is incorrect because Gandhi, in 'Hind Swaraj',  criticized the English education system, arguing it was detrimental to Indian culture and self-reliance. He favored vernacular education.  Statement 3 is incorrect as Gandhi was not associated with the revolutionary newspaper 'Yugantar'. He was associated with publications like 'Indian Opinion', 'Young India', and 'Navjivan'. These inaccuracies make this a difficult question, testing detailed knowledge of Gandhi's life and work and his views on education. The seemingly plausible nature of the incorrect statements makes this a good distractor for a UPSC-level question.


**3. With reference to the Civil Disobedience Movement, consider the following statements:**

1. The Dandi March, a pivotal event in the Civil Disobedience Movement, commenced on April 6, 1930, culminating in Gandhi's defiance of the salt tax at Dandi.
2.  The Gandhi-Irwin Pact of 1931 resulted in the immediate release of all political prisoners, regardless of the nature of their crimes.
3.  The Communal Award of 1932, which introduced separate electorates for various communities, was wholeheartedly accepted by the Indian National Congress.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 3 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

All three statements are incorrect. Statement 1 is wrong because the Dandi March began on March 12, 1930, not April 6th.  While the salt law was broken on April 6th, this was the culmination of the march, not its start. Statement 2 is false because the Gandhi-Irwin Pact did not lead to the release of *all* political prisoners;  it only ensured the release of those not convicted of violence.  The commutation of Bhagat Singh's death sentence was a key demand that remained unmet. Statement 3 is incorrect because the Indian National Congress vehemently opposed the Communal Award, viewing it as a divisive measure that undermined Indian unity.  The Congress's rejection of the Award and Gandhi's subsequent fast leading to the Poona Pact highlight the crucial differences in perspectives. The inaccuracies in all three statements, combined with the significant historical context, make this a challenging question testing detailed knowledge of the movement and its nuances.


**4. With reference to the Round Table Conferences, consider the following statements:**

1. The First Round Table Conference, held in 1930, saw the participation of Mahatma Gandhi as the sole representative of the Indian National Congress.
2. The Second Round Table Conference, held in 1931, concluded with a significant agreement on the establishment of a fully responsible government in India.
3. The Third Round Table Conference, held in 1932, was boycotted by the Indian National Congress due to the failure of the previous conferences to address key Indian demands.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 3 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Only statement 3 is correct.  Statement 1 is incorrect; Gandhi did *not* attend the First Round Table Conference; the Congress boycotted it.  The Congress's participation began with the Second Round Table Conference. Statement 2 is incorrect because the Second Round Table Conference did *not* result in an agreement on a fully responsible government.  The conference ended with disagreements on key issues, particularly minority representation, leading to the Communal Award.  Statement 3 correctly states that the Third Round Table Conference was boycotted by the Congress due to the lack of progress in the previous conferences. The significant historical context of the Round Table Conferences, including the Congress's participation strategy and the ultimate failure to achieve consensus, makes this a suitable question for the UPSC exam. The inclusion of plausible but incorrect details in the other options increases the question's difficulty.


**5. With reference to the East India Company's policies in India, consider the following statements:**

1. The Permanent Settlement, introduced by Lord Cornwallis, granted proprietary rights to the ryots (peasants), significantly improving their economic condition.
2. The Ryotwari System, primarily implemented in the Madras Presidency, involved direct revenue collection from individual cultivators, often leading to overassessment and exploitation.
3. The Mahalwari System, prevalent in parts of North India, assessed land revenue collectively at the village level, promoting village community solidarity and economic stability.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 2 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Only statement 2 is correct. Statement 1 is incorrect: the Permanent Settlement granted proprietary rights to the *zamindars* (landlords), not the ryots. This led to the exploitation of ryots by zamindars, not an improvement in their condition.  Statement 3 is also incorrect: while the Mahalwari System did assess revenue at the village level, it didn't necessarily promote village solidarity or economic stability.  The system often led to disputes and inequities within the village community due to variations in landholdings and productivity.  Therefore, only statement 2 accurately describes a key feature of the Ryotwari System and its consequences.  The incorrect options present plausible but ultimately flawed interpretations of the land revenue systems, making it a challenging question that tests detailed knowledge of colonial land policies and their socio-economic impacts.  The subtle differences between the land revenue systems are crucial for understanding the complexities of British rule.



**6.  With reference to the  impact of British policies on Indian society, consider the following statements:**

1. The British actively promoted social reforms in India, leading to the abolition of Sati and other harmful practices without significant opposition.
2. British policies consistently supported the empowerment of women in India, granting them equal rights and opportunities alongside men.
3.  British efforts to modernize India's infrastructure, such as the construction of railways and canals, primarily benefitted the Indian population and fostered economic development.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

All three statements are incorrect. Statement 1 is inaccurate because while the British did abolish Sati, it wasn't without considerable opposition from conservative elements within Indian society.  The process was complex and involved significant social and political maneuvering. Statement 2 is incorrect: British policies did not consistently support women's empowerment.  While some individual officials or initiatives may have advocated for women's rights, overall British policies did little to address the deep-seated inequalities faced by women in India.  Statement 3 is also inaccurate; the construction of railways and canals, while contributing to infrastructure development, primarily served British economic interests, often at the expense of Indian farmers and laborers.  The railways facilitated the movement of raw materials and goods, enriching British industries, rather than primarily fostering Indian economic development.  The incorrect options represent common misconceptions about British policies, making this a difficult question for UPSC aspirants who need to have a nuanced understanding of the colonial impact on Indian society.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided text, adhering to all specified criteria.  The questions are designed to be challenging and assess a range of cognitive skills, primarily factual recall with elements of analysis and evaluation.  Note that the difficulty level is subjective and may vary depending on the examinee's prior knowledge.

**1. With reference to the Charter Act of 1813, consider the following statements:**

1.  The Act completely abolished the East India Company's monopoly over the Indian spice trade, paving the way for free market competition.
2.  A significant financial allocation was made for the education of Indians, though debates surrounding its implementation ensued.
3.  The Act explicitly transferred the sovereignty of all Indian territories directly to the British Crown, ending the Company's rule.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) None of the above

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. The Charter Act of 1813 did end the Company's monopoly on most Indian trade, but it *preserved* its monopoly on the lucrative tea trade and trade with China.  This partial dismantling of the monopoly reflected the growing influence of laissez-faire economics in Britain and the pressure from British business interests.  The complete opening of the Indian market had to wait for later acts.

Statement 2 is correct.  The Act did allocate a sum of one lakh rupees annually for the education of Indians. However, the implementation of this provision was delayed by significant debate among British officials regarding the approach to Indian education  the Orientalist-Anglicist controversy. This highlights a crucial aspect of British policy: while resources were allocated, the practical application was often hampered by internal disagreements and conflicting priorities.

Statement 3 is incorrect. The Charter Act of 1813 did not transfer sovereignty to the British Crown.  While it acknowledged the Crown's ultimate authority, the Company retained control over territories and revenues for a further period.  The complete transfer of power to the Crown occurred after the Sepoy Mutiny of 1857 with the Government of India Act 1858.  This difference in the timeline demonstrates the gradual shift in power dynamics between the Company and the Crown.



**2. With reference to the impact of British revenue policies on Indian agriculture, consider the following statements:**

1. The Ryotwari system, implemented primarily in the Madras Presidency, ensured equitable land distribution and protected small farmers from exploitation.
2. The Permanent Settlement, introduced in Bengal, aimed to enhance agricultural productivity by granting land ownership rights to Zamindars.
3. The Mahalwari system, prevalent in parts of North India, resulted in efficient revenue collection and prevented widespread peasant indebtedness.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) None of the above

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. The Ryotwari system, while aiming for direct revenue collection from cultivators, often resulted in overassessment and high tax burdens, leading to peasant indebtedness and land alienation.  The system lacked effective mechanisms to protect small farmers, and its implementation was often flawed due to inaccurate land surveys and arbitrary tax estimations.

Statement 2 is incorrect. While the Permanent Settlement granted Zamindars proprietary rights, it didn't automatically lead to enhanced agricultural productivity.  Instead, it often resulted in absentee landlordism, exploitation of tenants (ryots), and neglect of agricultural improvements by the Zamindars who focused primarily on maximizing rent extraction.  The high initial tax rates also left little room for the Zamindars to withstand economic downturns.

Statement 3 is incorrect. The Mahalwari system, while attempting to involve village communities in revenue collection, also suffered from issues of inaccurate assessments, corruption, and high tax demands, ultimately contributing to peasant impoverishment and indebtedness. The system's complexity and the potential for manipulation by revenue officials often undermined its intended efficiency.


**3. With reference to the development of education in British India, consider the following statements:**

1. Lord Macaulay's Minute advocated for the exclusive use of Indian vernacular languages as the medium of instruction in higher education.
2. The Wood's Despatch of 1854 promoted a hierarchical education system with vernacular primary schools at the base and universities at the apex.
3. The Hunter Commission primarily focused on improving higher education and the establishment of new universities across British India.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) None of the above

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. Macaulay's Minute strongly advocated for English as the medium of instruction in higher education, believing that Western knowledge was superior and that English would be the most efficient way to disseminate it.  The promotion of English was a key element of British cultural and political dominance.

Statement 2 is correct. Wood's Despatch indeed laid out a structured educational system, starting with vernacular primary schools, progressing through Anglo-Vernacular high schools, and culminating in affiliated colleges and universities.  This hierarchical structure reflected the British approach to disseminating Western education while accommodating existing vernacular languages at the primary level.

Statement 3 is incorrect. The Hunter Commission primarily focused on primary and secondary education, highlighting their deficiencies and recommending improvements. While it touched upon higher education, its main concern was addressing the widespread neglect of basic education.  The establishment of new universities was a later development, not a primary focus of this commission.


**4. Consider the following statements regarding the Charter Acts:**

1. The Charter Act of 1793 mandated that the East India Company pay a substantial annual sum to the British government from the revenues collected in India.
2. The Charter Act of 1833 ended the East India Company's monopoly over trade with China and in tea, opening these markets to private enterprise.
3. The Charter Act of 1853 introduced a system of competitive examinations for recruitment to the Indian Civil Service, ending the Company's patronage system.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3
(d) 1 only

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

All three statements are correct.  The Charter Act of 1793 significantly increased the British government's financial stake in the Company's Indian operations by requiring an annual payment. The Charter Act of 1833 marked a major shift towards free trade by ending the Company's monopoly over the tea trade and trade with China.  The Charter Act of 1853 is pivotal for its introduction of open competition for the Indian Civil Service, a move that, while slow to impact the reality on the ground, was symbolic of a changing power dynamic and a crucial step towards the eventual Indianization of the service.  The progressive nature of these Acts, in terms of increased governmental control, free market principles, and the introduction of meritocratic principles in the civil service, reflects the evolving socio-economic and political landscape of the time.


These questions aim for a high difficulty level by requiring precise recall of details and nuanced understanding of the historical context.  The distractors are plausible, forcing candidates to carefully evaluate each statement before selecting an answer.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple choice questions based on the provided target content, adhering to all specified criteria.  Each question includes the correct answer and a detailed explanation.


**1. With reference to the early Indian nationalist movement, consider the following statements:**

1.  The "Nehru Report," advocating for dominion status, was authored by Motilal Nehru.
2.  The Non-Cooperation Movement saw significant participation from both Motilal Nehru and Jawaharlal Nehru.
3.  The Deccan Educational Society was primarily associated with Gopal Krishna Gokhale.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 3 only

**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. Motilal Nehru was indeed the primary author of the Nehru Report, a significant document outlining the Congress's demands for constitutional reforms in British India, including the proposal for dominion status.

Statement 2 is also correct.  Both Motilal Nehru, a prominent leader of the Indian National Congress, and his son Jawaharlal Nehru actively participated in the Non-Cooperation Movement, a major phase of the Indian independence struggle led by Mahatma Gandhi.

Statement 3 is incorrect.  While Gokhale was a significant figure in the Indian National Congress and advocated for educational reforms, the Deccan Educational Society's founding is primarily associated with figures like Justice Ranade, not Gokhale.


**2. With reference to the Indian National Congress and its evolution, consider the following statements:**

1.  The Surat Split of 1907 formally divided the Congress into moderate and extremist factions, with Dadabhai Naoroji playing a key mediating role.
2.  The Morley-Minto Reforms of 1909, aimed at placating moderate nationalists, introduced some limited electoral representation.
3.  The cancellation of the Partition of Bengal in 1911 was a direct response to the militant nationalist movement's success in mobilizing mass support.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. While the Surat Split of 1907 did indeed divide the Congress, Dadabhai Naoroji was not a key mediator; he had already played a significant role in the Congress's earlier phases. The split was primarily due to irreconcilable differences between the moderates and extremists regarding strategies and goals.

Statement 2 is correct. The Morley-Minto Reforms of 1909 did introduce limited electoral representation, although it was indirect and favored certain groups like landlords, reflecting the British policy of divide and rule.

Statement 3 is correct. The cancellation of the Partition of Bengal in 1911 was a significant concession by the British government, partly in response to the widespread unrest and mobilization triggered by the militant nationalist movement's Swadeshi and boycott campaigns.


**3. With reference to the figures of the Indian independence movement, consider the following statements:**

1.  Mahatma Gandhi's writings appeared regularly in "Young India," a publication that frequently criticized the Montford Reforms.
2.  Maulana Abul Kalam Azad, known for his views on Indian independence, also founded the Indian Council for Cultural Relations (ICCR).
3.  Jawaharlal Nehru's autobiography vividly describes the impact of Tilak's activities on young Indian nationalists studying abroad.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. Mahatma Gandhi's writings frequently appeared in "Young India," and the publication strongly criticized the Montford Reforms, deeming them inadequate to address India's aspirations for self-rule.

Statement 2 is correct. Maulana Abul Kalam Azad, a prominent figure in the Indian National Congress and a key player in the independence movement, is also credited with founding the Indian Council for Cultural Relations (ICCR).

Statement 3 is correct. Jawaharlal Nehru's autobiography provides detailed insights into the impact of Tilak's political activities and imprisonment on the Indian nationalist sentiment among students in England during the early 20th century.


**4. With reference to the Permanent Settlement in British India, consider the following statements:**

1.  Lord Cornwallis is solely credited with the implementation of the Permanent Settlement, a land revenue policy implemented in Bengal.
2.  The Permanent Settlement aimed to establish a stable and predictable revenue system for the British East India Company.
3.  The Permanent Settlement created a class of powerful zamindars with hereditary rights to land, leading to long-term socio-economic consequences.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. While Lord Cornwallis is largely associated with the implementation of the Permanent Settlement, the policy's genesis involved various individuals and discussions preceding his tenure, and its full implementation involved a complex process over time.

Statement 2 is correct. The Permanent Settlement's primary aim was to create a stable and predictable revenue stream for the British East India Company, ensuring a fixed tax revenue from land.

Statement 3 is correct. The Permanent Settlement did create a class of powerful zamindars with hereditary rights to land, significantly altering the socio-economic landscape, resulting in both positive and negative consequences for various segments of the population, including the peasantry.


**5. With reference to the impact of the Charter Act of 1813, consider the following statements:**

1. The Act significantly increased the amount of money allocated for education in India, marking a turning point in the development of the educational system.
2. The Act completely ended the East India Company's trade monopoly across all sectors, leading to increased competition and economic liberalization.
3. The Act reinforced the British Crown's authority over the East India Company's administration in India.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 and 3 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3

**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The Charter Act of 1813 allocated a substantial sum of money (one lakh rupees annually) for the advancement of education in India, though this was a modest beginning compared to later investments.

Statement 2 is incorrect.  The Act did modify the East India Company's trade monopoly, but it did not end it entirely.  The Company retained control over the tea trade and trade with China.

Statement 3 is correct. The Act further strengthened the British Crown's control and oversight of the East India Company's governance in India, asserting the Crown's ultimate authority.


**6.  With reference to prominent figures of the early 20th-century Indian nationalist movement, consider the following statements:**

1.  Bal Gangadhar Tilak's newspaper, "Kesari," was known for its strong criticism of the British Raj and its policies.
2.  Dayananda Saraswati, a prominent social reformer, significantly contributed to the development of the Indian National Congress's early strategies.
3.  C.R. Das, a leader within the Indian National Congress, played a crucial role in the Non-Cooperation Movement.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 and 3 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3

**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct.  "Kesari," edited by Bal Gangadhar Tilak, was a highly influential Marathi-language newspaper that vehemently criticized British policies and played a vital role in shaping nationalist sentiment.

Statement 2 is incorrect. While Dayananda Saraswati was a significant social reformer, his direct influence on the early strategies of the Indian National Congress was limited. His focus was primarily on religious and social reform through the Arya Samaj.

Statement 3 is correct. C.R. Das was a prominent leader in the Indian National Congress and a significant participant in the Non-Cooperation Movement, though he later diverged from Gandhi's approach.


**7. With reference to the language landscape of India, consider the following statements:**

1.  Bengali, a language with origins tracing back to the 8th century, emerged as a distinct language by the 12th century.
2.  Gujarati, declared a classical language of India, has its roots in Jaina Prakrit works.
3.  Marathi, developed by figures like Eknath and Tukaram, was used as an administrative language in the Bahmani kingdom.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct.  Bengali's historical development shows its origins in Prakrit and Apabhramsha, evolving into a distinct language by the 12th century,  though its roots extend further back.

Statement 2 is correct.  Gujarati, having been officially granted classical language status, has its origins traceable to Jaina Prakrit texts and its development over centuries.

Statement 3 is correct.  Marathi, significantly shaped by literary figures like Eknath and Tukaram, was indeed employed as an administrative language in the Bahmani kingdom, reflecting its regional importance.


**8.  With reference to the impact of British rule on India, consider the following statements:**

1.  The introduction of English education in India was primarily associated with Lord Dalhousie's tenure as Governor-General.
2.  The Ilbert Bill, concerning the jurisdiction of Indian judges over European citizens, sparked significant controversy and highlighted the issue of racial inequality.
3.  The early nationalists in India primarily employed methods of constitutional agitation and peaceful political action to achieve their goals.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. The introduction of English education as a significant policy was more associated with Lord Macaulay's Minute and the subsequent Charter Acts, not solely Lord Dalhousie.  Dalhousie did contribute to educational policy, but the initial push for English education predates his time.

Statement 2 is correct. The Ilbert Bill, proposing changes to the jurisdiction of Indian judges over Europeans, caused great outrage among the British community in India and exposed the deep-seated racial bias.

Statement 3 is correct. The early phase of the Indian nationalist movement (1885-1905) was largely characterized by constitutional methods, petitions, and appeals to the British government for reforms.  This changed later with the rise of extremism.


**9. With reference to the leaders of the Indian independence movement and their contributions, consider the following statements:**

1.  Jawaharlal Nehru's political views were significantly influenced by Mahatma Gandhi, shaping his approach to both domestic and foreign policy.
2.  Subhas Chandra Bose's collaboration with Jawaharlal Nehru was consistent and unwavering throughout their political careers.
3.  Jawaharlal Nehru's role in drafting the Objectives Resolution was instrumental in shaping the Indian Constitution.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 and 3 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3

**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. Mahatma Gandhi's influence on Jawaharlal Nehru was profound, shaping his philosophy of non-violent resistance and his vision for independent India.

Statement 2 is incorrect. While Nehru and Bose collaborated in the early stages of the Congress, their relationship became strained later, with differences in political strategy and leadership leading to a significant rift.

Statement 3 is correct. Jawaharlal Nehru played a pivotal role in drafting the Objectives Resolution, which served as the foundational document for the principles and goals of the Indian Constitution.


**10. With reference to the various phases of the Indian nationalist movement, consider the following statements:**

1.  The Home Rule movement saw significant leadership from both Bal Gangadhar Tilak and Annie Besant, representing a shift towards more assertive political action.
2.  The rise of revolutionary terrorism in Bengal was primarily a response to the failure of constitutional methods and escalating government repression.
3.  The Partition of Bengal directly led to the establishment of the Indian National Congress as a unified pan-Indian organization.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 3 only

**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct.  The Home Rule movement, launched by both Tilak and Besant, marked a significant shift towards more active and assertive political mobilization, moving away from solely constitutional means.

Statement 2 is correct.  The rise of revolutionary terrorism in Bengal, represented by groups like the Anushilan Samiti, was a direct consequence of the perceived failure of constitutional methods and the harsh repressive measures adopted by the British government.

Statement 3 is incorrect. The Indian National Congress was founded *before* the Partition of Bengal, although the Partition did act as a catalyst for increased nationalist activity and unity.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided target content, adhering to all specified criteria.  Each question is designed to be challenging and requires detailed knowledge of the Permanent Settlement, its key figures, and its impact.

**1. With reference to the Permanent Settlement, consider the following statements:**

1.  The initial proposal for the Permanent Settlement was made in 1793, aiming to establish a stable revenue system in Bengal.
2.  While granting proprietary rights to Zamindars, the Permanent Settlement also inadvertently created a class of tenants known as ryots or raiyyats.
3.  The implementation of the Permanent Settlement was solely driven by philanthropic motives to improve the lives of the peasantry.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is partially incorrect. The initial proposal for a system similar to the Permanent Settlement was floated around 1776,  but the actual implementation under Lord Cornwallis happened in 1793. The aim was indeed to create a stable revenue system for the British East India Company in Bengal, but it wasn't solely focused on this goal; other factors like administrative convenience also played a role.

Statement 2 is correct. The Permanent Settlement, while granting land ownership rights to the Zamindars, did not address the rights of the tenant cultivators (ryots or raiyyats) who worked the land.
