3.  He implemented the Permanent Settlement, a major land revenue system.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

All three statements are correct. Lord Cornwallis played a pivotal role in shaping the early British administration in India.

Statement 1 is accurate.  While the Permanent Settlement aimed to stabilize revenue collection, it did inadvertently grant Zamindars considerable power and influence, often leading to exploitation of the peasantry.  The hereditary aspects of the settlement solidified their position within the landowning structure.

Statement 2 is also correct. The Treaty of Seringapatam, signed in 1792, concluded the Third Anglo-Mysore War and significantly expanded British influence in South India. Cornwallis's involvement in the negotiations and the treaty's outcome illustrate his strategic role in consolidating British power.

Statement 3 is correct. The Permanent Settlement, introduced by Cornwallis, was a landmark land revenue system that fixed land revenue demands in perpetuity.  While intended to create stability and predictability for the British, it had significant long-term social and economic consequences, affecting land ownership patterns and the agrarian structure of Bengal and other regions.



**3. With reference to the impact of the Charter Act of 1793, consider the following statements:**

1. The Act led to the establishment of new Maal Adalats to resolve revenue disputes.
2. It significantly increased the legislative powers of the subordinate presidencies of Bombay and Madras.
3. It mandated royal approval for the appointment of key officials like the Governor-General and Governors.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 2 and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statement 3 is correct. The Charter Act of 1793 did indeed introduce a crucial element of increased royal control over the East India Company's administration in India. Mandating royal approval for the appointment of key officials like the Governor-General, Governors, and the Commander-in-Chief, reduced the Company's autonomy and strengthened the British Crown's direct influence.

Statement 1 is incorrect.  The Act actually led to the *disappearance* of Maal Adalats. The separation of revenue administration from judicial functions that the Act introduced rendered these courts obsolete.  This was part of Cornwallis's reforms aimed at creating a more efficient and less corrupt administrative system.

Statement 2 is incorrect. While the Act gave the Governor-General *more* powers and control over the subordinate presidencies, it did not significantly *increase* their legislative powers. The power remained largely centralized under the Governor-General, reflecting the continued dominance of the British administration.


**4. With reference to the individuals involved in the establishment of Hindu College in Calcutta, consider the following statements:**

1.  Raja Ram Mohan Roy was the sole founder of Hindu College.
2.  David Hare played a significant role in its establishment.
3.  Alexander Duff actively opposed the establishment of the college.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) 2 only


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Statement 2 is correct. David Hare was a key figure in the establishment of Hindu College.  He actively promoted the idea of a college that would provide modern education to Hindus in Bengal, working closely with Raja Ram Mohan Roy and Alexander Duff.

Statement 1 is incorrect. While Raja Ram Mohan Roy was a significant supporter and collaborator in the Hindu College's founding, he was not the sole founder.  The college was a collaborative effort involving several individuals, reflecting the growing support for modern education among the educated elite in Bengal.

Statement 3 is incorrect. Alexander Duff, though having different educational philosophies, did not actively oppose the establishment of Hindu College.  His involvement in other educational initiatives reflects a broader context of educational reform and modernization in Bengal. The differences in their approaches to education should not be construed as outright opposition.  


**5. With reference to the early 19th-century educational developments in India, consider the following statements:**

1. The Charter Act of 1813 allocated funds specifically for the promotion of Western education in India.
2. Lord Macaulay's Minute advocated for the exclusive promotion of Indian traditional learning.
3. The establishment of the Sanskrit College at Benaras was primarily driven by missionary zeal.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 1 and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The Charter Act of 1813, while not exclusively focused on Western education, did allocate funds for the "revival and improvement of literature and the encouragement of learned natives of India." This marked a significant shift in the Company's policy, reflecting growing pressure to address educational needs in India.

Statement 2 is incorrect.  Lord Macaulay's Minute (1835) strongly advocated for the promotion of Western literature and science through the English language, effectively prioritizing Western knowledge over traditional Indian learning. His perspective reflected a belief in the superiority of Western education.

Statement 3 is incorrect. The establishment of the Sanskrit College at Benaras in 1791 was primarily driven by the East India Company's administrative needs, aiming to train individuals in Hindu law and philosophy to aid in the legal administration of the company. While missionaries played a role in educational developments, the Sanskrit College's founding was not primarily a missionary endeavor.

**1. With reference to early Indian nationalist newspapers and their publishers, consider the following statements:**

1.  Annie Besant's association with *New India* is notable for its advocacy of Home Rule and its role in shaping the political discourse of the time.
2.  *Young India*, edited by Mahatma Gandhi, primarily focused on promoting Khadi and advocating for non-violent resistance against British rule.
3.  The *Amrit Bazar Patrika*, initially published in Bengali, later transitioned to English to circumvent restrictions imposed on vernacular publications.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. Annie Besant, a prominent Theosophist and later a staunch nationalist, played a significant role in the Indian independence movement.  *New India* served as a powerful platform for her Home Rule movement, advocating for self-governance and challenging British authority through persuasive journalism. Her contributions to the paper significantly influenced the political climate of the time.

Statement 2 is incorrect. While *Young India*, edited by Mahatma Gandhi, did promote Khadi and non-violent resistance,  it covered a wider range of topics than simply Khadi promotion.  It served as a crucial platform for articulating Gandhian philosophy, disseminating his views on satyagraha, and mobilizing public opinion on various social and political issues concerning India's struggle for freedom.  Focusing solely on Khadi and non-violent resistance is an oversimplification of its multifaceted content and impact.

Statement 3 is correct.  The *Amrit Bazar Patrika*, initially published in Bengali, transitioned to English publication to avoid the restrictions imposed by the Vernacular Press Act of 1878. This act specifically targeted vernacular newspapers perceived as critical of the British government. The shift to English allowed the *Amrit Bazar Patrika* to continue its publication and dissemination of nationalist ideas without facing direct censorship under the act. This strategic move highlights the challenges faced by Indian newspapers during the colonial era and their efforts to navigate the restrictive legal environment.


**2. With reference to the impact of the Indian nationalist movement on the press, consider the following statements:**

1.  The Vernacular Press Act of 1878 primarily aimed at suppressing English-language newspapers critical of British policies.
2.  The early nationalist press played a crucial role in shaping public opinion and mobilizing support for the Indian National Congress.
3.  Bal Gangadhar Tilak's imprisonment for sedition was directly related to his criticism of British economic policies in *Kesari*.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. The Vernacular Press Act of 1878 specifically targeted vernacular (Indian language) newspapers, not English-language ones.  The British administration perceived vernacular newspapers as having a greater potential to incite unrest among the wider population who were not fluent in English. The act aimed to control the dissemination of nationalist ideas and criticism of the government among the masses.

Statement 2 is correct. The early nationalist press, including newspapers like *Amrit Bazar Patrika*, *Kesari*, and *Maharatta*, played a vital role in shaping public opinion and mobilizing support for the Indian National Congress. These publications served as platforms for disseminating nationalist ideology, critiquing British policies, and raising awareness about various social and political issues affecting the Indian population. Their influence extended beyond urban areas, reaching rural communities and contributing significantly to the growth of the nationalist movement.

Statement 3 is incorrect. While Tilak's writings in *Kesari* were indeed critical of British policies, his imprisonment was not solely due to economic criticisms.  His arrest and conviction were primarily related to his inflammatory speeches and writings that were perceived by the British as inciting violence and sedition. The government used his writings and speeches, including those related to Shivaji Maharaj, to portray him as a threat to public order and imperial authority.  Attributing his imprisonment solely to economic critique overlooks the broader political context of his actions.


**3. With reference to the evolution of the Indian press and its relationship with the British government, consider the following statements:**

1.  The "Metcalfe Act" of 1835 imposed stricter censorship on the Indian press compared to the pre-existing regulations.
2.  The *Amrit Bazar Patrika* initially published in English, later switched to Bengali to better connect with a wider readership.
3.  The post-1857 period witnessed a significant increase in government control over the Indian press due to concerns about nationalist activities.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 3 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect.  The "Metcalfe Act" of 1835, actually, *eased* restrictions on the press compared to previous regulations. It was considered a landmark step towards press freedom in India.  Prior to this act, stringent licensing and censorship were commonplace.  The Metcalfe Act relaxed these restrictions, leading to a notable expansion of the Indian press.

Statement 2 is incorrect. The *Amrit Bazar Patrika* initially published in Bengali, later switched to *English* to circumvent the restrictions of the Vernacular Press Act. This strategic move was designed to avoid the censorship and potential suppression that targeted vernacular publications perceived as promoting sedition.

Statement 3 is correct.  The post-1857 period witnessed increased government control over the Indian press. The 1857 revolt heightened British anxieties about the potential for unrest and the role of the press in shaping public opinion.  This led to the enactment of several laws aimed at restricting press freedom and controlling the dissemination of information deemed subversive to British rule.  This tighter control was manifested through acts like the Vernacular Press Act and subsequent repressive measures.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided target content, adhering to all specified criteria.  Each question includes the correct answer and a detailed explanation.


**1. With reference to the Dutch presence in India, consider the following statements:**

1. The Dutch East India Company initially established its primary base in Masulipatam, later expanding its operations along the Coromandel Coast.
2.  The Dutch successfully ousted the Portuguese from all their forts on the Malabar Coast, establishing undisputed control over the spice trade in the region.
3.  Dutch colonial interests in India primarily focused on the spice trade, with significant trading partnerships established with Indian traders in Gujarat and Bengal.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is partially correct.  While the Dutch did establish a presence in Masulipatam and expand along the Coromandel Coast,  it wasn't their *initial* primary base.  Their initial focus was more on the Spice Islands (Indonesia) before significantly expanding into India.  The statement oversimplifies their early strategy.

Statement 2 is incorrect.  The Dutch did compete with and challenge the Portuguese, seizing some forts, but they did not completely oust the Portuguese from all their Malabar Coast forts. The Portuguese retained a significant presence in the region.  The Dutch dominance was largely confined to specific areas.

Statement 3 is largely correct.  The Dutch *did* have a primary interest in the spice trade and engaged in trade with Indian merchants in various locations, including Gujarat and Bengal.  However,  limiting their interests solely to the spice trade is an oversimplification; they traded in other commodities as well.


**2. With reference to the economic impact of the Industrial Revolution on India during the first half of the nineteenth century, consider the following statements:**

1. The introduction of machines in the Indian textile industry led to a significant increase in employment opportunities for Indian workers.
2. Heavy duties imposed on the import of British manufactures helped protect Indian handicrafts from foreign competition.
3. The construction of railway lines facilitated the movement of British manufactures into India and the export of raw materials from India.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 3 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. The Industrial Revolution in Britain led to the decline of Indian handicrafts due to competition from cheaper machine-made goods. This resulted in job losses for Indian textile workers, not an increase.

Statement 2 is incorrect.  The opposite occurred.  The British implemented a policy of free trade, allowing British goods to enter India with minimal tariffs, while Indian goods faced high tariffs in British markets. This severely disadvantaged Indian handicrafts.

Statement 3 is correct. The construction of railways greatly facilitated the penetration of British goods into the Indian interior and the efficient export of raw materials to Britain.  This was a crucial element of the British colonial economic policy.


**3. With reference to the activities of the English East India Company in India, consider the following statements:**

1. The Companys staple exports from Bengal in the mid-18th century included raw cotton, oilseeds, and opium.
2. The Company's commercial policy after 1813 was primarily driven by the interests of British industry, aiming to transform India into a supplier of raw materials and a consumer of British manufactures.
3. The Company established its first factory in India during the reign of Akbar, securing favorable trade agreements through diplomatic efforts.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct.  Cotton, silk, saltpetre (potassium nitrate, used in gunpowder), and opium were major exports from Bengal during the mid-18th century. These commodities were crucial for the British economy.

Statement 2 is correct. After the Charter Act of 1813, the Company's trade monopoly ended, but its policy shifted towards making India a supplier of raw materials and a consumer of British manufactured goods.  This is a key aspect of the economic drain.

Statement 3 is incorrect. The Company's first factory in India was established during the reign of Jahangir, not Akbar.  While diplomatic efforts were made with various Mughal emperors,  the chronology is incorrect.


**4. With reference to the economic drain from India during British rule, consider the following statements:**

1.  The "economic drain" primarily refers to the transfer of wealth from India to Britain, with inadequate economic returns for India.
2. Dadabhai Naoroji's theory of economic drain highlighted the outflow of profits from foreign investments in India as a significant component of the drain.
3. The British government's expenditure on infrastructure projects in India, such as railways, completely offset the negative impact of the economic drain.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 2 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The core concept of the "economic drain" is the systematic transfer of wealth from India to Britain, leaving India with insufficient economic benefits in return.  This was a central argument of Indian nationalists.

Statement 2 is correct. Dadabhai Naoroji's analysis included the outflow of profits from foreign investments as a major component of the economic drain. This demonstrates the exploitation inherent in colonial capitalism.

Statement 3 is incorrect. While the British did invest in infrastructure,  the vast majority of the benefits accrued to Britain, and the economic drain significantly outweighed the positive impacts of these investments.  The infrastructure served primarily British economic interests.


**5. Consider the following statements regarding the impact of British rule on Indian agriculture:**

1. The Permanent Settlement system, while aiming to stabilize land revenue, led to increased insecurity for tenants and the rise of absentee landlordism.
2. The commercialization of Indian agriculture primarily benefited the cultivators, leading to increased prosperity in rural areas.
3. The British government invested heavily in improving agricultural productivity and providing support to Indian farmers.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The Permanent Settlement, while intending to fix land revenue, had unintended consequences, including increased insecurity for tenants and the rise of absentee landlordism, which often exploited the peasantry.

Statement 2 is incorrect. Commercialization of agriculture often benefited intermediaries more than the cultivators themselves.  Fluctuations in global market prices often left cultivators vulnerable to indebtedness and hardship.

Statement 3 is incorrect. The British government's investment in agricultural improvement was minimal compared to the revenue extracted from the land.  The focus was on maximizing revenue for the British, not improving the lives of Indian farmers.  This neglect contributed to widespread poverty and famines.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided target content, adhering to all specified criteria.  Each question includes the correct answer and a detailed explanation.


**1. Consider the following statements:**

1.  The English East India Company's initial factory in India was established during the reign of Akbar, primarily focusing on textile trade.
2.  The Portuguese levied a duty on tobacco, showcasing their early economic control over certain commodities in India.
3.  Red chillies were introduced into India during the 17th century, significantly impacting the culinary landscape of the subcontinent.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) 2 and 3 only

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. The English East India Company established its first factory in India during the reign of Jahangir, not Akbar. While Akbar's reign saw significant interaction with the English, the establishment of a formal trading post occurred later.  The initial focus was indeed on textiles, but attributing it solely to Akbar is inaccurate.

Statement 2 is correct. The Portuguese, being early European arrivals in India, established significant economic control in certain regions. Their imposition of a duty on tobacco reflects this economic dominance and their attempt to regulate and profit from the trade of this newly introduced crop.

Statement 3 is incorrect. Red chillies were introduced to India during the 16th century, not the 17th.  Their arrival, likely via Portuguese traders, had a profound and lasting effect on Indian cuisine, but the timeframe is crucial for accuracy.  The 17th century saw the expansion of their cultivation and use, but not their initial introduction.


**2. With reference to the activities of European trading companies in India, consider the following statements:**

1.  The Dutch East India Company's primary trade interest in India was centered around spices, particularly pepper, and they established factories in several key locations including Surat.
2.  The English East India Company, after initial setbacks and conflicts with Mughal authorities, secured significant trading privileges, including exemptions from customs duties in Bengal, under the Mughal emperor Farrukhsiyar.
3. The Portuguese initially established a strong foothold in India, primarily focusing on the spice trade and establishing strategic forts along the Malabar Coast, but their influence gradually declined due to competition from the Dutch and the English.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3
(d) None of the above

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

All three statements are correct and reflect key aspects of the European presence in India.

Statement 1 accurately describes the Dutch East India Company's focus on the spice trade in India and their establishment of trading posts in various locations, including Surat.  Their competition with the Portuguese for control of the spice trade is a significant aspect of early modern Indian history.

Statement 2 correctly notes the English East India Company's initial struggles and later success in securing favorable trading terms from Mughal emperors, particularly Farrukhsiyar's granting of exemptions from customs duties.  This highlights the importance of securing imperial patronage for successful trade operations.

Statement 3 accurately portrays the Portuguese early dominance, their strategic coastal forts, and the subsequent erosion of their power due to the rising power of the Dutch and the English. This illustrates the dynamic nature of colonial competition in India.


**3. With reference to the Mughal Empire's decline and the rise of regional powers, consider the following statements:**

1.  The death of Aurangzeb marked a turning point, leading to a period of instability and wars of succession that significantly weakened the empire's central authority. This was further exacerbated by the rise of ambitious regional leaders.
2.  The Marathas, initially focused on consolidating their power in Maharashtra, gradually expanded their influence across regions like Gujarat, Malwa, and Bundelkhand, posing a significant challenge to Mughal control before their setback at the Third Battle of Panipat.
3.  The Jat kingdom of Bharatpur, under the leadership of Suraj Mal, reached its zenith during the 18th century and controlled a substantial territory, including regions of Agra, Mathura, Meerut, and Aligarh, before facing decline after his death.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3
(d) 2 and 3 only

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

All three statements are accurate depictions of the events leading to the decline of the Mughal Empire and the emergence of regional powers.

Statement 1 accurately highlights the pivotal role of Aurangzeb's death in accelerating the Mughal decline. The subsequent period saw a power vacuum filled by ambitious regional actors, weakening the empire's centralized control.

Statement 2 correctly outlines the Maratha expansion, their initial regional focus, and their subsequent growth into a major power before the Third Battle of Panipat significantly altered the political landscape. This shows the Marathas ambition and their impact on the weakening Mughal Empire.

Statement 3 correctly describes the rise and fall of the Jat kingdom under Suraj Mal, emphasizing his administrative skills and territorial expansion. This illustrates the emergence of a significant regional power.



**4.  With reference to the early establishment of the English East India Company in India, consider the following statements:**

1. The English East India Company initially established factories in Orissa in 1633, demonstrating early interest in the eastern coast of India.
2.  The Company's acquisition of the zamindari rights to three villages  Sutanati, Kalikata, and Govindpur  in 1698, laid the foundation for the future city of Calcutta and provided a secure base for their operations in Bengal.
3.  The Company's early expansion in eastern India was significantly aided by the Mughal emperor Aurangzebs preoccupation with wars against the Marathas, creating opportunities to establish fortified settlements.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3
(d) 1 only

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

All three statements accurately reflect the English East India Company's early activities in India.

Statement 1 is correct, indicating an early presence on the eastern coast. This demonstrates their strategic approach to establishing trading outposts across various parts of the subcontinent.

Statement 2 correctly describes the crucial acquisition of the three villages, forming the basis of Calcutta. This illustrates the transition from mere trading posts to establishing more substantial and secure bases.

Statement 3 is also correct, highlighting the opportunistic nature of the Company's expansion. Aurangzeb's preoccupation with other conflicts provided a window for the English to establish fortified settlements and expand their influence without major confrontation.


**5. With reference to the 18th-century battles in India, consider the following statements:**

1. The Battle of Plassey, fought in 1757, resulted in the British East India Company's decisive victory over Siraj ud-Daulah, significantly altering the political balance of power in Bengal.
2. The Battle of Buxar, fought in 1764, led to the consolidation of the British East India Company's control over Bengal, Bihar, and Orissa, following their victory over the combined forces of Mir Kasim, the Nawab of Awadh, and the Mughal emperor Shah Alam II.
3. The Third Battle of Panipat, fought in 1761, resulted in a decisive victory for the Marathas over Ahmad Shah Abdali, temporarily halting his expansionist ambitions in India.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 2 only
(d) 3 only

**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The Battle of Plassey was a pivotal moment, marking the beginning of significant British dominance in Bengal. The treachery of Mir Jafar and the relatively small scale of the battle compared to its consequences are key aspects to note.

Statement 2 is also correct. The Battle of Buxar solidified British control over a vast region of northern India.  The defeat of the combined forces of Mir Kasim, the Nawab of Awadh, and the Mughal Emperor is a significant historical event.

Statement 3 is incorrect. The Third Battle of Panipat resulted in a decisive victory for Ahmad Shah Abdali over the Marathas, a significant blow to Maratha ambitions and a major turning point in 18th-century Indian politics.  This victory temporarily checked Maratha expansion and weakened them considerably.

**1. With reference to the early European presence in India, consider the following statements:**

1. The Portuguese established their first factory in Surat in 1508, gaining a significant foothold in the lucrative spice trade.
2.  The Dutch East India Company, a formidable competitor to the Portuguese, established a major trading post in Pulicat by 1609, focusing on textiles and spices.
3. The French East India Company, arriving later than the Portuguese and Dutch, initially established a factory in Masulipatnam before expanding to other locations along the Coromandel Coast.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 2 is correct. The Dutch East India Company did indeed establish a significant presence in Pulicat, a strategically important port on the Coromandel Coast, around 1609.  Pulicat provided access to the thriving textile and spice trades, allowing the Dutch to compete effectively with the already established Portuguese.  Their presence in Pulicat was a key element of their broader strategy in India.

Statement 1 is incorrect. While the Portuguese were indeed active in Surat, their earliest factory was not located there.  Their initial focus was on the Malabar Coast, establishing key settlements in places like Cochin and Goa before expanding to other coastal trading centers. Surat became important later in their Indian operations.

Statement 3 is also incorrect. While the French did establish factories along the Coromandel Coast, their earliest factory was not in Masulipatnam.  The English East India Company established its first factory in Masulipatnam. The French initially established factories in other locations such as Surat and then expanded into Masulipatnam. The chronology and locations of the French's early establishments differ from what's presented in the statement.


**2. With reference to the establishment of European factories in India, consider the following statements:**

1. The English East India Company's initial factory in India was established in Surat, primarily focusing on the textile trade.
2. The French established their earliest factory in Cochin, capitalizing on the pre-existing spice trade networks in the region.
3.  The Dutch East India Company, known for its efficient organization and focus on spices, established its first factory in Masulipatnam.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 3 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

All three statements are factually incorrect. The English East India Company's first factory was not in Surat, but rather in Masulipatnam. The French's earliest factory was not in Cochin, but rather in Surat. The Dutch's first factory was not in Masulipatnam but also in Surat. The establishment of European factories in India followed a complex pattern, with various competing companies vying for control of key trading centers. The order of establishment and the initial locations of these factories often differed from commonly held assumptions. The initial focus of each company also varied, depending on their specific commercial interests and strategic goals in the region.


**3. With reference to the Anglo-French rivalry in India, consider the following statements:**

1.  Dupleix, the French governor of Pondicherry, successfully captured Madras in 1746, demonstrating French military prowess.
2. Robert Clive, a key figure in the British East India Company, played a crucial role in the Battle of Plassey in 1757, securing British dominance in Bengal.
3. The Battle of Wandiwash, fought in 1760, resulted in a decisive victory for the French, significantly impacting the power balance in South India.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Only statement 2 is correct. Robert Clive's role in the Battle of Plassey was pivotal in establishing British dominance in Bengal.  This victory had far-reaching consequences, significantly impacting the trajectory of British power in India.

Statement 1 is incorrect. While Dupleix was a significant figure in the Anglo-French rivalry, he did not successfully capture Madras in 1746.  The French *did* briefly occupy Madras in 1746 under Admiral La Bourdonnais, but this was a temporary occupation, not a permanent conquest.  The British regained control.

Statement 3 is incorrect. The Battle of Wandiwash in 1760 resulted in a decisive *British* victory, severely weakening French power in South India.  This battle is often cited as a turning point in the Anglo-French conflict in the region. The statement incorrectly attributes the victory to the French.


**4. With reference to the early activities of the East India Company, consider the following statements:**

1. The East India Company initially operated as a modest trading enterprise, focusing solely on peaceful trade with Indian rulers.
2. The Companys acquisition of Bombay from Portugal in 1668 marked a significant shift towards establishing fortified settlements and asserting greater political control.
3. The Company's early interactions with Indian rulers were characterized by mutual respect and cooperation, with minimal instances of conflict or coercion.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 2 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Only statement 2 is entirely accurate. The acquisition of Bombay represented a strategic shift in the East India Company's approach.  Bombay offered a well-defended harbor and a crucial base for expanding operations, allowing the company to shift its focus from merely trading to establishing a more substantial presence. This marked a transition towards a more assertive and expansionist policy.

Statement 1 is incorrect. While the company began as a trading enterprise, it did not remain solely focused on peaceful trade.  From its early days, the company engaged in various strategies, including forming alliances, engaging in conflict, and gradually expanding its political influence and power.  The narrative of a purely peaceful trading enterprise is an oversimplification.

Statement 3 is incorrect. The Company's interactions with Indian rulers were far from consistently peaceful or cooperative.  The company frequently engaged in political maneuvering, conflicts, and the use of force to secure advantageous trade terms and expand its territorial control.  The narrative of mutual respect and cooperation is a misrepresentation of the historical reality.


**5.  With reference to the Mughal Empire's response to the East India Company, consider the following statements:**

1. Aurangzeb, despite his vast empire, initially underestimated the long-term threat posed by the East India Company, granting them trading concessions.
2.  The Mughal emperors consistently enforced strict control over the East India Company, preventing them from building fortifications or exercising independent political power.
3.  The war between the English and the Mughal Emperor in 1686 ended with a decisive Mughal victory, forcing the Company to abandon its expansionist ambitions.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statements 1 and 3 are largely accurate reflections of the historical record. Aurangzeb, preoccupied with other conflicts, initially underestimated the potential threat of the East India Company. He granted them concessions, seeing them primarily as traders contributing to the state's revenue. The war of 1686 did indeed end in a significant defeat for the English, forcing them to temporarily retreat and adopt a more conciliatory approach.  This demonstrated the Mughal Empire's military superiority at that time.

Statement 2 is incorrect. While Mughal emperors did attempt to regulate the East India Company at times, they did not consistently prevent the Company from building fortifications or exercising influence. The Company's gradual accumulation of power and territory was a process that unfolded over time, involving both periods of cooperation and conflict with the Mughals.  The statement presents an overly simplistic and inaccurate representation of the complex relationship between the Mughals and the Company.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided target content, adhering to all specified criteria.  Each question is designed to be challenging, requiring in-depth knowledge and careful analysis to avoid plausible distractors.


**1. Consider the following statements regarding the Maratha Empire:**

1.  The Maratha expansion significantly contributed to the weakening of the Vijayanagara Empire, ultimately leading to its decline.
2.  Shivaji Maharaj's military strategies, characterized by guerrilla warfare, were crucial in establishing Maratha dominance in the Deccan.
3.  The Marathas consistently maintained a policy of complete independence from the Mughal Empire, rejecting all forms of negotiation or accommodation.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The Maratha conquests in the Deccan significantly weakened the Vijayanagara Empire, contributing to its eventual disintegration.  The Marathas capitalized on the internal conflicts and vulnerabilities of the empire, steadily expanding their influence and control over its territories. This process involved both military campaigns and strategic alliances, ultimately leading to the collapse of Vijayanagara's power structure.

Statement 2 is also correct. Shivaji Maharaj's military genius was instrumental in the rise of the Maratha Empire. He skillfully employed guerrilla warfare tactics, utilizing the terrain and employing swift, decisive attacks to overcome numerically superior opponents.  His innovative strategies, coupled with his charismatic leadership, enabled the Marathas to establish a powerful presence in the Deccan that formed the basis for future expansion.

Statement 3 is incorrect. While the Marathas certainly resisted Mughal rule and fought for their independence, their relationship with the Mughal empire was complex and involved periods of both conflict and negotiation.  Shivaji Maharaj himself engaged in negotiations with Aurangzeb, and the Marathas at various times acknowledged the authority of the Mughal emperor, albeit often reluctantly and temporarily.  The Marathas relationship with the Mughal Empire was characterized by a dynamic interplay of conflict and negotiation.


**2. With reference to the interactions between the Marathas and other powers in medieval India, consider the following statements:**

1.  The Thanjavur Nayakas successfully repelled all Maratha incursions into their territory, maintaining their independence.
2.  The Marathas' control extended to Malwa, significantly impacting the regional political landscape.
3.  Malik Ambar, a prominent figure in the Deccan, employed Maratha soldiers extensively in his army.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. The Thanjavur Nayakas ultimately succumbed to Maratha power, losing their independence to the expanding Maratha empire after a series of conflicts.  While they initially resisted, the Marathas eventually prevailed, incorporating Thanjavur into their dominion.

Statement 2 is correct. The Marathas extended their control over Malwa, a strategically important region, significantly altering the regional power dynamics.  Their presence in Malwa represented a major expansion of their influence beyond the Deccan, bringing it under their administrative and revenue control.

Statement 3 is correct.  Malik Ambar, a powerful figure in the Deccan, recognized the military prowess of the Marathas and strategically integrated them into his army.  He utilized their skills and expertise in warfare to enhance the strength and effectiveness of his own forces, showcasing the Marathas' growing military reputation and importance in the region.



**3. With reference to the early European trading companies in India, consider the following statements:**

1.  The Portuguese were the first to establish a joint-stock company to trade with India.
2.  The Dutch established their trading centers primarily in coastal regions of South India such as Nagapattinam, Cochin, and Machilipatnam.
3.  The French and English East India Companies engaged in intense rivalry, often leading to military conflicts.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 2 and 3 only
(b) 3 only
(c) 1 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect.  The Portuguese did establish a significant presence in India through their early voyages and conquests, but they did not establish a joint-stock company in the same manner as the Dutch, English, and French. Their expansion was driven primarily by the Crown and its military initiatives.

Statement 2 is incorrect. While the Dutch did establish a presence in several locations mentioned, their trading centers were more spread out and encompassed regions in both eastern and western India, including areas like Surat and Chinsura.

Statement 3 is correct. The French and English East India Companies engaged in intense rivalry for control of trade and influence in India, frequently leading to direct military confrontations in various regions.  The Carnatic Wars are a prime example of this competition and illustrate the devastating consequences of their rivalry.


**4. With reference to the East India Company's establishment and early expansion in India, consider the following statements:**

1.  The East India Company initially operated primarily as a trading company, with limited political ambitions.
2.  The Company's acquisition of the zamindari of three villagesSutanuti, Kalikata, and Govindpurmarked the beginning of Calcutta's development as a major city.
3.  The Company's early successes in establishing fortified settlements in Madras and Bombay were primarily due to the Mughal emperor's active support and encouragement of European trade.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 2 only
(d) All three


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct.  The East India Company's primary objective upon its establishment was trade, but their ambitions gradually shifted over time as they sought to consolidate their power and influence in India. Their initial focus was on securing trading rights and establishing profitable trade networks.

Statement 2 is correct. The East India Company's acquisition of the zamindari of Sutanuti, Kalikata, and Govindpur, provided them with a foothold and the foundation upon which the city of Calcutta would grow.  This acquisition marked a crucial step towards establishing a significant territorial base in Bengal.

Statement 3 is incorrect. While the Mughal emperors initially tolerated, and even sometimes benefitted from, European trade, they did not actively support or encourage the establishment of fortified settlements by the East India Company. This was a major point of conflict as the Mughal rulers saw the building of forts as an encroachment on their sovereignty.


**5. With reference to the Subsidiary Alliance system implemented by Lord Wellesley, consider the following statements:**

1.  The Subsidiary Alliance system forced Indian rulers to disband their armies and rely entirely on British military protection.
2.  The Nizam of Hyderabad was the first Indian ruler to sign a Subsidiary Alliance treaty with the British.
3.  The Subsidiary Alliance system ensured the complete economic independence of the Indian states.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. A key element of the Subsidiary Alliance system was the requirement for Indian rulers to disband their own armies and instead rely on the British for military protection. This significantly reduced the military capacity of Indian states and enhanced British power and control.

Statement 2 is correct. The Nizam of Hyderabad was indeed the first ruler to enter into a Subsidiary Alliance with the British, setting a precedent for the system's application to other Indian states.  This treaty marked a significant step in the British consolidation of power.

Statement 3 is incorrect.  The Subsidiary Alliance system did not ensure economic independence for the Indian states. Instead, it often led to increased financial dependence on the British, as the cost of maintaining the British subsidiary force was a substantial burden on the Indian rulers' treasuries.  The system frequently resulted in the cession of territories or other concessions to the British as payment for this protection.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided target content, adhering to all specified criteria.  Each question includes the correct answer and a detailed explanation.


**1. Consider the following statements about the Anglo-Mysore Wars:**

1.  The Treaty of Mangalore concluded the First Anglo-Mysore War, resulting in the restoration of territories to Hyder Ali.
2.  The Second Anglo-Mysore War saw the Nizam of Hyderabad initially allied with Hyder Ali against the British.
3.  Tipu Sultan, during the Third Anglo-Mysore War, decisively defeated the British army at Pollilur, preventing any territorial concessions.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. The Treaty of Mangalore concluded the *Second* Anglo-Mysore War, restoring territories to Hyder Ali. The First Anglo-Mysore War ended with the Treaty of Madras. Statement 2 is correct. The Nizam of Hyderabad was indeed initially allied with Hyder Ali during the Second Anglo-Mysore War, although this alliance was not consistently stable.  Statement 3 is incorrect. While Tipu Sultan did achieve initial victories, including at Pollilur during the Second Anglo-Mysore War, he did not win the Third Anglo-Mysore War decisively. The war concluded with the Treaty of Seringapatam, where Tipu ceded significant territories to the British. The question tests factual recall of the Anglo-Mysore Wars, their timelines, and the key treaties involved, requiring precise knowledge beyond general awareness.  Options (a), (c), and (d) incorporate plausible distractors by mixing up details across different wars and treaties, making them incorrect.


**2. With reference to Tipu Sultan's reign, consider the following statements:**

1.  Tipu Sultan's coinage system spanned across two distinct eras, reflecting his evolving political ideology.
2.  He conquered significant territories in Kerala, expanding his kingdom's reach significantly.
3.  Tipu Sultan's administration was characterized by a complete lack of tolerance towards Hindu religious practices and structures.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. Tipu Sultan's coinage system indeed reflected changes over his reign, showcasing shifts in his political and administrative approaches. Statement 2 is also correct; his conquests extended into Kerala, though the extent of his control varied over time. Statement 3 is incorrect. While his religious policies were complex and not without contradictions,  Tipu Sultan's rule is not accurately characterized by a complete lack of tolerance towards Hindus. He protected some Hindu temples and even funded repairs to some, demonstrating a more nuanced approach than a blanket policy of intolerance. The question assesses factual recall and requires a nuanced understanding of Tipu Sultan's multifaceted reign, challenging simplistic interpretations often found in generalized accounts of his rule. The distractors in the options are designed to test the candidate's ability to differentiate between factual accuracy and common misconceptions.


**3. With reference to the political landscape of 18th-century India, consider the following statements:**

1.  The Jat kingdom under Suraj Mal extended its influence from the Ganga River in the east to the Chambal River in the south, encompassing significant parts of several Mughal subahs.
2.  The Sikh misls, initially twelve in number, consolidated their power in Punjab following the invasions of Nadir Shah and Ahmad Shah Abdali.
3.  The Maratha expansion under the Peshwas was halted decisively by the Third Battle of Panipat, after which they ceased to be a significant political force.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 2 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct.  Suraj Mal's Jat kingdom did reach this considerable extent, showcasing the power of regional entities during the Mughal decline.  Statement 2 is also correct. The Sikh misls did consolidate after the devastating invasions, laying the groundwork for Ranjit Singh's later unification of Punjab. Statement 3 is incorrect.  The Third Battle of Panipat was a major setback for the Marathas, but it did not end their political significance. They continued to be a powerful force, posing a significant challenge to the British East India Company for decades to come. The question assesses factual recall of the rise of regional powers in 18th-century India, testing the candidates ability to differentiate between the extent of power and the impact of specific events. Options (b), (c), and (d) provide plausible distractors by presenting incomplete or inaccurate portrayals of the political dynamics of the period.


**4. With reference to the later Mughal Emperors, consider the following statements:**

1.  Bahadur Shah I, unlike his predecessor Aurangzeb, implemented a policy of religious tolerance, marked by the absence of temple destruction during his reign.
2.  Jahandar Shah's reign was largely characterized by the effective administration of his Wazir, Zulfiqar Khan, who implemented several reforms, including the abolition of the jizya tax.
3.  Farrukhsiyar, despite his own weaknesses, actively resisted the dominance of the Sayyid brothers, maintaining firm control over the Mughal administration.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 2 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. Bahadur Shah I, in contrast to Aurangzeb's stricter policies, adopted a more tolerant approach towards Hindus, characterized by a cessation of temple destruction. Statement 2 is also correct. Zulfiqar Khan, as Wazir during Jahandar Shah's weak reign, played a crucial administrative role, implementing reforms including the abolition of the jizya. Statement 3 is incorrect. Farrukhsiyar lacked the strength to control the powerful Sayyid brothers, who effectively held the real power in the Mughal administration despite his attempts to resist them.  This question tests the candidates knowledge of the internal dynamics of the weakening Mughal Empire, focusing on the reigns of relatively less-known emperors after Aurangzeb. The distractors provided in the options challenge the candidate's understanding of subtle differences in the rulers' approaches and actions.


**5. With reference to the economic conditions in 18th-century India, consider the following statements:**

1.  While agriculture remained technologically backward, the hard work of the peasantry ensured a surplus of agricultural produce, which supported the rest of society.
2.  India's exports significantly exceeded its imports, leading to a substantial inflow of precious metals, making India a sink of precious metals.
3.  The traditional education system, while widespread at the elementary level, lacked the focus on science and technology that characterized Western education systems.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1, 2, and 3
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1 only


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

All three statements are correct. Statement 1 accurately reflects the situation: despite technological backwardness in agriculture, the peasantry's hard work generated a surplus.  Statement 2 is correct; India's trade balance favored exports, resulting in a net inflow of precious metals. Statement 3 is also correct; the traditional education system was indeed widespread at the elementary level but lacked the scientific and technological aspects present in Western systems. The question tests the candidates understanding of the economic and educational realities of 18th-century India, requiring a detailed knowledge of the period.  All options are included to test the candidate's knowledge of the facts and to make the question challenging.  Incorrect options are designed to test the candidate's ability to discern details.


**6. With reference to the social structure of 18th-century India, consider the following statements:**

1.  The Hindu social structure, beyond the four varnas, was characterized by numerous sub-castes, with caste status exhibiting fluidity in certain regions.
2.  Despite Islams emphasis on social equality, Muslim society was also stratified by caste, race, tribe, and status, leading to internal divisions.
3.  The practice of Sati was widespread across India and was uniformly supported by all social and religious groups.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 2 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct.  The Hindu social structure was indeed complex, going beyond the four varnas, with regional variations in caste fluidity. Statement 2 is also correct; while Islam preached equality, social stratification existed within Muslim society based on various factors. Statement 3 is incorrect.  The practice of Sati, while prevalent, was not uniformly supported; there was opposition to it from within various sections of society. This question tests the candidate's understanding of the complex social dynamics of 18th-century India, requiring a nuanced understanding of both Hindu and Muslim social structures. The inclusion of all options ensures that the question is challenging and tests the candidate's knowledge of the facts.


**7.  With reference to the cultural developments in 18th-century India, consider the following statements:**

Statement 3 is incorrect; the 18th century was a period of significant growth in Urdu literature and poetry, with prominent figures like Mir, Sauda, and Nazir. **8. With reference to the decline of the Mughal Empire, consider the following statements:**

1. The death of Aurangzeb, while not immediately causing the empire's collapse, marked the beginning of a period of intense internal conflict and weakening of central authority.
2. The rise of regional powers like the Marathas, Sikhs, and Jats directly contributed to the decline by challenging Mughal authority and carving out independent territories.
3.  Economic problems, including a stagnant economy and the jagirdari crisis, played a minor role in the empire's downfall, overshadowed by military defeats and weak rulers.

(b) 1 only
(c) 2 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3

Statements 1 and 2 are correct. Aurangzeb's death initiated a period of instability and internal strife, weakening central control.  The rise of regional powers actively challenged Mughal dominance and contributed directly to its decline. Statement 3 is incorrect.  Economic problems, including the jagirdari crisis and a generally stagnant economy, were significant factors in the Mughal decline, exacerbating the issues caused by weak rulers and military setbacks.  The question tests the candidates analytical and evaluative skills by requiring them to assess the relative importance of various factors contributing to the Mughal decline. The inclusion of all options tests the candidate's understanding of the nuances of the Mughal decline.


**9. With reference to the  1857 Revolt, consider the following statements:**

1. The Revolt's success was primarily due to the complete absence of Hindu-Muslim cooperation among the rebels and leaders.
2. Bahadur Shah II, though nominally the leader, lacked firm resolve and decisive leadership, which hampered the revolt.
3. The revolt was confined to a few specific regions, with Madras, Bombay, and Bengal remaining largely unaffected despite some sympathy for the rebels.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect.  The 1857 Revolt was significantly strengthened by Hindu-Muslim unity among both the people and leaders.  Statement 2 is correct. Bahadur Shah II's weak leadership and indecisiveness significantly hampered the revolt's effectiveness. Statement 3 is also correct.  While the revolt was widespread, certain regions like Madras, Bombay, and Bengal remained largely unaffected, although pockets of sympathy for the rebels did exist.  This question tests the candidates ability to analyze the causes of the 1857 Revolt's success and failure. Options (a), (c), and (d) present distractors by misrepresenting the level of Hindu-Muslim unity and the geographical scope of the revolt.


**10. With reference to the Portuguese presence in India, consider the following statements:**

1. The Portuguese initially established their first fortress in Goa, securing a crucial foothold on the Indian coast.
2.  The Portuguese maintained a consistently peaceful relationship with all Indian rulers and groups, avoiding any significant conflicts.
3. The Portuguese primarily focused on establishing a large land-based empire in India, rather than concentrating on maritime trade and control.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 3 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The Portuguese established their first significant foothold in India at Cochin, not Goa.  Statement 2 is incorrect. The Portuguese were frequently involved in conflicts with various Indian rulers and groups, vying for control of trade routes and territories. Statement 3 is incorrect. The Portuguese initially focused on establishing maritime dominance and control over crucial trade routes in the Indian Ocean region, rather than building a large land-based empire.  This question tests the candidate's knowledge of the Portuguese in India, challenging common misconceptions about their relations with Indian powers and their strategic goals.  All options are included to make the question challenging and test the candidate's knowledge of the facts.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided target content, adhering to all specified criteria.  Each question includes the correct answer and a detailed explanation.

**1. With reference to the historical evolution of Delhi, consider the following statements:**

1. The Tomars, a Rajput dynasty, preceded the Chauhans in controlling Delhi.
2. The Khalji rulers significantly expanded the architectural landscape of Delhi, introducing the Mughal style.
3. The Painted Grey Ware culture, an early Iron Age archaeological find, is associated with the Kuru tribe's presence in the Delhi region.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 and 3 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3

**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct.  The Tomars were a prominent Rajput clan that held sway over Delhi before the Chauhans.  Historical records indicate a clear succession, with the Tomar rule preceding the Chauhan dynasty's control of the region.

Statement 2 is incorrect. While the Khalji rulers were important in Delhi's history,  attributing the introduction of the Mughal architectural style to them is inaccurate. The Mughal style emerged much later, under the Mughal emperors, significantly influenced by Persian and Central Asian traditions, after the Delhi Sultanate period. The Khalji's architectural contributions were distinct from the later Mughal style.

Statement 3 is correct. Archaeological evidence, specifically the discovery of Painted Grey Ware (PGW), strongly suggests the presence of the Kuru tribe in the Delhi region during the early Iron Age.  The PGW culture is a well-established marker of this period and its location supports the claim of Kuru occupation.


**2. With reference to the political history of Delhi, consider the following statements:**

1.  Bahlul Lodi, the founder of the Lodi dynasty, initially controlled only a small territory around Delhi before expanding his influence.
2.  The Tughlaq dynasty's rule in Delhi saw significant administrative reforms and expansion of the empire's boundaries, including the temporary shift of the capital to Daulatabad.
3.  The Sharqi rulers of Jaunpur consistently attempted to conquer Delhi, posing a significant threat to the established power structures.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3

**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. Bahlul Lodis initial control was indeed limited to the immediate vicinity of Delhi. He gradually consolidated power and expanded the Lodi Sultanate's reach. This gradual expansion is a key aspect of his reign.

Statement 2 is correct. The Tughlaq dynasty, particularly under Muhammad bin Tughlaq, implemented significant administrative reforms and undertook ambitious territorial expansions. The relocation of the capital to Daulatabad, although ultimately unsuccessful, showcases their expansive ambitions and administrative strategies.

Statement 3 is incorrect. While the Sharqi rulers of Jaunpur did challenge the Delhi Sultanate, describing their attempts as "consistent" is an overstatement. Their challenges were intermittent and not a continuous, sustained threat to Delhi's dominance.  The Sultanate's power fluctuated, but Jaunpur's efforts weren't a constant pressure.


**3. With reference to the socio-cultural aspects of Delhi, consider the following statements:**

1.  The Nizamuddin Auliya Dargah, a significant Sufi shrine, reflects Delhi's rich syncretic cultural heritage.
2.  The craft of Phulkari, known for its vibrant embroidery, originated in Delhi and spread to other regions of India.
3.  The Revolt of 1857 had minimal impact on Delhi's socio-political structure, primarily affecting only a small segment of the population.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3

**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The Nizamuddin Auliya Dargah is a testament to Delhi's diverse cultural landscape, blending Sufi traditions with the city's broader historical context.  Its significance as a site of pilgrimage and cultural exchange is well-documented.

Statement 2 is incorrect.  Phulkari embroidery is primarily associated with Punjab, not Delhi.  While Delhi has a rich textile tradition, Phulkari's origins and primary development are firmly rooted in Punjab's cultural heritage.

Statement 3 is incorrect. The Revolt of 1857 profoundly impacted Delhi's socio-political fabric. The revolt was centered in Delhi, leading to significant upheaval, changes in power structures, and lasting consequences for the city's social dynamics.  It had a widespread impact, not just a limited one.


**4.  Consider the following statements regarding the strategic importance of Delhi:**

1. Delhi's location near the Khyber Pass made it vulnerable to invasions from Central Asia throughout history.
2.  The city's proximity to Panipat, a historically significant battlefield, played a crucial role in shaping its political fortunes.
3.  The size of Delhi during the medieval period was comparable to major European capitals like Paris, reflecting its economic and political dominance.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3

**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct.  Delhi's location near the Khyber Pass, a major gateway to the Indian subcontinent, made it a frequent target for invaders from Central Asia. This geographical vulnerability is a recurring theme in Delhi's history.

Statement 2 is correct. The proximity of Delhi to Panipat, the site of several decisive battles, directly influenced the city's political landscape. The outcomes of battles at Panipat profoundly impacted the rulers and the fate of Delhi.

Statement 3 is incorrect.  While Delhi was a major city during the medieval period, a direct comparison of its size to major European capitals like Paris during the same era requires careful qualification.  The methods of measuring urban areas and population varied across different geographical contexts.  Direct comparisons require sophisticated data analysis, which isn't readily available.   Claims of comparable size need strong evidence.


**5. With reference to the early European presence in India, consider the following statements:**

1. The Portuguese established a factory in Bandel, Bengal, demonstrating their early commercial presence in the region.
2. The chronological order of European entry into Indian trade is Portuguese, Dutch, English, and French.
3.  Albuquerque is considered the founder of Portuguese power in India, following Vasco da Gama's initial voyages.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. While the Portuguese did establish a significant presence in Bengal, Bandel was primarily associated with the activities of the Portuguese Jesuits and the establishment of a church there, not a major trading factory.  The Portuguese had a major port at Hooghly, not Bandel.

Statement 2 is correct. The chronological order of the arrival of major European powers in India for trade is accurately reflected in the statement; Portuguese, followed by Dutch, then English and finally the French. This sequence is well-established in historical accounts.

Statement 3 is correct. Although Vasco da Gama's voyages were crucial in initiating Portuguese contact with India, it was Albuquerque who consolidated their power and influence, establishing key bases and consolidating their position on the Indian coast.  His role as the architect of Portuguese power is widely acknowledged.



**6. With reference to the East India Company's operations in India, consider the following statements:**

1. The secret of the East India Company's success was primarily its superior military training and weaponry compared to Indian armies.
2. The English East India Company acquired Bombay from the Dutch in 1668, strategically expanding their presence on the west coast.
3.  Job Charnock is credited with establishing the initial English settlement at Sutanuti, which later developed into Calcutta.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is partially correct but oversimplified. While superior military technology and training were contributing factors to the East India Company's success, it's an oversimplification to say it was the *primary* factor.  Other factors such as the exploitation of internal conflicts in India, superior diplomacy, and economic advantages played equally significant roles.

Statement 2 is incorrect. The East India Company acquired Bombay from the Portuguese, not the Dutch. This acquisition through Charles II, who received it as dowry, proved strategically vital for the Company.

Statement 3 is correct. Job Charnock played a pivotal role in establishing the English presence at Sutanuti, securing a foothold which would eventually develop into the major city of Calcutta.  His negotiations and efforts laid the foundation for this important settlement.


**7. With reference to the Anglo-Afghan relations in the 19th century, consider the following statements:**

1. The Anglo-Afghan wars were primarily driven by British concerns about Russian expansion towards India.
2.  The British East India Companys initial interactions with Afghanistan were largely peaceful and focused on trade.
3. The First Anglo-Afghan War ended with a decisive British victory and the establishment of a stable British protectorate in Afghanistan.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3

**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct.  The primary driver of British involvement in Afghanistan during the 19th century was the strategic concern about the potential expansion of Russian influence into Central Asia and the threat to British interests in India.  This "Great Game" geopolitical rivalry shaped the conflicts.

Statement 2 is incorrect. The British East India Company's interactions with Afghanistan were not initially peaceful.  There were early attempts at establishing influence, but these were quickly followed by conflicts and military interventions.

Statement 3 is incorrect. The First Anglo-Afghan War ended disastrously for the British. The British suffered heavy losses and were ultimately forced to withdraw from Afghanistan. The war did not lead to the establishment of a British protectorate.  It highlighted the difficulties of imperial expansion in the region.


**8. With reference to Maharaja Ranjit Singh and his kingdom, consider the following statements:**

1.  Lahore was the capital of Maharaja Ranjit Singh's kingdom.
2.  Ranjit Singh's kingdom was primarily associated with the Ahluwalia Misl.
3.  The Western Presidency of the East India Company, during its early period, was located in Surat.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 and 3 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3

**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. Lahore served as the capital of Maharaja Ranjit Singh's kingdom, a strategically important location in the Punjab region.

Statement 2 is incorrect. Ranjit Singh's kingdom was associated with the Sukerchakia Misl, not the Ahluwalia Misl.  The Sukerchakia Misl was one of the prominent Sikh confederacies that emerged during the period of decline of the Mughal Empire.

Statement 3 is incorrect. The Western Presidency of the East India Company was based in Bombay, not Surat.  The shift from Surat to Bombay reflected the changing strategic importance of the ports and the growing threat of the Maratha power in the region.  Bombay offered better defenses and access to the sea.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided text, adhering to all specified criteria.  Each question is designed to be challenging and test in-depth knowledge of the subject matter.


**1. With reference to Aurangzeb's reign and its impact, consider the following statements:**

1. Aurangzeb's religious policies, particularly the reimposition of the jizya tax, significantly alienated the Rajput population, turning them from staunch supporters of the Mughal Empire into persistent enemies.
2.  The Deccan policy pursued by Aurangzeb, characterized by prolonged campaigns and resource depletion, proved to be a critical factor in weakening the Mughal Empire's overall strength and contributing to its eventual decline.
3. Aurangzeb's death in 1707 immediately triggered a widespread collapse of Mughal authority across all provinces, leading to the swift establishment of independent successor states.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 2 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. Aurangzeb's religious policies, especially the reintroduction of the jizya tax, significantly strained relations with the Rajputs, a previously loyal group. This alienated a powerful military and political force, weakening the empire's stability.

Statement 2 is also correct. Aurangzeb's prolonged and costly Deccan campaigns drained the empire's resources, both human and financial. This military overstretch and economic depletion significantly weakened the central government, creating vulnerabilities exploited by regional powers.

Statement 3 is incorrect. While Aurangzeb's death did accelerate the decline of the Mughal Empire, the collapse wasn't immediate or widespread. The process of disintegration was gradual, with various regions asserting independence over several decades following his death.  Wars of succession and the incompetence of subsequent rulers further contributed to the empire's fragmentation.


**2. With reference to the successor states that emerged after the decline of the Mughal Empire, consider the following statements:**

1. The independent state of Hyderabad was founded by Saadat Khan, also known as Burhan-ul-Mulk, who initially played a role in the conspiracy against the Sayyid brothers.
2.  Murshid Quli Khan is credited with establishing the independent state of Bengal, transforming it into a prosperous region during his rule.
3. The establishment of the independent principality of Awadh is attributed to Kilich Khan, popularly known as Nizam-ul-Mulk, who defeated Mubariz Khan in the Battle of Shakr-Kheda.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 3 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect.  Saadat Khan (Burhan-ul-Mulk) founded Awadh, not Hyderabad.  Kilich Khan (Nizam-ul-Mulk) founded Hyderabad.

Statement 2 is correct. Murshid Quli Khan is recognized as the founder of the independent state of Bengal, known for his effective administration and the prosperity he brought to the region.

Statement 3 is incorrect. Kilich Khan (Nizam-ul-Mulk) founded Hyderabad after defeating Mubariz Khan. Saadat Khan is associated with Awadh.


**3. With reference to the socio-economic conditions in 18th-century India, consider the following statements:**

1. While agriculture remained technologically backward, it was sustained by the immense labor of peasants, who nevertheless received minimal compensation for their efforts, leading to widespread poverty.
2.  India's trade balance was characterized by a surplus of exports over imports, with significant quantities of cotton textiles, raw silk, and spices being exported to global markets.  Import of silver and gold balanced this trade.
3.  The education system in 18th-century India was highly advanced in science and technology, rivaling the developments in the West, although it lacked in literacy rates.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 2 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct.  The text highlights the stark contrast between the arduous work of peasants and their meager returns, resulting in widespread poverty despite the agricultural sector's importance.

Statement 2 is also correct.  The passage details India's robust export trade, emphasizing the significant volume of textiles, silk, and spices shipped to various global markets. The influx of silver and gold helped balance the trade.

Statement 3 is incorrect. The education system in 18th-century India was traditional and lacked the advancement seen in the West in science and technology. The text explicitly mentions the absence of physical and natural sciences, technology, and geography in the curriculum.


**4. Consider the following statements regarding the evolution of the police system in British India:**

1.  The Indian Police Act of 1861, based on the recommendations of the Police Commission of 1860, established a unified All-India police force with standardized ranks and a hierarchical structure.
2.  Under Cornwallis, a regular police force was organized, modernizing the existing thana system and relieving zamindars of their police duties.
3. The Frazer Commission (1902-03) recommended the creation of a Criminal Investigation Department (CID) at the center and in each province, a crucial step in enhancing investigative capabilities within the police force.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 2 and 3 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. The 1861 Act provided guidelines, not a unified All-India force.  Provincial variations persisted.

Statement 2 is correct. Cornwallis's reforms were a significant step in establishing a more organized police force, removing police responsibilities from the often unreliable zamindars.

Statement 3 is correct. The Frazer Commission's recommendations led to the creation of the CID, a significant development in improving criminal investigation capabilities.


**5. With reference to the British administrative policies in India after 1857, consider the following statements:**

1. The "divide and rule" policy, employed extensively after 1857, involved pitting various groups against each otherprinces versus people, castes against castes, and, notably, Hindus against Muslimsto maintain British control.
2. The British government actively encouraged modern education in India after 1857, viewing it as a tool for preparing Indians for self-governance and participation in administration.
3. Following the 1857 revolt, the British administration consistently showed a favourable attitude towards educated Indians, recognizing their potential contribution to the stability and progress of the country.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct.  The "divide and rule" policy was a cornerstone of British administration after 1857, effectively exploiting existing social and religious divisions to weaken any unified opposition.
