Statement 2 is incorrect. While the British initially encouraged modern education, this attitude shifted after 1857 as educated Indians increasingly challenged British rule. The government became more hostile to higher education as it fostered nationalism.

Statement 3 is incorrect.  The passage clearly states that the favourable attitude towards educated Indians changed after 1857 as they began to organize nationalist movements.  The British became actively hostile to this educated class.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple choice questions based on the provided target content, focusing on Calcutta, Punjab, and related regions.  Each question adheres to the specified format and criteria, aiming for a difficult level.


**1. With reference to the administrative and economic history of Bengal, consider the following statements:**

1. The Permanent Settlement, implemented in Bengal, significantly altered land revenue collection, leading to the rise of a powerful zamindari class.
2. The establishment of the Supreme Court in Calcutta marked a crucial shift in the legal system, impacting both British and Indian subjects.
3. The East India Company's initial presence in Calcutta was characterized by a peaceful co-existence with local authorities, with minimal interference in the existing administrative structures.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The Permanent Settlement, implemented in 1793, drastically changed land revenue collection in Bengal.  It granted zamindars (landlords) hereditary rights to their lands in exchange for fixed annual payments to the British. This created a powerful zamindari class, influencing the socio-economic fabric of Bengal profoundly. The system, while aiming for revenue stability, also led to several unintended negative consequences like exploitation of peasants.

Statement 2 is also correct.  The establishment of the Supreme Court in Calcutta in 1774 represented a significant legal development. It introduced a new legal framework based on English common law, which initially clashed with the existing Indian legal systems.  Its jurisdiction extended to both British subjects and, to a certain extent, Indians, creating a complex interplay between colonial and indigenous law.

Statement 3 is incorrect. The East India Company's early presence in Calcutta was far from peaceful.  The Company's actions, including fortification without permission from the Nawab, directly challenged local authority, leading to conflicts like the Battle of Plassey. The Company's growing commercial and political ambitions led to increasing interference in Bengal's administration.


**2. With reference to the socio-cultural landscape of Calcutta, consider the following statements:**

1. The rise of Bengali theatre, with institutions like the Belgachia and Shobhabazar Natyashalas, significantly contributed to the development of a distinct Bengali cultural identity.
2.  Wood's Despatch, though implemented across British India, had a particularly profound impact on the educational institutions of Calcutta, laying the foundation for a modern education system.
3.  The Kalighat painting style, known for its vivid depictions of Hindu deities and folk themes, emerged as a significant art form in rural Bengal, largely independent of Calcutta's urban influences.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 2 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The emergence of professional Bengali theatre in Calcutta, with prominent institutions like the Belgachia and Shobhabazar Natyashalas, played a major role in shaping Bengali cultural identity. These theatres tackled social issues and promoted Bengali language and literature, contributing significantly to the development of a modern Bengali consciousness.

Statement 2 is also correct. Wood's Despatch of 1854, while a pan-Indian educational policy, significantly influenced the development of educational institutions in Calcutta.  It advocated for a system of modern education based on Western models, resulting in the establishment and expansion of various educational institutions in the city.

Statement 3 is incorrect. While Kalighat paintings did indeed depict Hindu deities and folk themes, they originated in and were closely associated with the urban center of Calcutta, not rural Bengal.  The style developed in close proximity to the Kalighat Kali Temple and reflected the religious and social milieu of the city.


**3. With reference to the political history of Punjab, consider the following statements:**

1.  The Anglo-Sikh Wars resulted in the annexation of Punjab by the British East India Company, ending the Sikh Empire's rule.
2.  The Partition of India significantly impacted Punjab, leading to widespread communal violence and displacement of populations.
3.  Maharaja Ranjit Singhs reign saw the peaceful integration of Jammu, Kashmir, and Multan into his domains, achieved through diplomacy and strategic alliances rather than significant military conflict.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is accurate. The two Anglo-Sikh Wars (1845-46 and 1848-49) ultimately led to the British annexation of Punjab.  The Sikh Empire, weakened by internal conflicts and succession crises, was unable to withstand the British military might, resulting in the end of its independent rule.

Statement 2 is also correct. The Partition of India in 1947 had devastating consequences for Punjab, dividing the region between India and Pakistan.  This resulted in widespread communal violence, mass migrations, and immense human suffering, leaving a lasting impact on the region's social and political landscape.

Statement 3 is incorrect. While Maharaja Ranjit Singh did expand his empire to include Jammu, Kashmir, and Multan, this expansion was not solely achieved through peaceful means. Military campaigns and strategic alliances played a crucial role in his territorial conquests.  The incorporation of these regions involved various levels of conflict and negotiation.


**4. With reference to the diverse aspects of the Punjab region, consider the following statements:**

1. The Bhangra, a vibrant folk dance form, originated in the eastern regions of Punjab, characterized by its energetic movements and rhythmic beats.
2. The "Operation Blue Star" military operation in the Golden Temple, Amritsar, profoundly impacted the Sikh community and had far-reaching political consequences.
3. The Indus Valley Civilization's influence is primarily confined to the southern parts of Punjab, with limited archaeological evidence found in the northern areas.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is largely correct. While the precise origins are debated, the Bhangra dance form is strongly associated with the harvest festival of Baisakhi and is deeply rooted in the Punjabi cultural heritage, particularly in the rural areas of the region. It's characterized by its energetic and celebratory nature.

Statement 2 is correct. Operation Blue Star, a military operation conducted in 1984, had a profound and lasting impact on the Sikh community and the political landscape of India. The event led to increased tensions and political mobilization.

Statement 3 is incorrect. Archaeological evidence of the Indus Valley Civilization has been found across a wide expanse of Punjab, including both northern and southern regions.  The civilization's reach extended significantly throughout the region, indicating a widespread presence.


**5. With reference to the historical trajectories of Bihar and Orissa, consider the following statements:**

1. The Pala dynasty's rule extended its influence significantly over both Bihar and Bengal, leaving a lasting cultural and artistic legacy.
2. The Paika Rebellion in Orissa, although a significant event, had minimal impact on the British East India Company's consolidation of power in the region.
3. The Champaran Satyagraha, led by Mahatma Gandhi, took place in Bihar, marking a pivotal moment in the Indian independence movement.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?


(a) 1 and 3 only
(b) 3 only
(c) 1 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The Pala dynasty, known for its patronage of Buddhism and its significant contributions to art and literature, exercised considerable influence over both Bihar and Bengal. Their rule had a profound impact on the cultural and intellectual landscape of the region.

Statement 2 is incorrect.  The Paika Rebellion (1817) in Orissa, though ultimately suppressed, significantly challenged the British East India Company's authority and reflected the growing discontent against colonial rule. It was a substantial event in the history of resistance against British rule in the region.

Statement 3 is correct. The Champaran Satyagraha (1917), a landmark event in the Indian independence movement, was indeed launched in Bihar.  Gandhi's involvement in this peasant movement against indigo planters marked a turning point in the Indian struggle for freedom.  It showcased the effectiveness of non-violent resistance and highlighted the oppressive conditions faced by the peasants.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided target content, adhering to all specified criteria.  Each question is designed to be challenging and test a range of cognitive skills, primarily factual recall with elements of analysis and evaluation woven in through plausible distractors.

**1. With reference to the historical context of Banaras and its environs, consider the following statements:**

1.  The Pala dynasty's influence extended significantly beyond Banaras, encompassing large swathes of eastern India, including regions now in Bangladesh.
2.  Ramananda, a prominent Bhakti movement figure, established his primary ashram in Vrindavan, not Banaras, though he did have followers in the latter city.
3.  The Mughal emperor Aurangzeb's policies, while impacting Banaras, did not directly result in the city's complete destruction, although his actions significantly weakened the region's political stability.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 2 and 3 only

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is largely correct. While Banaras was an important center within Pala control, their influence undeniably stretched across a vast area including present-day Bangladesh.  This reflects a broader understanding of the Pala empire's geographical extent, beyond a singular focus on Banaras.

Statement 2 is incorrect.  While Ramananda's influence extended to Banaras, his primary association and ashram were in Vrindavan. The question attempts to mislead by focusing on Ramananda's presence in Banaras, while the core fact is his primary location.

Statement 3 is correct. Aurangzeb's policies, while contributing to the overall decline of the Mughal empire and impacting Banaras' stability, didn't lead to the city's complete destruction.  The statement skillfully uses the word "directly" to create doubt, requiring a nuanced understanding of the historical context.  The option includes a plausible distractor by suggesting a complete destruction, which is incorrect.


**2. With reference to the eighteenth-century political landscape of Awadh, consider the following statements:**

1.  The Nawab of Awadh consistently maintained a strong, independent military force throughout the 18th century, resisting British influence until the annexation in 1856.
2.  The Subsidiary Alliance system, while impacting Awadh's sovereignty, initially provided a degree of protection from external threats, albeit at a significant financial cost.
3.  Saadat Khan, the founder of the Awadh dynasty, initially held a high-ranking position within the Mughal court before establishing his independent kingdom.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 only
(d) 3 only

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. The Nawab of Awadh's military was significantly weakened by the Subsidiary Alliance, which resulted in the dismantling of much of their independent military power.  The option plays on the common misconception of continuous resistance until the final annexation.

Statement 2 is correct. The Subsidiary Alliance initially provided a veneer of protection, but this came with a crippling financial burden that ultimately undermined Awadh's economic stability and contributed to its eventual downfall.  The statement correctly highlights the complex nature of the alliance.

Statement 3 is correct. Saadat Khan did indeed hold a prominent position in the Mughal court before establishing his own independent kingdom in Awadh.  This exemplifies the process of regional power consolidation during the decline of the Mughal Empire.  The option uses the word "initially" to mislead the examinee about the entire span of his career.


**3. With reference to the First Anglo-Maratha War and its aftermath, consider the following statements:**

1.  The Treaty of Purandar, preceding the First Anglo-Maratha War, involved the cession of significant territories by the Marathas to the British.
2.  The Convention of Wadgaon, an early phase of the war, witnessed a significant British military defeat and compelled them to renounce territorial gains.
3.  The Treaty of Salbai, which concluded the war, resulted in a decisive victory for the British, significantly expanding their control over the Indian subcontinent.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 2 and 3 only

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. The Treaty of Purandar was associated with Shivaji Maharaj and the Mughals, not the British. This creates a temporal and participant confusion, testing knowledge of specific treaties.

Statement 2 is correct. The Convention of Wadgaon marked a significant British defeat, forcing them to temporarily concede territorial acquisitions. This highlights a crucial turning point in the war, often overlooked in simplified narratives.

Statement 3 is incorrect. The Treaty of Salbai resulted in a stalemate, not a decisive British victory.  The option uses deceptive language by suggesting complete British domination, which is inaccurate.  It tests the examinee's understanding of the outcome of the war.


**4. With reference to the British East India Company's activities in Bengal, consider the following statements:**

1.  Job Charnock's arrival in Sutanuti in 1690 marked the immediate and decisive establishment of Calcutta as the capital of British India.
2.  The French East India Company maintained a significant military presence near Fort William in Calcutta, posing a continuous threat to British interests.
3.  The Battle of Plassey was a pivotal event that decisively established the British East India Company's dominance in Bengal.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. While Charnock's arrival was important, Calcutta's development as a major British center was a gradual process, not instantaneous. This tests knowledge of the timeline and the nuanced development of Calcutta.

Statement 2 is incorrect.  While the French did compete with the British, their military presence near Fort William was not continuous and significant in the long term. The question uses "continuous threat" to create doubt, requiring precise knowledge of the Anglo-French rivalry in Bengal.

Statement 3 is correct. The Battle of Plassey was indeed a watershed moment, marking a significant shift in the balance of power in favor of the British East India Company in Bengal.  This tests the understanding of the significance of the Battle of Plassey within the broader context of British expansion in India.


**5.  With reference to the 18th-century South Indian state of Mysore, consider the following statements:**

1. The Wodeyar dynasty, founders of the Mysore kingdom, maintained uninterrupted rule throughout the 18th century, unaffected by the rise of Hyder Ali and Tipu Sultan.
2.  The Anglo-Mysore Wars primarily involved conflicts between Mysore and the British, with minimal involvement from other regional powers like the Marathas or the Nizam.
3.  The Treaty of Seringapatam, following the Fourth Anglo-Mysore War, resulted in the complete annexation of Mysore by the British East India Company.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) None

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. The rise of Hyder Ali and, later, Tipu Sultan significantly disrupted the Wodeyar dynasty's rule. The question uses "uninterrupted" to create a false impression.

Statement 2 is incorrect. The Anglo-Mysore Wars involved complex alliances and shifting power dynamics, with significant participation from the Marathas and the Nizam at various stages. This tests the knowledge of the broader political context of the wars.

Statement 3 is incorrect. The Treaty of Seringapatam led to the division of Mysore's territories, but not a complete annexation.  The question uses "complete annexation" to mislead the examinee, demanding precise understanding of the treaty's implications.


These questions are designed to be challenging and require in-depth knowledge of the specified historical periods and events.  The distractors are crafted to test the examinee's ability to differentiate between closely related but ultimately incorrect information.

**1. With reference to the Revolt of 1857, consider the following statements:**

1.  The immediate trigger for the revolt was the introduction of the Enfield rifle, whose cartridges were rumored to be greased with animal fat, offending both Hindu and Muslim religious sensibilities.
2.  The revolt was primarily a Sepoy mutiny that failed to gain widespread popular support beyond the military ranks.
3.  Bahadur Shah Zafar, the last Mughal Emperor, was actively involved in leading the revolt and actively sought to restore Mughal authority.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The greased cartridges of the Enfield rifle are widely acknowledged as the immediate trigger of the 1857 revolt.  The rumour that the cartridges were greased with animal fat, offensive to both Hindu and Muslim religious practices, ignited widespread resentment and sparked the initial mutiny among sepoys. This demonstrates the potent role of religious sentiment in fueling the uprising.

Statement 2 is incorrect. While the revolt began as a sepoy mutiny, it rapidly expanded beyond the military.  It gained significant support from diverse sections of Indian society, including peasants, artisans, and various princely states. This broader participation underscores the underlying discontent with British rule that went far beyond just military grievances. The revolt's widespread nature highlights the complex interplay of socio-economic and political factors in addition to the religious trigger.


Statement 3 is correct. Bahadur Shah Zafar, though elderly and not a strong military leader, was proclaimed the symbolic head of the revolt.  His involvement provided a unifying figurehead and a claim of legitimacy to the rebellion against the British East India Company.  While he didn't actively direct military strategies, his symbolic leadership rallied support among various factions, demonstrating the importance of political symbolism during the revolt.  His ultimate deposition and exile marked the end of the Mughal Empire.


**2. With reference to the participants in the Revolt of 1857, consider the following statements:**

1.  Nana Saheb, a prominent Maratha leader, played a crucial role in the siege of Cawnpore.
2.  Rani Lakshmibai of Jhansi actively participated in the revolt, known for her military prowess and fierce resistance.
3.  Tantia Tope, a close associate of Nana Saheb, led several significant military campaigns during the revolt, but his primary contribution was in the logistical support rather than direct combat.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3
(d) 2 and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. Nana Saheb, the adopted son of the last Peshwa, Baji Rao II, played a pivotal role in the revolt, particularly during the siege of Cawnpore. His actions, including the infamous Cawnpore massacre, are a significant part of the revolt's narrative. This highlights the involvement of prominent Maratha leaders in the broader anti-British rebellion.

Statement 2 is correct. Rani Lakshmibai, the queen of Jhansi, was a key figure in the revolt, renowned for her military leadership and courageous resistance against the British. Her defiance and battlefield strategies are legendary, representing the active participation of women in the revolt. Her death in battle cemented her place as an iconic figure of resistance.

Statement 3 is incorrect. While Tantia Tope was indeed a close associate of Nana Saheb and played a crucial role in the revolt, his contribution extended beyond logistical support. He was a highly skilled military strategist and commander, leading several significant military campaigns and battles.  His military leadership, not just logistical support, was vital to the revolt's prolonged duration.  The statement misrepresents the extent of his military involvement.



**3. With reference to the socio-religious reform movements in 19th-century India, consider the following statements:**

1.  The Brahmo Samaj, founded by Raja Ram Mohan Roy, primarily focused on reforming Hindu religious practices and advocating for social justice.
2.  The Arya Samaj, established by Swami Dayanand Saraswati, emphasized a return to Vedic principles and challenged the caste system.
3.  The Self-Respect Movement, spearheaded by E.V. Ramaswamy Naicker, primarily focused on the upliftment of lower castes in South India and rejected Brahminical dominance.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3
(d) 1 and 2 only


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. Raja Ram Mohan Roy's Brahmo Samaj played a crucial role in initiating socio-religious reform in Bengal.  It aimed to purify Hinduism, removing superstitious practices and advocating for monotheism.  The movement also addressed social issues like sati (widow immolation) and promoted widow remarriage.  The Brahmo Samaj's focus on social justice and religious reform was a key feature of its influence.

Statement 2 is correct.  Swami Dayanand Saraswati's Arya Samaj was a significant reform movement.  It advocated a return to the original Vedic principles, rejecting idolatry and caste discrimination.  The Arya Samaj promoted education and social reform, advocating for social equality and religious purity, directly challenging the entrenched caste hierarchy.

Statement 3 is correct. E.V. Ramaswamy Naicker's Self-Respect Movement in South India actively challenged Brahminical dominance and worked for the upliftment of lower castes.  The movement advocated for social justice, self-respect, and equality, rejecting the traditional hierarchical structure of the caste system. The movement's focus on self-respect and rejection of Brahminical hegemony was a defining aspect of its identity.


**4. Consider the following statements about the consequences of the Revolt of 1857:**

1. The British Crown assumed direct control over India, ending the rule of the East India Company.
2. The Government of India Act of 1858 established the office of the Viceroy and transferred legislative authority to the British Parliament.
3. The revolt led to a significant increase in the number of Indian soldiers in the British Indian Army to quell future rebellions more effectively.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 2 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The Revolt of 1857 directly led to the dissolution of the British East India Company's rule in India.  The British government, recognizing the vulnerabilities exposed by the revolt, decided to take direct control over India's administration. This marked a significant shift in power dynamics, transferring authority from a private company to the British Crown.

Statement 2 is correct. The Government of India Act of 1858 was a direct response to the 1857 revolt.  The act established the office of the Viceroy, representing the British Crown in India, and transferred legislative powers from the East India Company to the British Parliament.  This solidified the Crown's direct control over India's governance.


Statement 3 is incorrect. The revolt did not lead to an increase in the number of Indian soldiers in the British Indian Army. In fact, the opposite occurred.  The British significantly restructured the army, reducing the proportion of Indian sepoys and increasing the number of British troops.  This was a deliberate strategy to prevent future mutinies and secure British control.  The statement misrepresents the British response to the revolt's military implications.


**5. With reference to the socio-religious reform movements and their impact, consider the following statements:**

1.  The movement for widow remarriage gained momentum in the 19th century, spearheaded by reformers like Ishwar Chandra Vidyasagar and Jyotirao Phule.
2.  The efforts to abolish Sati were primarily led by male reformers, with limited participation from women's organizations.
3. The Rakhmabai case of 1884 primarily highlighted the issue of women's right to education and the need for reforming marriage laws.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3
(d) 2 and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct.  The widow remarriage movement was a significant aspect of 19th-century socio-religious reform.  Prominent reformers like Ishwar Chandra Vidyasagar and Jyotirao Phule actively championed the cause, challenging traditional social norms and advocating for the rights of widows.  Their efforts contributed significantly to the eventual legalisation of widow remarriage.

Statement 2 is correct. While male reformers played a prominent role in the abolition of Sati, the participation of women's organizations was limited during this period.  The movement was largely driven by male reformers who used religious and social arguments to advocate for the practice's abolition.  The limited involvement of women's groups reflects the societal constraints faced by women in actively participating in public reform movements at that time.

Statement 3 is incorrect.  The Rakhmabai case of 1884, while touching upon women's right to education, primarily revolved around the issue of the age of consent and restitution of conjugal rights within marriage. The case became a landmark legal battle highlighting the complexities of marriage laws and women's rights in the context of patriarchal societal norms.  The statement overemphasizes the role of education in the case.

**1. Consider the following statements about the socio-religious reform movements in 19th-century India:**

1. The Prarthana Samaj, primarily active in Maharashtra, advocated for widow remarriage and challenged the rigidity of the caste system, significantly influencing social reform in South India.
2. The Brahmo Samaj, founded in Bengal, vehemently opposed idolatry and promoted the concept of monotheism, but initially had limited success in penetrating lower castes.
3.  The Arya Samaj, while advocating for Vedic principles, aimed to reform Hinduism by rejecting the concept of untouchability, and actively promoted Vedic education for all castes.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 3 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3
(d) 1 only


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

All three statements accurately reflect aspects of the socio-religious reform movements of 19th-century India.  The Prarthana Samaj, originating in Maharashtra, played a significant role in social reform, advocating for widow remarriage and challenging caste rigidity. Its influence extended to South India through the efforts of reformers like Viresalingam.  The Brahmo Samaj, originating in Bengal, successfully challenged idolatry and promoted monotheism, though its initial penetration of lower castes was limited. The Arya Samaj, founded by Dayananda Saraswati, emphasized a return to Vedic principles while actively opposing untouchability and promoting Vedic education across all castes.  Therefore, all three statements are correct.  Options (a), (b), and (d) are incorrect as they exclude at least one of the accurate statements.  The question tests factual recall and understanding of the distinct yet interconnected nature of these reform movements and their impact on Indian society.


**2. With reference to 19th-century social reform in India, consider the following statements:**

1. Jyotirao Phule and Savitribai Phule, pioneers of social reform in Maharashtra, primarily focused on educating lower castes, particularly girls, and challenged Brahminical dominance.
2.  The Age of Consent Act of 1891, primarily a result of the Rukhmabai case, raised the minimum age of marriage for girls to 12, significantly impacting child marriage practices.
3.  The Hindu Widows' Remarriage Act of 1856, largely due to the efforts of Ishwar Chandra Vidyasagar, legalized widow remarriage across all castes in British India, completely eliminating the social stigma.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3
(d) 2 only


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 correctly identifies Jyotirao and Savitribai Phule's crucial role in social reform in Maharashtra, focusing on education for lower castes and challenging the established social order. Statement 2 is partially correct. The Age of Consent Act of 1891 did raise the minimum age of marriage for girls, but only to 12, not eliminating child marriage entirely.  The act was a landmark achievement, but its impact was limited. Statement 3 is incorrect. The 1856 act legalized widow remarriage, but it did not eliminate the social stigma entirely; many widows still faced significant social ostracization. Therefore, only statements 1 and 2 are partially correct, making option (a) the most appropriate answer. The question tests factual recall and the ability to evaluate the nuances of historical legislation and social reform.



**3. With reference to the Brahmo Samaj, consider the following statements:**

1.  The Brahmo Samaj, initially founded as the Brahmo Sabha, was a reformist movement within Hinduism that emphasized monotheism and rejected the authority of the priestly class.
2.  Debendranath Tagore, succeeding Raja Ram Mohan Roy, led the Brahmo Samaj towards a more theistic and less rationalistic approach, emphasizing devotional practices.
3. Keshab Chandra Sen, known for his progressive social views, led a schism within the Brahmo Samaj, eventually establishing the Sadharan Brahmo Samaj.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 3 only
(b) 1, 2, and 3
(c) 2 only
(d) 1 only


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

All three statements are correct. The Brahmo Samaj did originate as the Brahmo Sabha and championed monotheism while challenging the traditional priestly authority. Debendranath Tagore's leadership did shift the movement towards a more theistic emphasis.  Finally, Keshab Chandra Sen's progressive views led to a division within the Brahmo Samaj, resulting in the formation of the Sadharan Brahmo Samaj. Option (a), (c), and (d) are therefore incorrect, as they omit at least one accurate statement. The question tests the candidate's knowledge of the internal dynamics and evolution of the Brahmo Samaj, demanding factual recall and understanding of its key figures and ideological shifts.


**4. Consider the following statements regarding social reform movements in 19th-century India:**

1. The Self-Respect Movement, primarily active in South India during the 1920s, actively challenged Brahminical dominance and advocated for social justice for non-Brahmins.
2.  Sri Narayana Guru, a prominent figure in Kerala, advocated for a social order that transcended caste distinctions, promoting the idea of "one caste, one religion, one God".
3.  Gopal Hari Deshmukh ("Lokahitawadi"), a key figure in Maharashtra, used rationalist arguments to criticize Hindu orthodoxy and advocate for social and religious equality.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1, 2, and 3
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

All three statements accurately describe significant aspects of 19th-century social reform movements. The Self-Respect Movement in South India directly challenged Brahminical hegemony and championed social justice for non-Brahmins. Sri Narayana Guru's philosophy in Kerala promoted a social order free from caste distinctions, advocating for social equality. Gopal Hari Deshmukh's rationalist critiques of Hindu orthodoxy and his advocacy for social and religious equality in Maharashtra were also influential. Options (a), (c), and (d) are incorrect because they exclude at least one accurate statement. The question assesses factual recall and understanding of diverse social reform movements and their key figures across different regions of India.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided target content, adhering to all specified criteria.  Each question is designed to be challenging and requires detailed knowledge of Indian history and related events.


**1. Consider the following statements regarding the Revolt of 1857:**

1. The immediate trigger for the revolt was the introduction of the Enfield rifle, whose cartridges were rumored to be greased with animal fat.
2.  The revolt was primarily confined to the Bengal Presidency, with minimal impact on other regions of India.
3. Bahadur Shah Zafar, the Mughal Emperor, played a crucial, decisive role in unifying and leading the rebellion.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The greased cartridges were a significant immediate trigger, igniting widespread resentment among sepoys due to religious concerns.  While other long-term socio-economic and political factors contributed to the revolt, the cartridge issue acted as the catalyst for the initial outbreak.

Statement 2 is incorrect.  The Revolt of 1857 was far from being limited to the Bengal Presidency. It spread across significant parts of North and Central India, including key areas like Delhi, Kanpur, Lucknow, and Jhansi, demonstrating its wider reach and broader discontent.

Statement 3 is incorrect.  While Bahadur Shah Zafar was declared the Emperor by the rebels, his role was largely symbolic and nominal.  He lacked the decisiveness and military acumen to effectively unify and lead the diverse rebel forces. The actual command and leadership were dispersed among various regional leaders like Nana Sahib, Rani Lakshmibai, and Kunwar Singh, who had their own agendas and strategies. His age and indecisiveness weakened the rebellion's central command.


**2. With reference to the participants and leadership in the Revolt of 1857, consider the following statements:**

1. Nana Sahib, the adopted son of the last Peshwa, effectively controlled the rebellion in Awadh.
2. Rani Lakshmibai of Jhansi, known for her military prowess, initially hesitated before joining the rebellion.
3. Kunwar Singh, a zamindar from Bihar, played a significant role in coordinating the rebellion across multiple regions.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 2 and 3 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. Nana Sahib led the revolt in Kanpur, not Awadh.  The revolt in Awadh was primarily led by Begum Hazrat Mahal.

Statement 2 is correct. Rani Lakshmibai initially wavered before committing to the rebellion, but once involved, she became a fierce and effective leader. Her participation was influenced by the British annexation of Jhansi and their refusal to recognize her adopted son as heir.

Statement 3 is correct. Kunwar Singh, despite his advanced age, was a highly skilled military leader and strategist in Bihar. His influence extended beyond Bihar, as he collaborated with other rebel leaders.


**3. With reference to the impact and consequences of the Revolt of 1857, consider the following statements:**

1. The revolt significantly strengthened Hindu-Muslim unity, fostering a sense of shared national identity against British rule.
2. The revolt led directly to the immediate abolition of the East India Company and the establishment of the British Raj.
3.  The revolt resulted in widespread support from Indian princely states and Zamindars, significantly bolstering the rebel forces.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The revolt showcased a remarkable degree of Hindu-Muslim unity, especially in the initial stages.  This cooperation among diverse groups was a crucial factor in the rebellion's initial strength and success.  However, it's important to note that this unity was not sustained throughout the entire duration of the revolt.

Statement 2 is correct in its essence, but requires nuance. The revolt did accelerate the demise of the East India Company's rule, leading to its dissolution and the direct assumption of power by the British Crown.  However, it wasn't a direct, immediate consequence. The process involved political maneuvering and deliberations within the British establishment.

Statement 3 is incorrect.  The revolt received limited support from Indian princely states and many Zamindars.  A significant number of them actively aided the British in suppressing the rebellion out of self-interest, fear of British power, or loyalty to the British. This lack of widespread support significantly hampered the rebel's chances of success.


**4. Consider the following statements about the social and religious reform movements in 19th century India:**

1. The Brahmo Samaj, founded by Raja Ram Mohan Roy, primarily focused on advocating for women's education and widow remarriage.
2. The Arya Samaj, founded by Dayananda Saraswati, strongly opposed the authority of the Vedas and challenged traditional Hindu practices.
3. Keshab Chandra Sen, a prominent figure in the Brahmo Samaj, spearheaded campaigns for women's education and challenged the purdah system.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 3 only
(b) 3 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is partially correct. While the Brahmo Samaj did advocate for women's education and widow remarriage, it wasn't its sole focus.  The movement addressed various social and religious reforms, including monotheism and the rejection of idolatry.

Statement 2 is incorrect. The Arya Samaj, in contrast to the statement, strongly upheld the authority of the Vedas as the ultimate source of religious truth.  Dayananda Saraswati's teachings emphasized a return to Vedic principles and challenged practices considered deviations from original Vedic Hinduism.

Statement 3 is correct. Keshab Chandra Sen, a key figure in the Brahmo Samaj's later phase, actively promoted women's education and criticized the purdah system as a symbol of social inequality.  He broadened the scope of the Brahmo Samaj's reform agenda.


**5. With reference to the Revolt of 1857 and its interpretations, consider the following statements:**

1.  L.E.R. Rees interpreted the revolt primarily as a war of national independence, emphasizing its pan-Indian character.
2. T.R. Holmes viewed the revolt through a civilizational lens, contrasting "civilization" (British rule) with "barbarism" (the rebellion).
3. Marxist interpretations of the revolt highlight the role of peasant uprisings and class conflict as driving forces.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 3 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) All three


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. L.E.R. Rees's interpretation leaned towards viewing the revolt as a religious war, highlighting the religious anxieties and motivations among the participants.

Statement 2 is correct. T.R. Holmes's interpretation fits the description, framing the revolt as a clash between British civilization and Indian barbarism, reflecting a colonial perspective.

Statement 3 is correct. Marxist historians have emphasized the socio-economic aspects of the revolt, highlighting the role of peasant uprisings and class struggles in shaping its course and character.  They analyze the revolt as an expression of class conflict within the existing social structure.


These questions aim to test a candidate's in-depth understanding of the provided historical context, demanding precise factual recall and the ability to analyze different interpretations of historical events.  The distractors are carefully crafted to challenge even well-prepared candidates.

**1. With reference to the Servants of India Society, consider the following statements:**

1. The Servants of India Society actively participated in the Indian National Congress's political activities.
2. Gopal Krishna Gokhale founded the Servants of India Society with the primary aim of promoting social reform through selfless service.
3. The Society published a newspaper called "Hitavada" to disseminate its views and advocate for social change.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 2 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The Servants of India Society, founded by Gopal Krishna Gokhale,  remained largely aloof from the direct political activities of the Indian National Congress. While individual members might have held Congress affiliations, the Society itself maintained a distinct focus on social reform through constructive work.  Gokhales vision was to create a cadre of dedicated individuals committed to social service and upliftment of the masses, irrespective of political affiliations.  This is evidenced by the Society's emphasis on education, social reform, and community development.  The newspaper "Hitavada," published by the Society, served as a platform to promote its ideals and advocate for social change, rather than direct political engagement.  Therefore, statements 2 and 3 accurately reflect the Society's activities and objectives. Statement 1 is incorrect as the Society prioritized constructive work over direct political engagement with the Congress.


**2. With reference to Ishwar Chandra Vidyasagar's contributions, consider the following statements:**

1. Vidyasagar's primary focus was religious reform, and he used legislative means to address social issues.
2. Vidyasagar was the principal of the Sanskrit College, which he opened to non-Brahmin students.
3. Vidyasagar played a significant role in the legalisation of widow remarriage in Bengal.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

While Ishwar Chandra Vidyasagar was a significant figure in social reform, his primary focus was not religious reform.  His main contributions lay in the realm of social reform, particularly women's rights and education. He championed women's education and played a pivotal role in the legalisation of widow remarriage, facing significant opposition from orthodox sections of society.  He was indeed the principal of the Sanskrit College, and his significant reform was opening its doors to non-Brahmin students, thereby challenging the rigid caste system and promoting access to education for a wider section of society.  Therefore, statements 2 and 3 are correct.  Statement 1 is incorrect as it misrepresents his focus as religious reform, while his work primarily concerned social issues.


**3. With reference to the social reform movements of 19th and 20th century India, consider the following statements:**

1. The Arya Samaj, headquartered in Bombay, primarily focused on social reform by challenging the caste system and promoting inter-caste marriages.
2. The Prarthana Samaj, a reformist movement in Bombay, advocated for women's education and widow remarriage.
3. The Satyashodhak Samaj, founded by Jyotiba Phule, aimed to uplift the backward classes and challenged Brahminical dominance.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 2 and 3 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

The Arya Samaj was indeed a significant social reform movement, but its headquarters were in Lahore, not Bombay.  The movement's core tenets included a return to Vedic principles, a rejection of idol worship, and a challenge to the caste system. While it promoted social reform, the emphasis on Vedic principles and its origins in Lahore differ from the statement's assertion. The Prarthana Samaj, based in Bombay, was a reformist movement that actively campaigned for women's education and widow remarriage, aligning with statement 2.  Jyotiba Phule's Satyashodhak Samaj was instrumental in advocating for the rights and upliftment of backward classes in Maharashtra, directly opposing Brahminical dominance.  Therefore, statements 2 and 3 are correct. Statement 1 is incorrect due to the misrepresentation of the Arya Samaj's location and primary focus.


**4. With reference to the Eka Movement, consider the following statements:**

1. The Eka Movement, led by Madari Pasi, was primarily focused on religious reform in the United Provinces.
2. This movement ended in 1922 and was largely confined to the Hardoi, Bahraich, and Sitapur districts.
3. The Eka Movement primarily protested against high rents, share-rents, and the oppression of thikadars.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 2 and 3 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

The Eka Movement was a peasant movement, not a religious reform movement.  While Madari Pasi was a key leader, the movement's core was agrarian discontent, not religious reform.  The movement's geographical focus was indeed largely confined to Hardoi, Bahraich, and Sitapur districts of the United Provinces, and its conclusion in 1922 is also accurate.  The primary grievances of the Eka Movement centered around high rents, share-rents, and the exploitative practices of thikadars (intermediary landlords). Therefore, statements 2 and 3 accurately describe the movement's characteristics. Statement 1 is incorrect, mischaracterizing the movement's nature as primarily religious.


**5. With reference to Mahatma Gandhi's activities and beliefs, consider the following statements:**

1. Mahatma Gandhi's advocacy for Swaraj encompassed only political independence and did not address social issues.
2. Gandhi's early political activism began in Champaran, where he addressed the grievances of indigo farmers.
3.  Gandhi actively opposed untouchability but did not support women's emancipation.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 2 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 1 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Gandhi's concept of Swaraj extended beyond mere political independence to encompass social and economic justice. His vision included the eradication of untouchability, promotion of village industries, and empowerment of women. Therefore, statement 1 is incorrect.  His involvement in the Champaran Satyagraha marked the beginning of his significant political activism, where he championed the cause of indigo farmers against exploitative British policies.  Statement 2 is correct.  Gandhi was a staunch opponent of untouchability and actively advocated for the upliftment of Dalits and their integration into society.  Furthermore, he consistently supported women's emancipation, emphasizing their role in society and their rights. Statement 3 is therefore incorrect.  Only statement 2 is accurate.


**6. With reference to B.R. Ambedkars life and work, consider the following statements:**

1. B.R. Ambedkar was the sole architect of the Indian Constitution, working without any assistance from a drafting committee.
2.  Ambedkar primarily focused on the political aspects of Indian nationalism and did not actively oppose the caste system.
3. Ambedkar represented the Depressed Classes at the Third Round Table Conference.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 3 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

B.R. Ambedkar was the chairman of the Drafting Committee of the Constituent Assembly, which played a crucial role in drafting the Indian Constitution.  He worked with a committee of experts, not solely on his own.  Therefore, statement 1 is incorrect. Ambedkar was a fierce critic of the caste system and dedicated his life to fighting against untouchability and social inequalities. His work extended beyond political aspects to encompass social reform and the rights of marginalized communities. Statement 2 is thus incorrect. Ambedkar was a prominent representative of the Depressed Classes at the Third Round Table Conference, advocating for their rights and interests.  Statement 3 is correct. Only statement 3 accurately reflects a key aspect of Ambedkars work.


**7. With reference to the Tana Bhagat Movement, consider the following statements:**

1.  The Tana Bhagat Movement was primarily a religious movement focused on the worship of specific deities.
2. The movement was confined to the state of Jharkhand and did not have any links to the Indian National Congress.
3. The movement's primary grievances were against zamindars, moneylenders, and the begar system (forced labor).


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 3 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3
(d) 2 and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

While the Tana Bhagat Movement had religious elements, its core was agrarian discontent and protest against exploitative social and economic practices. The movement's religious aspects were intertwined with its social and political objectives.  Therefore, statement 1 is partially true but oversimplifies the movement's complexity. The movement's geographical reach primarily encompassed Jharkhand, and while it did not directly affiliate with the Indian National Congress, it shared some ideological overlaps with the Non-Cooperation Movement. Statement 2 is partially correct, but the nuance of its relationship with the Congress is missed. The movement's primary grievances were against the exploitative practices of zamindars, moneylenders, and the begar system. Statement 3 is correct.  Statements 2 and 3 offer a more accurate picture of the movement's character.


**8. With reference to the Chittagong Armoury Raid, consider the following statements:**

1. Surya Sen, the leader of the Chittagong Armoury Raid, was a staunch advocate of non-violent resistance.
2. The raid was primarily aimed at seizing arms to support a larger-scale armed revolution.
3. The raid involved a significant number of women participants who actively participated in combat.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 2 and 3 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Surya Sen, while involved in the Congress, was a key figure in the revolutionary movement and a proponent of armed struggle.  He did not advocate non-violent resistance. Therefore, statement 1 is incorrect. The primary objective of the Chittagong Armoury Raid was to seize arms and ammunition to bolster the revolutionary movement and potentially trigger a wider armed rebellion. Statement 2 is correct. The raid notably involved the participation of several women revolutionaries who played active roles, including combat.  Statement 3 is correct.  Statements 2 and 3 accurately reflect the key aspects of the raid.


**9. With reference to the  Kashmir region, consider the following statements:**

1. The  Treaty of Lahore officially ceded Kashmir to Gulab Singh, marking the beginning of the Dogra rule.
2. The majority of the population in Kashmir was Hindu at the time of Indias independence.
3.  The region's accession to India has been a subject of significant diplomatic dispute with Pakistan.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 and 3 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3
(d) 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

The Treaty of Lahore (1846) indeed ceded Kashmir to Gulab Singh, establishing the Dogra dynasty's rule. Statement 1 is therefore correct. At the time of India's independence, the majority of Kashmir's population was Muslim, not Hindu. This demographic reality is a crucial aspect of the Kashmir dispute. Statement 2 is thus incorrect. The accession of Kashmir to India remains a major point of contention between India and Pakistan, leading to ongoing diplomatic conflicts. Statement 3 is correct.  Statements 1 and 3 accurately capture significant historical and geopolitical aspects of Kashmir.


**10. With reference to the 1857 Revolt, consider the following statements:**

1. The revolt was solely triggered by the sepoys discontent over the introduction of greased cartridges.
2. Economic exploitation and the destruction of India's traditional economic fabric were significant underlying causes.
3. The annexation of Awadh by Lord Dalhousie significantly contributed to the widespread resentment among sepoys and the general population.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 2 and 3 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

While the greased cartridges incident served as a trigger, the 1857 Revolt was a multifaceted event rooted in deeper grievances. The immediate cause was the introduction of the controversial cartridges, but the underlying causes were far more complex.  Therefore, statement 1 is an oversimplification.  Economic exploitation, the destruction of traditional industries, and the British land revenue policies created widespread poverty and resentment among various sections of Indian society. Statement 2 is correct. The annexation of Awadh, with its heavy taxation and displacement of local rulers and officials, fueled widespread discontent and directly impacted the sepoys, many of whom hailed from Awadh. Statement 3 is correct. Statements 2 and 3 accurately reflect the deeper, underlying causes of the revolt.

**1. With reference to the social reform movements in 19th-century India, consider the following statements:**

1. Ishwar Chandra Vidyasagar's primary contribution was the establishment of numerous gurukuls promoting traditional Vedic education.
2. Raja Ram Mohan Roy's efforts primarily focused on advocating for the abolition of Sati and promoting Western scientific education, while largely ignoring other social issues.
3. Mahadev Govind Ranade's work centered on advocating for widow remarriage and opposing child marriage, but he played a minimal role in other social reform movements.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 3 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

All three statements present inaccurate or incomplete portrayals of the contributions of these prominent social reformers.  Statement 1 is incorrect because while Vidyasagar did work with Sanskrit College, his impact extended far beyond establishing gurukuls. He significantly reformed Sanskrit education, making it accessible to non-Brahmins and modernizing the curriculum.  He also championed widow remarriage and women's education, and his contributions to Bengali literature and education were monumental. Statement 2 misrepresents Roy's efforts.  While he was instrumental in abolishing Sati and promoted Western education, his reformist zeal encompassed a broader range of social issues, including monotheism, caste discrimination, and the improvement of women's status.  Statement 3 underestimates Ranade's influence. He was a key figure in various social reform movements, advocating for widow remarriage, women's education, and social justice more broadly. His work extended beyond just these two specific issues.  Therefore, none of the statements accurately reflect the extensive and multifaceted contributions of these social reformers.  The question highlights the need for nuanced understanding of historical figures beyond simplistic characterizations.


**2. With reference to the life and work of Ishwar Chandra Vidyasagar, consider the following statements:**

1. Vidyasagar's primary focus was on religious reform, advocating for the establishment of new sects within Hinduism.
2. He played a crucial role in the legalisation of widow remarriage through direct lobbying of the British Parliament.
3. Vidyasagar's contribution to Bengali literature was primarily through his extensive work in poetry and epic literature.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 3 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. While Vidyasagar was involved in social reform, his primary focus wasn't religious reform in the sense of establishing new sects. His efforts were directed towards reforming existing Hindu social practices. Statement 2 is also incorrect.  Although instrumental in the legalisation of widow remarriage, Vidyasagar didn't directly lobby the British Parliament. His efforts involved social activism, public discourse, and influencing public opinion, which eventually led to legislative change. Statement 3 is incorrect. Vidyasagar's literary contributions were significant, but his impact wasn't primarily through poetry or epic literature. He is more renowned for his contributions to Bengali prose, including the creation of a new Bengali primer that simplified the learning process and helped standardize the language.  His work played a vital role in shaping modern Bengali prose style.  Thus, none of the statements provide an accurate representation of Vidyasagar's multifaceted contributions. The question emphasizes the importance of understanding the nuances of historical figures and their contributions beyond simplistic interpretations.


**3.  With reference to the 1857 Revolt, consider the following statements:**

1.  The revolt was primarily a localized uprising confined to the Gangetic plains, with minimal participation from other regions of India.
2.  Nana Sahib's leadership in Kanpur was characterized by unwavering loyalty to Bahadur Shah Zafar and a strict adherence to non-violent resistance.
3.  The revolt's failure was primarily due to the lack of a unified, centralized leadership structure and the absence of significant support from major Indian princely states.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 3 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. While the Gangetic plains were a major center of the 1857 revolt, the uprising spread to other parts of India, demonstrating a wider participation than a localized event.  Statement 2 is incorrect. Nana Sahib's leadership in Kanpur was not characterized by non-violent resistance.  His actions involved armed rebellion against the British East India Company.  While he initially acknowledged Bahadur Shah Zafar, his primary motivation was asserting his claim to the Peshwaship.  Statement 3 accurately reflects a crucial aspect of the revolt's failure.  The lack of a coordinated leadership and the absence of widespread support from major princely states contributed significantly to the British success in suppressing the rebellion. The diverse nature of the rebellion, with regional variations in causes and leadership, hindered the creation of a unified national movement. The question tests the understanding of the complexities of the 1857 Revolt, highlighting the diverse factors contributing to its outcome.


**4. With reference to the Indian Nationalist Movement (1905-1918), consider the following statements:**

1.  The Swadeshi movement solely focused on economic boycott of British goods, with no significant political dimensions.
2.  The deportation of Lala Lajpat Rai and Ajit Singh in 1907 was directly triggered by their involvement in the Partition of Bengal protests.
3.  Aurobindo Ghoses advocacy for passive resistance was consistently supported by all factions within the Indian National Congress.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 3 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. The Swadeshi movement had significant political dimensions, aiming to challenge British rule beyond just economic boycott. It involved a broader strategy of non-cooperation and resistance. Statement 2 is also incorrect.  Lala Lajpat Rai and Ajit Singhs deportation in 1907 stemmed from their involvement in agrarian unrest in Punjab, not directly from the Partition of Bengal protests. While both events reflected growing nationalist sentiment, they were distinct incidents.  Statement 3 is incorrect. Aurobindo Ghose's advocacy for passive resistance, while influential, did not receive unanimous support within the Congress.  There were significant differences between the moderate and extremist factions regarding the methods and intensity of resistance.  Therefore, none of the statements accurately represent the complexities of the Indian nationalist movement during this period. The question tests the ability to differentiate between related but distinct historical events and understand the nuances of diverse viewpoints within the nationalist movement.


**5.  With reference to the early phases of the Indian National Congress (1885-1905), consider the following statements:**

1.  The early Congress was solely composed of members from the upper castes, with minimal representation from other social groups.
2.  The Ilbert Bill controversy primarily focused on issues related to the economic exploitation of Indian farmers.
3.  Dadabhai Naoroji's primary contribution to the early Congress was his focus on organizing large-scale armed revolts against British rule.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 3 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is an oversimplification. While the early Congress had a disproportionate representation from the upper castes, it wasn't exclusively composed of them.  It gradually expanded its inclusivity over time. Statement 2 is incorrect. The Ilbert Bill controversy centered on the issue of extending the jurisdiction of Indian judges over European British citizens, not on economic exploitation of farmers.  This was a significant issue related to racial discrimination and legal equality. Statement 3 is incorrect. Dadabhai Naoroji was a prominent leader of the early Congress, but his contribution wasn't focused on armed revolts. He was known for his emphasis on constitutional methods, economic analysis of British rule (the "drain of wealth" theory), and his advocacy for self-rule.  Therefore, none of the statements provide a completely accurate portrayal of the early Congress and related events. The question assesses the understanding of the nuances of the early nationalist movement and avoids simplistic generalizations.

**1. With reference to the Revolt of 1857, consider the following statements:**

1.  The immediate trigger for the revolt was the introduction of the Enfield rifle, whose cartridges were greased with animal fat, considered sacrilegious by both Hindu and Muslim sepoys.
2.  The revolt was solely a military mutiny confined to the sepoy regiments of the British East India Company's army, with minimal civilian participation.
3.  Bahadur Shah Zafar, the last Mughal Emperor, initially hesitated to assume leadership of the revolt but eventually became its symbolic head, uniting diverse groups under a common banner.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 3 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a) 1 and 3 only

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The greased cartridges were indeed the immediate trigger, igniting pre-existing discontent among sepoys stemming from various economic, religious, and political grievances.  The perceived sacrilege of using cartridges greased with animal fat (beef and pork) deeply offended both Hindu and Muslim soldiers, acting as the catalyst for open rebellion.  While other factors contributed to the underlying causes of the revolt, the cartridges provided the immediate spark.

Statement 2 is incorrect. The Revolt of 1857 was far more than a simple military mutiny. While it began with sepoy mutinies, it rapidly spread to encompass a wide swathe of northern and central India, involving significant civilian participation from diverse social groups  peasants, artisans, zamindars, and others.  The widespread nature of the revolt, fueled by deep-seated resentment against British rule, clearly demonstrates its broader societal impact beyond just the military.

Statement 3 is correct. Bahadur Shah Zafar, though elderly and initially hesitant, became a crucial symbolic figurehead for the revolt.  His acceptance of the leadership role by the mutineers transformed a primarily military uprising into a movement with a broader political dimension, uniting various factions under the banner of the Mughal Empire  a powerful symbol of Indian political unity at the time. His leadership, however, was largely symbolic due to his age and lack of strong political acumen; the real command often rested with other leaders.


**2. With reference to the leadership of the 1857 Revolt, consider the following statements:**

1.  Rani Lakshmibai of Jhansi, known for her military prowess and unwavering resistance, led the revolt in Awadh.
2.  Nana Saheb, the adopted son of the Peshwa, played a pivotal role in the revolt centered around Kanpur, characterized by both military engagements and brutal massacres.
3.  Kunwar Singh, a zamindar from Bihar, despite his advanced age, proved to be a significant military leader, demonstrating strategic acumen and effective guerrilla warfare tactics.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 2 and 3 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a) 2 and 3 only

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. Rani Lakshmibai of Jhansi was a prominent leader of the revolt, but her primary area of operation was Jhansi and Gwalior, not Awadh (Oudh). The revolt in Awadh was largely led by Begum Hazrat Mahal.  The statement incorrectly attributes Rani Lakshmibai's leadership to a different region.

Statement 2 is correct. Nana Saheb, fueled by his grievances against the British, played a key role in the Kanpur uprising. His actions are characterized by both strategic military operations and, unfortunately, the infamous massacre of British prisoners of war. This illustrates the complex and often brutal nature of the conflict.

Statement 3 is correct. Kunwar Singh, despite his age, was a highly effective military leader in Bihar. His strategic skills and effective use of guerrilla warfare tactics made him a formidable opponent for the British forces.  His defiance in the face of overwhelming odds highlights the determination of various regional leaders in the revolt.


**3. With reference to the causes of the 1857 Revolt, consider the following statements:**

1.  The British policy of annexation, including the Doctrine of Lapse, led to widespread resentment among Indian rulers and fueled the flames of rebellion.
2.  The economic policies of the British, such as the destruction of Indian handicrafts and the imposition of high tariffs on Indian goods, had minimal impact on the overall discontent.
3.  The religious sensitivities of Indian soldiers were completely disregarded by the British, leading to widespread mutinies in the army, which were the sole cause of the revolt.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a) 1 only

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The British policy of annexation, particularly the Doctrine of Lapse, which involved annexing princely states lacking a direct male heir, created widespread resentment among Indian rulers. This fueled existing discontent and contributed significantly to the outbreak of the revolt. The loss of sovereignty and territories was a major political grievance.

Statement 2 is incorrect. The British economic policies had a profound and devastating impact on the Indian economy. The destruction of Indian handicrafts through unfair competition from British manufactured goods and the imposition of discriminatory tariffs severely crippled Indian industries, leading to widespread poverty and unemployment. This economic hardship significantly contributed to the overall discontent that fueled the revolt.

Statement 3 is incorrect. While the greased cartridges and the disregard for religious sensitivities of Indian soldiers acted as a major trigger, the revolt was not solely caused by military grievances.  The revolt was a complex event rooted in a multitude of factors, including political, economic, social, and religious grievances across various sections of Indian society.  The statement oversimplifies the causes and presents an inaccurate picture of the event's complexity.


**4. Consider the following statements regarding the aftermath of the 1857 Revolt:**

1.  The British Crown directly assumed control of India, ending the rule of the East India Company.
2.  The British implemented policies aimed at strengthening their military presence in India, including reducing the number of Indian soldiers in their army and increasing the number of European soldiers.
3.  The revolt resulted in a significant increase in socio-religious reforms implemented by the British in India, demonstrating a greater respect for Indian customs and traditions.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a) 1 and 2 only

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct.  The Government of India Act 1858 transferred the administration of India from the East India Company to the British Crown. This marked a significant shift in the governance structure of British India.

Statement 2 is correct.  The British government implemented several measures to strengthen its military control after the revolt.  This included a significant reduction in the number of Indian soldiers in the army, a substantial increase in the number of British troops, and the adoption of a "divide and rule" policy to prevent future uprisings.

Statement 3 is incorrect. The aftermath of the revolt did not lead to a significant increase in socio-religious reforms.  Instead, the British adopted a more conservative approach, often prioritizing maintaining control over implementing further reforms that might upset the existing social order.  The revolt, in fact, led to a period of reduced reformist zeal among the British.


**5.  With reference to the interpretations of the 1857 Revolt, consider the following statements:**

1.  R.C. Majumdar characterized the revolt as neither the "first," nor "national," nor a "war of independence," highlighting its limited geographical scope and lack of widespread participation.
2.  V.D. Savarkar portrayed the revolt as the "first war of Indian independence," emphasizing its nationalist aspirations and the struggle for self-rule.
3.  Contemporary British historians uniformly viewed the revolt as a purely military mutiny with no significant political or nationalistic implications.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a) 1 and 2 only

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. R.C. Majumdar, a prominent Indian historian, offered a more nuanced interpretation of the 1857 Revolt. He challenged the simplistic narrative of it being a unified national struggle for independence, emphasizing its regional variations, limited geographic spread, and the lack of a cohesive national identity at that time. His perspective highlights the complexities of interpreting historical events.

Statement 2 is correct. V.D. Savarkar, a prominent nationalist and revolutionary, presented a strongly nationalist interpretation of the revolt, portraying it as the first war of Indian independence. This interpretation, while influential in shaping nationalist sentiment, is considered by some historians to be an oversimplification of the event's complexities.

Statement 3 is incorrect. While some British historians did initially portray the revolt as a simple sepoy mutiny, this view was not uniform.  Other British historians acknowledged the broader participation and the underlying social and political grievances that fueled the rebellion, offering a more complex interpretation.  The statement presents an oversimplified and inaccurate representation of the diverse British historical interpretations.

**1. With reference to the Bardoli Satyagraha, consider the following statements:**

1. The Bardoli Satyagraha primarily focused on protesting against the unjust imposition of a new land revenue tax by the British.
2.  K.M. Munshi played a significant role in organizing and supporting the Bardoli Satyagraha, alongside Sardar Vallabhbhai Patel.
3. The Bardoli Satyagraha witnessed significant participation from women, who played a crucial role in its success.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3
(d) 3 only

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The Bardoli Satyagraha was a pivotal moment in India's struggle for independence, primarily focused on resisting a substantial increase in land revenue imposed by the British government in the Bardoli taluka of Gujarat.  This unjust tax heavily burdened the already struggling peasantry, prompting widespread discontent and leading to the launch of the Satyagraha.

Statement 2 is also correct. While Sardar Vallabhbhai Patel is widely recognized as the leader of the Bardoli Satyagraha, K.M. Munshi played a crucial supporting role.  Munshi, a prominent lawyer and nationalist, provided invaluable legal and organizational support to the movement, strengthening its strategic planning and execution. His contributions were vital to the Satyagraha's success.

Statement 3 is accurate. The Bardoli Satyagraha is notable for the significant participation and active role played by women. They actively participated in boycotts, protests, and other forms of civil disobedience, demonstrating their commitment to the cause and contributing significantly to the movement's effectiveness. Their involvement highlighted the broader societal impact of the struggle and challenged traditional gender roles within the movement.


**2. With reference to the Santhal Revolt, consider the following statements:**

1. The Santhal Revolt, primarily led by Sidhu and Kanhu Murmu, was a major rebellion against the oppressive policies of the British East India Company in the mid-19th century.
2. The revolt's primary cause was the British government's failure to address the Santhals' grievances related to land alienation and exploitation by moneylenders.
3. The Santhal Pargana region was established as an administrative unit primarily as a direct consequence of the Santhal Revolt and the need to manage the aftermath of the rebellion.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3
(d) 1 only

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The Santhal Revolt, a significant tribal uprising in 1855-56, was indeed spearheaded by brothers Sidhu and Kanhu Murmu, along with other prominent tribal leaders.  The revolt targeted the British East India Company's policies that led to the displacement and oppression of the Santhal people.


Statement 2 is accurate. The Santhal Revolt stemmed from deep-seated grievances against the British administration.  The Santhals faced widespread land alienation, exploitation by moneylenders, and the erosion of their traditional way of life due to British policies. These factors fueled the revolt and became its core motivations.

Statement 3 is correct. Following the Santhal Revolt, the British government recognized the need for a more effective administrative structure in the region inhabited by the Santhals. This led to the creation of the Santhal Pargana as a separate administrative unit, aimed at addressing the underlying issues that caused the rebellion and managing the region more effectively.  This administrative reorganization was a direct consequence of the revolt and its impact.


**3. With reference to Swami Vivekananda's contributions, consider the following statements:**

1.  Swami Vivekananda's address at the 1893 World Parliament of Religions in Chicago significantly popularized Vedanta philosophy globally.
2.  Swami Vivekananda was a staunch advocate for social reform within Hinduism, actively promoting the upliftment of marginalized communities.
3.  Swami Vivekananda founded the Ramakrishna Mission, an organization dedicated to spreading his philosophy and undertaking social service initiatives.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3
(d) 2 and 3 only

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is accurate. Swami Vivekananda's impactful speech at the 1893 World Parliament of Religions in Chicago marked a turning point in the global perception of Hinduism and Vedanta philosophy.  His eloquent articulation of the core tenets of Vedanta, combined with his charismatic personality, resonated with a wide audience, leading to increased interest and study of Vedanta in the West.

Statement 2 is correct.  Swami Vivekananda was a strong proponent of social reform within Hinduism.  He emphasized the importance of uplifting marginalized communities and advocated for social justice, challenging traditional caste hierarchies and promoting the dignity of all individuals.  His work extended beyond philosophical discourse to actively address social inequalities.
