Statement 3 is also correct. Swami Vivekananda, a prominent disciple of Ramakrishna Paramahamsa, established the Ramakrishna Mission. This organization plays a vital role in propagating his philosophy and engaging in various social service activities across the globe.  The mission continues to be a significant institution, reflecting Vivekananda's commitment to both spiritual and social progress.


**4. With reference to the Brahmo Samaj, consider the following statements:**

1. Raja Ram Mohan Roy is widely credited with establishing the Brahmo Samaj, a key social and religious reform movement within Hinduism.
2. The Brahmo Samaj advocated for the abolition of Sati, promoted widow remarriage, and worked towards women's education.
3.  The Brahmo Samaj, while advocating social reforms, remained largely confined to Bengal and did not spread significantly to other parts of India.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 2 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3

**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. Raja Ram Mohan Roy, a pioneering figure in the socio-religious reform movement, is widely acknowledged as the founder of the Brahmo Samaj.  His vision for a reformed Hinduism, emphasizing monotheism and rejecting certain traditional practices, laid the foundation for this influential movement.

Statement 2 is also correct. The Brahmo Samaj played a crucial role in advocating for several key social reforms within Hinduism. The movement actively campaigned against the practice of Sati (widow immolation), promoted widow remarriage as a means of uplifting women's status, and worked tirelessly to improve access to education for girls and women.

Statement 3 is incorrect.  While the Brahmo Samaj originated in Bengal, its influence extended beyond the region. The movement established branches and followers in other parts of India, demonstrating a wider reach than the statement suggests.  Its impact on social reform was felt across various regions, though its strongest base remained in Bengal.


**5. With reference to Jyotiba Phule's contributions, consider the following statements:**

1. Jyotiba Phule authored the seminal work "Gulamgiri," a powerful critique of caste-based oppression and social inequalities in India.
2.  Jyotiba Phule founded the Satyashodhak Samaj, an organization dedicated to uplifting the marginalized communities and challenging Brahmanical dominance.
3.  Jyotiba Phule's social reform efforts were primarily focused on Maharashtra and did not extend significantly to other parts of India.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1, 2, and 3
(c) 2 only
(d) 1 only


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. Jyotiba Phule, a prominent social reformer, authored "Gulamgiri," a scathing critique of the caste system and its oppressive impact on marginalized communities.  This work is considered a landmark text in the Dalit movement and remains a significant contribution to social justice discourse.

Statement 2 is also correct. Jyotiba Phule established the Satyashodhak Samaj, a crucial organization dedicated to challenging Brahmanical dominance and fighting for the rights and upliftment of the lower castes.  The Samaj played a vital role in promoting social justice and empowering marginalized communities in Maharashtra.

Statement 3 is incorrect. While Jyotiba Phule's primary focus was Maharashtra, his ideas and influence extended beyond the region.  His work inspired similar social reform movements and contributed to broader discussions on caste and social justice throughout India.  His impact was not limited to a single state.


**6. With reference to the events of the early 20th-century nationalist movement, consider the following statements:**

1. The deportation of several Bengal leaders, including Krishna Kumar Mitra and Ashwini Kumar Dutt in 1908, intensified the nationalist movement's momentum.
2.  The arrest and imprisonment of Bal Gangadhar Tilak in 1908 further fueled the growing discontent and resistance against British rule.
3. The Morley-Minto Reforms of 1909, while intended to placate moderate nationalists, ultimately failed to address the core grievances of the nationalist movement and further radicalized it.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1, 2, and 3
(c) 2 only
(d) 3 only

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is accurate. The deportation of prominent Bengal leaders in 1908, including Krishna Kumar Mitra and Ashwini Kumar Dutt, served as a catalyst, further igniting the nationalist movement.  This act of repression by the British government backfired, strengthening the resolve of nationalists and galvanizing public opinion against colonial rule.

Statement 2 is correct. The arrest and subsequent imprisonment of Bal Gangadhar Tilak, a leading figure in the nationalist movement, further intensified the atmosphere of resistance. Tilak's imprisonment became a symbol of the struggle against British oppression and was widely protested, fueling the growing momentum of the movement.

Statement 3 is also correct. The Morley-Minto Reforms of 1909, while presenting some constitutional concessions, failed to adequately address the fundamental concerns of the nationalist movement.  The reforms fell short of expectations, leaving many nationalists dissatisfied and contributing to the further radicalization of the movement. The limited nature of the reforms ultimately proved counterproductive to British aims of appeasement.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided target content, adhering to all specified criteria.  Each question includes the correct answer and a detailed explanation.


**1. With reference to the historical context of Kolhapur and its surrounding areas, consider the following statements:**

1.  Shivaji's conquests significantly impacted the political landscape of Kolhapur, leading to its incorporation into the Maratha empire.
2.  Kolhapur's historical significance extends beyond its political role, as it was also a prominent center for glass manufacturing.
3.  The Gadkari Revolt, a significant peasant uprising, primarily unfolded in the regions surrounding Kolhapur, highlighting agrarian discontent.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3
(d) 3 only

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

All three statements are accurate reflections of Kolhapur's historical context.  Statement 1 correctly identifies Shivaji's role in shaping Kolhapur's political destiny.  His conquests brought Kolhapur under Maratha rule, a pivotal event in the region's history.  Statement 2 accurately highlights Kolhapur's contribution to the glass industry.  While less emphasized than its political history, Kolhapur possessed a vibrant glass-making tradition, adding to its economic and cultural significance.  Finally, Statement 3 correctly places the Gadkari Revolt within the broader context of Kolhapur's history. This revolt, while not solely confined to Kolhapur, significantly affected the region, illustrating the widespread peasant unrest prevalent during that period.  The other options fail to capture the multifaceted historical significance of Kolhapur encompassing political conquests, economic activities, and social uprisings.


**2. With reference to the historical city of Surat and its role in India's past, consider the following statements:**

1.  The Portuguese initially held significant influence over Surat's port, posing a challenge to the ambitions of the East India Company.
2.  Surat's strategic location facilitated its role as a major communication route connecting Bombay and other regions of India.
3.  The Surat Salt Agitations of the early 20th century showcase the city's involvement in broader nationalist movements challenging British policies.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3
(d) 1 only

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

All three statements accurately reflect aspects of Surat's historical significance.  Statement 1 correctly highlights the Portuguese presence and its rivalry with the East India Company for control of Surat's lucrative port.  This competition underscores the broader struggle for dominance in India's maritime trade during the early modern period.  Statement 2 accurately describes Surat's position as a crucial communication link with Bombay.  Its location fostered trade and facilitated the movement of goods and people, solidifying its importance within India's network of cities. Statement 3 correctly points to the Surat Salt Agitations as evidence of Surat's participation in the Indian nationalist movement.  These agitations reflect the city's involvement in resisting British economic policies, demonstrating the widespread nature of the anti-colonial struggle.  The other options are incomplete in their portrayal of Surat's rich history, neglecting either its early modern maritime conflicts, its role in regional connectivity, or its contributions to the nationalist movement.


**3. With reference to the socio-political dynamics of Sylhet, consider the following statements:**

1.  The Khasi Uprising, a significant tribal rebellion, took place within the geographical boundaries of modern-day Sylhet, demonstrating resistance against external authorities.
2.  Sylhet's history includes periods under the control of various regional and imperial powers, reflecting its strategic location and significance in regional politics.
3.  The Bhils, a tribal group known for their participation in various revolts against the British, had significant presence in and around Sylhet, contributing to the region's history of resistance.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3

**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statements 1 and 2 correctly represent aspects of Sylhet's historical context.  Statement 1 accurately identifies the Khasi Uprising as an event within Sylhet's history, showcasing the region's involvement in broader struggles against imperial control.  Statement 2 correctly points to Sylhet's changing political landscape over time, indicating its strategic position within the larger political geography of the region.  However, Statement 3 is incorrect. While the Bhils were indeed involved in various revolts against the British, their primary areas of activity were in the Western Ghats and not Sylhet.  The other options incorrectly include Statement 3, which provides an inaccurate geographical placement of the Bhils' activities.  Therefore, only statements 1 and 2 are accurate.


**4. With reference to the 1857 Revolt and its various interpretations, consider the following statements:**

1.  The Revolt of 1857, while primarily originating as a sepoy mutiny, rapidly evolved into a wider rebellion encompassing diverse social groups and grievances.
2.  The participation of various regional leaders, such as Nana Saheb, Rani Lakshmibai, and Kunwar Singh, added distinct regional dimensions to the Revolt, making it a complex and multi-faceted event.
3.  Historians uniformly agree on the Revolt's primary motive, with a consensus view identifying religious factors as the sole and decisive cause of the uprising.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 2 only
(d) 3 only

**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statements 1 and 2 accurately reflect key aspects of the 1857 Revolt. Statement 1 correctly emphasizes the Revolt's transformation from a sepoy mutiny into a broader rebellion involving civilians from various social strata. This expansion reflects the accumulation of widespread discontent against British rule. Statement 2 correctly highlights the participation of regional leaders who brought diverse regional concerns and dynamics into the revolt.  The actions of Nana Saheb, Rani Lakshmibai, and Kunwar Singh, among others, demonstrate the complex interplay of local and broader issues. However, Statement 3 is inaccurate.  Historical interpretations of the 1857 Revolt are diverse and contested. While religious factors played a role, particularly the greased cartridges incident, attributing the Revolt solely to religious motivations is an oversimplification.  Scholars have highlighted economic, political, and social factors as equally significant contributors. The other options fail to adequately capture the complexity and multiple interpretations of this pivotal historical event.


**5. With reference to the leaders of the 1857 Revolt and their respective areas of influence, consider the following statements:**

1.  Khan Bahadur effectively led the revolt in Bareilly, utilizing his local influence and military capabilities to resist British forces.
2.  Kunwar Singh, despite his advanced age, played a crucial leadership role in Bihar, effectively organizing and coordinating rebel forces against the British.
3.  Maulvi Ahmadullah, initially active in Madras, later shifted his focus to Awadh and Rohilkhand, becoming a prominent leader in the northern regions.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1, 2, and 3
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1 only

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

All three statements accurately reflect the contributions of these leaders to the 1857 Revolt. Statement 1 correctly identifies Khan Bahadur's leadership in Bareilly, showcasing his successful organization of rebel forces and resistance against British authority. Statement 2 accurately describes Kunwar Singh's crucial role in Bihar, demonstrating his military prowess and organizational skills despite his age.  Statement 3 is also accurate in tracing Maulvi Ahmadullah's activities, highlighting his initial presence in Madras and his subsequent leadership in Awadh and Rohilkhand.  The other options fail to fully encompass the contributions of these significant leaders to the 1857 Revolt in their respective regions.


**6. With reference to the impact of the 1857 Revolt, consider the following statements:**

1.  The revolt led to the immediate and complete abolition of the East India Company's rule, paving the way for direct British Crown rule in India.
2.  The Queen's Proclamation of 1858, while making certain promises to the Indian populace, ultimately failed to address the deep-seated grievances that fueled the revolt.
3.  The revolt resulted in significant changes in the structure and composition of the British Indian Army, leading to a reduction in the number of Indian soldiers and an increase in the European contingent.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

All three statements accurately reflect the long-term consequences of the 1857 Revolt. Statement 1 is correct in stating that the revolt led to the end of the East India Company's rule, bringing about direct rule by the British Crown.  This significant change fundamentally altered the administrative structure of British India. Statement 2 is correct as the Queen's Proclamation, while promising religious tolerance and other reforms, ultimately did not fully address the underlying causes of the revolteconomic exploitation, political subjugation, and social injustices. Statement 3 is also correct because the British significantly reorganized the Indian army after 1857, reducing the proportion of Indian soldiers and increasing the number of European troops. This reflected a shift in British military strategy aimed at enhancing control and minimizing the risk of future uprisings.  The other options are incomplete, neglecting certain crucial consequences of the 1857 Revolt.


**7. With reference to the socio-religious reform movements in 19th-century India, consider the following statements:**

1.  Raja Ram Mohan Roy's reformist efforts focused primarily on advocating for Western education and actively opposing traditional practices like Sati.
2.  Swami Dayanand Saraswati played a crucial role in the revival of Vedic traditions and the promotion of social reforms within the Hindu community.
3.  Swami Vivekananda's influence extended beyond religious reforms, encompassing social and nationalistic aspects, contributing to the rise of modern Indian nationalism.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3
(d) 1 only

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

All three statements accurately describe the contributions of these prominent figures to 19th-century socio-religious reform movements.  Statement 1 correctly identifies Raja Ram Mohan Roy's advocacy for Western education and his opposition to Sati.  His efforts were instrumental in initiating modern social reforms within the Hindu community. Statement 2 accurately highlights Swami Dayanand Saraswati's role in the revival of Vedic traditions and his promotion of social reforms. His Arya Samaj movement had a significant impact on Hindu society. Statement 3 correctly notes Swami Vivekananda's multifaceted influence, encompassing religious reform, social work, and the promotion of nationalism.  His contributions to the rise of modern Indian nationalism are widely acknowledged.  The other options fail to fully capture the breadth and depth of the contributions made by these influential reformers.


**8.  With reference to the Wahabi Movement, consider the following statements:**

1.  The Wahabi Movement was primarily a revivalist movement within the Islamic faith, advocating for a return to what its adherents perceived as the purer and original form of Islam.
2.  The movement's activities were largely confined to a single region of India, with limited geographical spread and influence.
3.  The British government viewed the Wahabi Movement with neutrality, not actively seeking to suppress its activities.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 3 only

**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Only Statement 1 accurately describes a central aspect of the Wahabi Movement. The movement aimed to purify Islamic practices and beliefs, returning to what its followers considered the original tenets of the faith.  Statement 2 is incorrect. The Wahabi movement was not confined to a single region, rather it spread across various parts of India, influencing many Muslims. Statement 3 is also incorrect. The British government did not remain neutral towards the Wahabi movement; they actively sought to suppress its activities, viewing it as a potential threat to their rule.  The other options include inaccurate statements about the movement's geographical reach and the British government's response, highlighting the importance of understanding the movement's broad influence and the colonial authorities' reaction.


**9. With reference to the Partition of Bengal and its aftermath, consider the following statements:**

1. The partition of Bengal was met with unanimous support from all sections of the Indian National Congress.
2. The Surat session of the Indian National Congress in 1907 witnessed a significant split between moderate and extremist factions.
3. The Morley-Minto Reforms of 1909 were introduced by the British government primarily to appease the extremist faction within the Indian National Congress.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 3 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 only
(d) 2 and 3 only

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Only Statement 2 correctly reflects the historical context surrounding the Partition of Bengal. The Surat session indeed saw a major split within the Congress, highlighting the growing rift between moderate and extremist nationalists. Statement 1 is incorrect as the partition was met with widespread opposition from various factions within the Congress, not unanimous support. Statement 3 is also incorrect; the Morley-Minto Reforms were intended to appease the moderates, not the extremists, as a strategy to divide and weaken the nationalist movement.  The other options incorrectly include statements that misrepresent the political dynamics within the Congress and the British government's strategies in response to the growing nationalist movement.


**10. With reference to the political and social conditions in Bihar during the 19th and early 20th centuries, consider the following statements:**

1. The Champaran Satyagraha, a significant event in India's freedom struggle, was entirely confined to the urban areas of Bihar.
2. The introduction of the Permanent Settlement in Bihar led to a significant improvement in the economic conditions of the peasantry.
3. Sahjanand Saraswati, a prominent leader of the peasant movement, played a crucial role in mobilizing rural communities in Bihar.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 3 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3
(d) 2 and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Only Statement 3 accurately reflects the historical context of Bihar. Sahjanand Saraswati was indeed a key figure in mobilizing peasants and advocating for their rights.  Statement 1 is incorrect; the Champaran Satyagraha involved both rural and urban areas of Bihar, highlighting the widespread agrarian distress. Statement 2 is also incorrect; the Permanent Settlement, while initially intended to stabilize revenue collection, led to the exploitation of peasants and their impoverishment in the long run.  The other options incorrectly include statements that misrepresent the scope and impact of specific events and policies in Bihar.  Therefore, only Statement 3 is accurate.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided text, adhering to all specified criteria.  Each question is designed to be challenging and require in-depth knowledge of the subject matter.


**1. With reference to 19th-century socio-religious reform movements in India, consider the following statements:**

1.  The Prarthana Samaj, unlike the Arya Samaj, primarily focused on reforming Hindu society through gradual, evolutionary changes rather than a complete overhaul of religious practices.
2.  The Aligarh Movement, spearheaded by Sir Syed Ahmad Khan, aimed to reconcile Islamic teachings with the demands of modern scientific thought and education, thereby promoting a more progressive Muslim society.
3.  The Ramakrishna Mission, emphasizing Vedanta philosophy and spiritual practices, differed significantly from the Arya Samaj's focus on Vedic literalism and social reform through a more assertive approach.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

All three statements accurately reflect the nuanced differences between prominent 19th-century socio-religious reform movements in India. The Prarthana Samaj, inspired by the Brahmo Samaj, advocated for a gradual and less confrontational approach to social reform within Hinduism, unlike the Arya Samaj's more radical and revivalist stance. The Aligarh Movement, under Sir Syed Ahmad Khan's leadership, successfully modernized Muslim education and society by bridging the gap between traditional Islamic beliefs and modern scientific knowledge.  The Ramakrishna Mission, while sharing some common goals with the Arya Samaj regarding social reform, distinctly emphasized spiritual realization through Vedanta philosophy, contrasting with the Arya Samaj's stricter Vedic interpretations and its more assertive social reform agenda.  Therefore, all three statements are correct.


**2. With reference to the British revenue policies in India, consider the following statements:**

1.  The Permanent Settlement, implemented primarily in Bengal, granted zamindars complete proprietary rights over their lands, leading to increased agricultural productivity and prosperity for the peasantry.
2.  The Ryotwari system, prevalent in Madras and Bombay Presidencies, directly taxed individual cultivators, resulting in efficient revenue collection but often leading to over-assessment and peasant indebtedness.
3.  The Mahalwari system, implemented in parts of North India, aimed to balance collective village responsibility with individual cultivator rights, but often suffered from inaccurate assessments and corruption.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. While the Permanent Settlement did grant zamindars proprietary rights, it did not lead to increased agricultural productivity or peasant prosperity.  Instead, it led to absentee landlordism, exploitation of tenants, and subinfeudation, hindering agricultural development.  Statements 2 and 3 correctly describe the Ryotwari and Mahalwari systems. The Ryotwari system, while efficient in revenue collection, often resulted in over-assessment and peasant indebtedness due to its inflexible nature. The Mahalwari system, while intending to balance collective and individual responsibilities, suffered from flaws in assessment and widespread corruption.  Therefore, only statements 2 and 3 are correct.


**3. With reference to the social reform movements in 19th-century India and the British response, consider the following statements:**

1.  The British government actively supported all social reform movements, viewing them as crucial for modernizing Indian society and strengthening their own rule.
2.  The abolition of Sati in 1829, while a significant humanitarian achievement, was primarily driven by the persistent advocacy of Indian reformers like Raja Ram Mohan Roy, with the British government initially hesitant.
3.  The Age of Consent Act of 1891, restricting child marriage, was passed primarily due to pressure from British reformers and social workers, with minimal involvement from Indian activists.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. The British government's support for social reform movements was inconsistent and often motivated by political expediency rather than a genuine commitment to social justice.  They sometimes actively opposed reforms that threatened established power structures or religious sensitivities. Statement 2 accurately highlights the crucial role of Indian reformers like Raja Ram Mohan Roy in advocating for the abolition of Sati, with the British government initially hesitant due to concerns about upsetting orthodox elements of Indian society. Statement 3 is incorrect. While British reformers certainly contributed to the discourse, the Age of Consent Act was also a result of significant pressure and advocacy from Indian activists, particularly concerning the Rukhmabai case.  Therefore, only statement 2 is correct.


**4. With reference to the causes of the 1857 Revolt, consider the following statements:**

1. The annexation of Awadh by Lord Dalhousie was a significant trigger for the revolt, particularly among sepoys from that region, who felt a strong sense of regional loyalty and resentment towards British expansion.
2.  The introduction of the Enfield rifle, with its allegedly greased cartridges, was the sole and primary cause of the widespread sepoy mutiny that ignited the revolt.
3. Economic grievances, including widespread poverty, land dispossession, and the destruction of traditional crafts, were insignificant factors in fueling popular discontent and participation in the revolt.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 2 only


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The annexation of Awadh, a region from which many sepoys originated, profoundly impacted their sense of loyalty and identity, fueling resentment towards British rule. This contributed significantly to the initial mutiny that spread into a wider revolt. Statement 2 is incorrect. The greased cartridges were a trigger for the sepoy mutiny but not the sole cause of the 1857 Revolt. The revolt was a complex event driven by multiple factors. Statement 3 is incorrect. Economic grievances, including widespread poverty, land dispossession, and the destruction of traditional crafts, were major factors contributing to popular discontent and widespread participation in the revolt. These grievances were not insignificant; they played a critical role in shaping the larger context of rebellion. Therefore, only statement 1 is correct.



**5. With reference to the individuals involved in 19th-century social reform movements, consider the following statements:**

1.  Pandit Ishwar Chandra Vidyasagar played a pivotal role in advocating for Hindu widows' remarriage, successfully pushing for the passage of the Hindu Widows' Remarriage Act of 1856.
2.  Behramji M. Malabari's efforts focused primarily on advocating for the rights of untouchable communities and the eradication of caste-based discrimination.
3.  Jyotiba Phule, along with his wife Savitribai, was a pioneering figure in social reform in Maharashtra, actively promoting women's education and challenging Brahmanical dominance.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 accurately reflects Ishwar Chandra Vidyasagar's crucial contribution to the Hindu Widows' Remarriage Act of 1856. Statement 2 is incorrect; Behramji M. Malabari's primary focus was on reforming Parsi society and advocating against child marriage, particularly through his work on the Age of Consent Act.  Statement 3 correctly describes Jyotiba Phule and Savitribai Phule's significant role in challenging Brahmanical dominance and promoting education for women from marginalized communities in Maharashtra.  Therefore, only statements 1 and 3 are correct.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided target content, adhering to all specified criteria.  Each question includes the correct answer and a detailed explanation.

**1. With reference to the Bhils, consider the following statements:**

1. The Bhils primarily inhabited the Aravalli range, participating in the Shamlaji Fair.
2.  Govind Guru played a significant role in the Bhil community's resistance against the British Raj.
3. The Bhils, known for their distinct cultural practices, shared a close geographical proximity with the Kolis.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is partially incorrect. While the Bhils do participate in the Shamlaji Fair, their primary habitat is not limited to the Aravalli range. They are spread across a wider geographical area, including the Western Ghats, as indicated in the target content.  The Shamlaji Fair is a significant event for them but doesn't define their entire geographical distribution.

Statement 2 is correct. Govind Guru's association with the Bhils is well-documented, highlighting his role in social reform and, indirectly, in their resistance to British rule. This aligns directly with the provided data.

Statement 3 is correct. The target content explicitly states that the Bhils and Kolis were neighbors, indicating a shared geographical proximity. This demonstrates a clear inter-tribal relationship.

Therefore, only statements 2 and 3 accurately reflect the information provided within the context of the Bhil community.


**2. With reference to the history of Mewar, consider the following statements:**

1.  The Mughals' conflict with Mewar culminated in Aurangzeb's successful annexation of the region.
2.  Chittor, a strategically important location, was under the control of Mewar throughout its history.
3. Rana Sanga's reign marked a period of significant expansion and consolidation of Mewar's power.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. While Aurangzeb did engage in conflicts with Mewar, he never successfully annexed the entire region. Mewar, despite facing numerous invasions and conflicts, maintained a degree of autonomy throughout its history. The statement presents an oversimplified and inaccurate depiction of a complex historical relationship.

Statement 2 is incorrect.  While Chittor was a crucial part of Mewar, its control wasn't absolute throughout Mewar's history. The region experienced periods of conflict and shifting control, making the statement too broad and inaccurate.

Statement 3 is correct. Rana Sanga's rule is indeed associated with a period of Mewar's expansion and consolidation of power, reflecting his important role in the region's history. This aligns with the historical record.

Therefore, only statement 3 accurately reflects the historical context of Mewar.


**3. With reference to the Arya Samaj, consider the following statements:**

1.  The Arya Samaj, founded in Bombay, primarily focused on promoting Vedic ideals and challenging the caste system.
2.  Dayananda Saraswati's Satyartha Prakash advocated for social reforms, including widow remarriage.
3. The Arya Samaj's activities were limited to the Punjab region, with Lahore as its primary center.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is partially incorrect. The Arya Samaj was indeed founded in Bombay, and it promoted Vedic ideals and challenged the caste system. However, its influence extended far beyond Bombay, making the statement too restrictive.

Statement 2 is correct. Dayananda Saraswati's Satyartha Prakash was a seminal work advocating for various social reforms, including widow remarriage, aligning perfectly with the target content.

Statement 3 is incorrect. The Arya Samaj's influence and activities were not confined to the Punjab region. While Lahore was an important center, the movement spread across several parts of India. This statement misrepresents the Samaj's geographical reach.

Therefore, only statements 1 and 2 correctly represent aspects of the Arya Samaj.


**4. With reference to the role of Bal Gangadhar Tilak, consider the following statements:**

1.  Tilak's Ganapati and Shivaji festivals were primarily aimed at fostering Hindu unity and challenging British rule.
2. Tilak, a leader of the Indian National Congress, consistently advocated for complete independence ('Swaraj').
3.  Tilak's newspaper, the *Kesari*, primarily focused on promoting constitutional methods of political action.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 2 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. Tilak's festivals were indeed instrumental in promoting Hindu unity and providing a platform to indirectly challenge British rule.  This reflects his strategic use of religious and cultural events for political mobilization.

Statement 2 is correct. Although Tilak's initial approach might have been more nuanced, his ultimate goal was indeed 'Swaraj', which he openly championed. The statement correctly reflects his stance on independence.

Statement 3 is incorrect.  While *Kesari* did cover constitutional matters, its primary focus was on promoting a more assertive and nationalist approach, often critical of the British government.  The statement misrepresents the newspaper's editorial stance.

Therefore, only statements 1 and 2 accurately reflect Tilak's role and activities.


**5. With reference to the Non-Cooperation Movement, consider the following statements:**

1. The Chauri Chaura incident led to the immediate suspension of the movement due to concerns about escalating violence.
2. The movement saw widespread participation from peasants, but the involvement of the urban elite remained limited.
3.  The Khilafat issue, although unrelated to Indian nationalism, provided a crucial impetus for the movement's launch.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The Chauri Chaura incident, characterized by violence, directly led Gandhi to suspend the Non-Cooperation Movement due to his unwavering commitment to non-violent methods.

Statement 2 is incorrect. While peasant participation was indeed substantial, the movement also involved significant participation from the urban elite, albeit with varying degrees of commitment.  The statement oversimplifies the movement's social base.

Statement 3 is correct. The Khilafat issue, although stemming from a separate concern, played a critical role in uniting Hindus and Muslims, providing the necessary momentum for launching the broader Non-Cooperation Movement.

Thus, statements 1 and 3 correctly capture key aspects of the Non-Cooperation Movement.


**6. With reference to the 1857 Revolt, consider the following statements:**

1. The annexation of Awadh by Lord Dalhousie was a major contributing factor to the widespread discontent among sepoys.
2. The revolt was primarily a result of sepoy mutiny, with limited participation from other sections of society.
3. Economic exploitation and the destruction of traditional economic structures were not significant factors leading to the revolt.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 3 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The annexation of Awadh fueled resentment among sepoys, many of whom originated from that region, and significantly contributed to the atmosphere of unrest that preceded the 1857 Revolt.

Statement 2 is incorrect. The 1857 Revolt was far more than just a sepoy mutiny; it involved widespread participation from peasants, artisans, and other social groups.  The statement drastically underestimates the revolt's scope.

Statement 3 is incorrect.  Economic exploitation and the disruption of traditional economic systems were major factors underlying the widespread discontent and were key drivers of the revolt.  The statement ignores crucial socio-economic factors.

Therefore, only statement 1 accurately reflects a significant cause of the 1857 Revolt.


**7.  Consider the following statements about social reform movements in 19th-century India:**

1.  The Brahmo Samaj actively supported widow remarriage and challenged traditional social practices.
2.  Jyotiba Phule's work focused primarily on uplifting the lower castes and promoting women's education.
3.  The Arya Samaj's activities were primarily confined to religious reform, with minimal focus on social issues.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 2 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The Brahmo Samaj played a significant role in advocating for widow remarriage and challenging many traditional practices, aligning with its broader reformist agenda.

Statement 2 is correct. Jyotiba Phule's contributions are well-known for his focus on social justice for lower castes and his advocacy for women's education and empowerment.

Statement 3 is incorrect. The Arya Samaj, while focused on religious reform, also actively addressed numerous social issues, including the caste system and widow remarriage. The statement overlooks the Samaj's comprehensive approach to reform.

Therefore, statements 1 and 2 accurately describe the contributions of these social reform movements.


**8. With reference to the Bengal region, consider the following statements:**

1.  The Permanent Settlement, implemented in Bengal, led to the concentration of land ownership in the hands of a few.
2.  The Indigo Revolt in Bengal demonstrated widespread peasant resistance against oppressive plantation practices.
3.  The Partition of Bengal, although initially intended to weaken nationalist sentiment, ultimately backfired and strengthened it.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The Permanent Settlement in Bengal, while aiming to stabilize revenue collection, resulted in the concentration of land ownership among a small elite, creating widespread agrarian issues.

Statement 2 is correct. The Indigo Revolt showcased widespread peasant resistance against the exploitative practices of indigo planters, highlighting the depth of agrarian discontent in Bengal.

Statement 3 is correct. The Partition of Bengal, intended to weaken nationalist sentiment, had the opposite effect, uniting various groups against British rule and strengthening the nationalist movement.

Therefore, all three statements accurately reflect significant historical events and their impact on Bengal.


**9. With reference to the role of Mahatma Gandhi, consider the following statements:**

1.  Gandhi's emphasis on non-violent resistance ('Satyagraha') proved ineffective against British rule in India.
2.  The Champaran Satyagraha demonstrated Gandhi's early application of Satyagraha and his ability to mobilize rural populations.
3.  Gandhi's political ideology was solely focused on achieving independence through non-violent means, without any engagement with other approaches.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 2 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. Gandhi's Satyagraha, although facing challenges, ultimately played a significant role in India's independence movement, demonstrating its effectiveness as a method of mass mobilization and resistance.

Statement 2 is correct. The Champaran Satyagraha is a landmark event showing Gandhi's early use of Satyagraha and its impact on mobilizing rural populations against exploitative practices.

Statement 3 is incorrect. While Gandhi strongly advocated for non-violent methods, his approach wasn't exclusively limited to non-violent means. He engaged with and considered various strategies, and his understanding evolved over time.

Therefore, only statement 2 accurately reflects aspects of Gandhi's role in the Indian independence struggle.


**10. With reference to Bihar, consider the following statements:**

1.  The Sepoy Mutiny of 1857 had limited impact in Bihar, with minimal participation from the local population.
2. The Champaran Satyagraha, led by Mahatma Gandhi, took place primarily in Bihar, addressing issues of peasant unrest.
3.  Bihar's historical significance is primarily associated with Buddhist sites, with limited evidence of other historical periods.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 2 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 2 and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. The Sepoy Mutiny of 1857 did affect Bihar, with participation from various social groups.  The statement misrepresents the extent of the revolt's reach.

Statement 2 is correct. The Champaran Satyagraha, a pivotal event in India's independence movement, did take place in Bihar, addressing the concerns of the local peasant population.

Statement 3 is incorrect. Bihar's historical significance extends far beyond Buddhist sites.  The region has a rich history spanning various periods and dynasties, including pre-Buddhist and post-Buddhist eras. The statement is an oversimplification of a complex history.

Therefore, only statement 2 accurately reflects aspects of Bihar's history and its association with the Indian independence movement.

**1. With reference to the 19th-century socio-religious reform movements in India, consider the following statements:**

1.  The Prarthana Samaj, founded in Bombay, primarily focused on religious reform, advocating monotheism as its central tenet.
2.  The Satyashodhak Samaj, founded by Jyotirao Phule, aimed at social transformation by advocating for the education of women and lower castes, challenging Brahmanical supremacy.
3.  The Arya Samaj, founded by Dayanand Saraswati, emphasized a return to Vedic principles, advocating for a casteless society and opposing idolatry, but also initiated the Shuddhi movement to reconvert those who had converted to other religions.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 2 only


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. While the Prarthana Samaj did advocate monotheism, its primary focus was on social reform rather than solely religious reform.  It addressed issues like caste discrimination, women's education, and widow remarriage, aligning with broader social reform movements of the time.  Its emphasis on monotheism was part of a larger effort to modernize and reform Hindu society, not its singular objective.

Statement 2 is correct. The Satyashodhak Samaj, founded by Jyotirao Phule, directly challenged the Brahmanical social order.  Its core aim was social justice and empowerment of marginalized communities through education and social reform. This was a radical departure from the more moderate approaches of other reform movements.  It actively worked to uplift the status of women and lower castes, addressing the root causes of social inequality.

Statement 3 is correct. The Arya Samaj, founded by Dayanand Saraswati, advocated a return to Vedic principles, interpreting them in a way that challenged traditional Hindu practices.  It promoted a casteless society, opposed idolatry and ritualistic excesses, and emphasized a rational approach to religion.  However, the Shuddhi movement, aimed at reconverting those who had converted to other religions, is a significant, though controversial, aspect of its activities. This movement, while intended to strengthen Hindu society, also contributed to communal tensions.


**2. With reference to the Aligarh Movement and its founder, consider the following statements:**

1.  Syed Ahmed Khan's primary objective was to promote a distinctly anti-Congress political front for Indian Muslims, advocating for complete separation from Hindu nationalist aspirations.
2.  Syed Ahmed Khan founded the Mohammedan Anglo-Oriental College (later Aligarh Muslim University) to promote Western scientific education among Indian Muslims while simultaneously advocating for a reconciliation between Western science and Islamic teachings.
3.  Syed Ahmed Khan vehemently opposed any form of social reform within the Muslim community, advocating for the strict adherence to traditional customs and practices.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect.  While Syed Ahmed Khan did advocate for a separate Muslim identity and initially opposed active participation in the Congress, his primary aim was not to create a distinctly anti-Congress political front. His focus was on educational and social reform within the Muslim community to enable them to compete with Hindus in the modernizing British India.  His later support for a separate Muslim electorate stemmed from concerns about Muslim representation and safeguarding their interests within a broader political landscape, not outright antagonism towards the Congress.

Statement 2 is correct. The establishment of the Mohammedan Anglo-Oriental College was a cornerstone of Syed Ahmed Khan's vision.  He believed that modern Western education, particularly in science and technology, was essential for the upliftment of Indian Muslims. His interpretation of Islamic teachings allowed for the integration of Western knowledge, demonstrating a pragmatic approach to modernization without compromising religious beliefs.

Statement 3 is incorrect. Syed Ahmed Khan was a significant advocate for social reform within the Muslim community. He actively championed women's education, opposed purdah and polygamy, and advocated for easier divorce procedures.  His efforts aimed at modernizing Muslim society, challenging traditional practices considered harmful or outdated.


**3. With reference to the 1857 Revolt, consider the following statements:**

1. The primary cause of the 1857 revolt was widespread dissatisfaction among sepoys solely due to the introduction of new Enfield rifles with greased cartridges rumored to be made of animal fat.
2. The annexation of Awadh by Lord Dalhousie significantly contributed to the unrest leading to the 1857 revolt, fueling resentment among sepoys and the Awadh population.
3. The 1857 revolt was a spontaneous and completely unorganized uprising, lacking any significant leadership or coordination among different groups involved.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. While the greased cartridges controversy acted as a trigger, it was not the sole or primary cause of the 1857 revolt.  The revolt was a culmination of numerous long-standing grievances, including economic exploitation, political subjugation, cultural insensitivity, and the undermining of traditional power structures. The cartridge issue served as a catalyst, igniting pre-existing discontent.

Statement 2 is correct. The annexation of Awadh was a major contributing factor.  The annexation itself, the subsequent administrative changes, and the economic hardships imposed on the Awadh population significantly fueled resentment and contributed to the widespread rebellion.  Many sepoys hailed from Awadh, making the annexation a deeply personal grievance.

Statement 3 is incorrect. The 1857 revolt, while not perfectly organized, was far from a spontaneous and uncoordinated uprising.  It involved various groupssepoys, peasants, zamindars, and even some princely stateswho, though not unified under a single leader, shared common grievances against British rule.  The revolt involved strategic planning and military actions in different regions, demonstrating a degree of coordination and leadership, although it lacked overall national unity.


**4. With reference to the Brahmo Samaj and its evolution, consider the following statements:**

1.  The Brahmo Samaj, founded by Raja Ram Mohan Roy, immediately upon its inception, advocated for complete rejection of all Hindu scriptures and traditions, promoting a purely monotheistic, Western-influenced religion.
2.  Keshab Chandra Sen's leadership of the Brahmo Samaj led to a period of increased dynamism and expansion, but also internal divisions due to his more radical interpretations of religious doctrines.
3.  Debendranath Tagore's leadership of the Brahmo Samaj focused primarily on political activism and direct confrontation with the British colonial government, leading to widespread arrests and suppression of the movement.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect.  Raja Ram Mohan Roy's Brahmo Samaj did not advocate for a complete rejection of Hindu scriptures and traditions.  Instead, it aimed at reforming Hinduism by emphasizing monotheism and rationalism, while selectively incorporating elements from other religions.  It sought to purify Hinduism by removing what it saw as superstitious practices and social evils,  not replacing it entirely.

Statement 2 is correct. Keshab Chandra Sen's leadership indeed marked a period of significant growth and expansion for the Brahmo Samaj, establishing branches across India.  However, his more radical interpretations of religious doctrines and his emphasis on a more inclusive and cosmopolitan approach led to internal conflicts and ultimately resulted in splits within the Samaj.

Statement 3 is incorrect. Debendranath Tagore's leadership of the Brahmo Samaj was not primarily focused on political activism and direct confrontation with the British. While the Brahmo Samaj did address social and political issues, its focus remained largely on religious and social reform.  It did not engage in widespread political activism that led to mass arrests or significant suppression by the colonial government.


**5. With reference to  19th-century social reformers in India, consider the following statements:**

1.  Gopal Ganesh Agarkar's primary contribution was in the field of religious reform, advocating for a complete overhaul of Hindu religious practices and the establishment of a new religion.
2.  Mahadev Govind Ranade was a key figure in the Prarthana Samaj, significantly contributing to its growth and influence through his advocacy for social reforms such as womens education and widow remarriage.
3.  Dadabhai Naoroji's work focused primarily on economic issues, notably his "Drain of Wealth" theory, and he played a limited role in social reform movements.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. Gopal Ganesh Agarkar was a prominent social reformer, but his primary focus was not religious reform in the sense of establishing a new religion.  He was more concerned with social and educational reforms, advocating for the elimination of caste discrimination, promoting rationalism and modern education.  His work was within the existing framework of Hindu society, aiming for internal reform rather than a complete religious overhaul.

Statement 2 is correct. Mahadev Govind Ranade played a crucial role in the Prarthana Samaj, contributing significantly to its popularity and its social reform agenda.  He was a strong advocate for social causes, including women's education and widow remarriage, using his influence to promote these within the Samaj and beyond.

Statement 3 is correct. Dadabhai Naoroji is primarily known for his economic analysis of British rule in India, most famously his "Drain of Wealth" theory, which highlighted the exploitative nature of British economic policies.  While he was involved in broader nationalist and social reform efforts, his main contribution lay in the economic realm.  His focus on economic exploitation did, however, indirectly support social reform by addressing the root causes of poverty and inequality.

**1. With reference to the East India Company's administration in India, consider the following statements:**

1. The East India Company's revenue policies consistently prioritized the welfare of Indian cultivators, leading to widespread agricultural prosperity.
2. The Company's  military force in India consisted solely of British troops, with no Indian soldiers employed.
3.  The Company's expansion in India involved significant conflicts with various Indian rulers and powers.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 3 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. The East India Company's revenue policies, including the Permanent Settlement, Ryotwari System, and Mahalwari System, often led to the exploitation of Indian cultivators and widespread rural indebtedness. While aiming for efficient revenue collection, these systems often neglected the welfare of the peasantry, resulting in famines and economic hardship.  The focus was on maximizing revenue for the Company, not on the well-being of the farmers.

Statement 2 is incorrect. The East India Company's army in India heavily relied on Indian sepoys. These Indian soldiers formed a significant part of the Company's military strength.  The reliance on Indian sepoys was a crucial aspect of the Company's military strategy and a major factor leading to the 1857 Revolt.

Statement 3 is correct. The East India Company's expansion across India was marked by numerous conflicts with various Indian rulers, including the Nawabs of Bengal, the Nizam of Hyderabad, and Maratha rulers. These conflicts, often involving military engagements, were instrumental in the Company's gradual consolidation of power across the subcontinent.  The Battle of Plassey and the Battle of Buxar are prime examples of such conflicts.


**2. With reference to the social and religious reform movements in 19th-century India, consider the following statements:**

1. The Prarthana Samaj primarily focused on advocating for radical social changes, including the complete abolition of the caste system.
2. The Faraizi Movement was a reform movement within Hinduism that emphasized a return to Vedic principles.
3.  The Satyashodhak Samaj, founded by Jyotirao Phule, aimed to uplift the marginalized castes and challenge social inequalities.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 3 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) 2 and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. While the Prarthana Samaj advocated for social reforms, its approach was more moderate than radical.  It focused on issues like widow remarriage and promoting monotheism, but didn't directly call for the complete abolition of the caste system.  Its reform efforts were gradual and aimed at influencing society through dialogue and education.

Statement 2 is incorrect. The Faraizi Movement was a socio-religious reform movement within Islam in Bengal. It aimed at purifying Islam and reforming Muslim society by returning to what its leaders considered the original teachings of Islam. It was not a Hindu reform movement.

Statement 3 is correct. The Satyashodhak Samaj, founded by Jyotirao Phule, was a crucial movement in challenging the caste system and advocating for the rights of the marginalized castes.  Phule's work focused on education, social justice, and empowering the lower castes, directly confronting the existing social inequalities.


**3. With reference to the figures involved in the Indian freedom struggle, consider the following statements:**

1. Mahadev Govind Ranade was a prominent leader of the revolutionary terrorist groups active in Bengal during the early 20th century.
2. Swami Sahajanand Saraswati is primarily known for his contributions to the trade union movement in India.
3.  N.G. Ranga played a significant role in the All India Kisan Sabha, a prominent organization representing the interests of Indian farmers.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 1 and 2 only


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. Mahadev Govind Ranade was a prominent social reformer, scholar, and leader of the Indian National Congress. He was associated with the moderate wing of the Congress and advocated for social and political reforms through constitutional means. He was not involved in revolutionary terrorism.

Statement 2 is incorrect. Swami Sahajanand Saraswati was a prominent leader of the peasant movement in India and played a significant role in the All India Kisan Sabha. While he may have had some indirect connection to labour issues through the broader context of social and economic justice, his primary contribution was to the Kisan movement.

Statement 3 is correct. N.G. Ranga was a key figure in the All India Kisan Sabha (AIKS), a significant organization representing the interests of Indian farmers.  He played a leading role in advocating for peasant rights and land reforms and was a prominent voice in the Indian nationalist movement.


**4. With reference to the 19th-century Indian uprisings, consider the following statements:**

1. The Indigo Rebellion was primarily a revolt by zamindars against the British East India Company's revenue policies.
2. The Waghera Uprising was a major peasant rebellion in Bengal against the British East India Company's policies.
3.  The revolt led by Kunwar Singh was a significant uprising during the 1857 Sepoy Mutiny.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 3 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) 2 and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. The Indigo Rebellion was primarily a peasant uprising in Bengal against the coercive indigo cultivation practices imposed by the British planters.  It was not a revolt led by zamindars.  The peasants resisted the forced cultivation and the unfair prices offered for indigo.

Statement 2 is incorrect. The Waghera Uprising was a rebellion in Gujarat, not Bengal, against British rule. It was a relatively localized uprising, not a major peasant rebellion across Bengal.  The uprising involved various grievances against the British administration.

Statement 3 is correct. Kunwar Singh's leadership was a crucial element of the 1857 Sepoy Mutiny. His participation in the rebellion, particularly his military leadership, significantly contributed to the spread and intensity of the uprising in Bihar and surrounding areas.  His resistance against the British forces was a notable part of the 1857 events.


**5. With reference to the impact of British policies on India, consider the following statements:**

1. The British implemented a policy of complete non-interference in the internal affairs of Indian princely states.
2. The British consistently supported social reform movements in India, leading to significant changes in social structures.
3.  The British revenue policies significantly contributed to the economic impoverishment of many Indian farmers.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 3 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) 2 and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. While the British initially adopted a policy of non-interference to maintain stability, as the 19th century progressed, they increasingly intervened in the internal affairs of princely states, exercising paramountcy to assert their control and influence.  This intervention was driven by political and strategic considerations.

Statement 2 is incorrect. The British attitude towards social reform was inconsistent. While initially supporting some reforms, they later adopted a more conservative stance, often siding with orthodox elements to maintain social order and prevent widespread unrest that might challenge their rule.

Statement 3 is correct.  The British revenue policies, particularly the Permanent Settlement, Ryotwari System, and Mahalwari System, had a significant negative impact on many Indian farmers.  High revenue demands, coupled with inefficient systems of collection and a lack of consideration for the welfare of cultivators, led to widespread rural poverty and indebtedness.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple choice questions based on the provided text, adhering to all specified criteria.  Each question includes the correct answer and a detailed explanation.


**1. With reference to the 1857 Revolt, consider the following statements:**

1.  The immediate cause of the 1857 Revolt was the introduction of the Enfield rifle with greased cartridges, believed to be greased with beef and pork fat, offending both Hindu and Muslim religious sensibilities.
2.  The revolt was entirely spontaneous and lacked any pre-planning or organized conspiracy, erupting solely due to the greased cartridge incident.
3.  While Bahadur Shah Zafar served as a symbolic figurehead, the actual leadership of the revolt in Delhi was primarily in the hands of General Bakht Khan.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 3 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The greased cartridges were indeed the immediate trigger, igniting pre-existing discontent among sepoys and the broader population.  The perceived sacrilege of the cartridges, combined with existing grievances against British rule, led to widespread rebellion.

Statement 2 is incorrect. The passage explicitly discusses the debate among historians regarding the organization of the revolt. While the extent of pre-planning is debated, the text suggests the existence of some level of organized conspiracy, evidenced by the circulation of chappatis and red lotuses, and the alleged coordination among regiments.  It was not entirely spontaneous.

Statement 3 is correct. The passage clearly states that Bahadur Shah Zafar, though proclaimed Emperor, was a weak link in the leadership chain. The real military command in Delhi rested with General Bakht Khan, who brought the Bareilly troops to Delhi and represented a more popular, plebian element within the revolt's leadership.  This highlights the complex layers of leadership within the rebellion, moving beyond the symbolic figurehead of the Mughal emperor.  The other leaders like Nana Saheb in Kanpur, the Begum of Avadh in Lucknow, and Rani Lakshmibai in Jhansi further demonstrate the decentralized nature of the rebellion.


**2. With reference to the leaders of the 1857 Revolt, consider the following statements:**

1.  Nana Sahib, adopted son of the last Peshwa, led the revolt in Lucknow, and his primary military strategist was Tantia Tope.
2.  Rani Lakshmibai of Jhansi joined the revolt primarily due to the British annexation of her state and refusal to acknowledge her adopted heir.
3.  Kunwar Singh, despite his advanced age, was a significant military leader in Bihar, later collaborating with Nana Sahib's forces.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 2 and 3 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. Nana Sahib led the revolt in Kanpur, not Lucknow. Lucknow's revolt was led by the Begum of Avadh.  Tantia Tope was indeed a key military figure for Nana Sahib, known for his guerrilla warfare tactics.

Statement 2 is correct. The passage explicitly mentions Rani Lakshmibais motivations for joining the revolt:  the British annexation of Jhansi and their refusal to recognize her adopted son as heir.

Statement 3 is correct. Kunwar Singh, despite his age (nearly 80), is described as an outstanding military leader and strategist, initially active in Bihar and later collaborating with Nana Sahib's forces in Avadh and Central India. His actions demonstrate the broad-based nature of the 1857 revolt, involving diverse regional leaders and not just sepoys.


**3. With reference to the impact and aftermath of the 1857 Revolt, consider the following statements:**

1.  The revolt's success was significantly hampered by the lack of participation from most Indian rulers and large zamindars, who remained loyal to the British.
2.  The British response to the revolt involved widespread brutality, including the burning of villages and mass killings of civilians, reflecting the depth of the rebellion.
3.  The revolt's failure resulted in the immediate and complete eradication of Hindu-Muslim unity in India, paving the way for communal tensions that would dominate later decades.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 2 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The passage highlights the crucial role of the lack of support from many Indian rulers and prominent zamindars in the revolts failure. Their loyalty to the British acted as a significant impediment to the rebellion's success. This underscores the complex political landscape of the time and the limitations of the revolt's leadership in securing widespread support.

Statement 2 is correct.  The British response is described as vigorous and ruthless, involving widespread violence against both sepoys and civilians. The description of the British actions emphasizes the scale of the revolt and the determination of the British to quell it.  This points to the deep-seated nature of the rebellion that necessitated such a harsh response.

Statement 3 is incorrect.  The passage explicitly notes the significant Hindu-Muslim unity during the revolt, highlighting the cooperation between the two communities among soldiers, leaders, and the population. While communal tensions would later emerge, the revolt itself was not the immediate cause of their eradication; rather, it showcased a period of considerable inter-religious cooperation against British rule.  This is a crucial point for understanding the complexities of Indian history and the development of communalism.


**4.  With reference to the post-1857 reorganization of the British Indian Army, consider the following statements:**

1. The British significantly increased recruitment from the Brahmin communities of Uttar Pradesh and Bihar to replace the mutinous sepoys.
2.  The Peel Commission was established to investigate the causes of the 1857 Revolt and recommend army reforms.
3. The British significantly altered their recruitment strategy, favoring Gurkhas, Sikhs, and Punjabis from the North to reduce the risk of future mutinies.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 3 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1 only
(d) 2 and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. The text explicitly states that the British recruited Gurkhas, Sikhs, and Punjabis from the North, not Brahmins from Uttar Pradesh and Bihar. This reflects a deliberate strategy to diversify recruitment and minimize the risk of future mutinies based on religious or regional sentiments.

Statement 2 is incorrect. The passage does not mention the Peel Commission.  It does, however, mention a commission associated with army reorganization after the revolt, but this is not explicitly named as the Peel Commission.

Statement 3 is correct.  The British decisively shifted their recruitment policies after the 1857 Revolt, prioritizing Gurkhas, Sikhs, and Punjabis from the North. This was a direct response to the mutiny, aiming to create a more loyal and less susceptible army.  This change in recruitment strategy is a key element in understanding the British response to the 1857 revolt and their subsequent efforts to consolidate their control over India.  The shift away from the sepoy regiments, which had been the backbone of the Company's army, is a crucial part of this reorganization.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided text, adhering to all specified criteria.  Each question includes the correct answer and a detailed explanation.


**1. With reference to the Indian Nationalist Movement (1905-1918), consider the following statements:**

1.  The deportation of Lala Lajpat Rai and Ajit Singh in 1907 followed riots in the canal colonies of Bengal.
2.  The Swadeshi and Boycott movement primarily focused on economic self-reliance and rejecting foreign goods.
3.  Aurobindo Ghose advocated for "passive resistance" as the sole method to achieve political freedom.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) 2 and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect.  Lala Lajpat Rai and Ajit Singh were deported following riots in the canal colonies of the *Punjab*, not Bengal, in 1907.  The text clearly specifies the Punjab as the location of the unrest.

Statement 2 is correct. The Swadeshi and Boycott movement, a crucial part of the early 20th-century Indian nationalist movement, aimed to promote Indian-made goods and boycott British products, fostering economic self-sufficiency and challenging British economic dominance.  This was a key strategy to weaken British control.

Statement 3 is incorrect. While Aurobindo Ghose was a prominent figure in the militant nationalist movement and advocated for a form of non-cooperation that would make British administration difficult, he didn't limit the methods to just "passive resistance."  The movement encompassed various strategies including Swadeshi, Boycott, and ultimately, in some factions, revolutionary terrorism.  The text highlights the diverse approaches within the movement.


**2. With reference to the impact of the Partition of Bengal on the Indian National Congress, consider the following statements:**

1. The 1905 Congress session, presided over by Dadabhai Naoroji, openly declared the goal of the Indian national movement as "self-government" or Swaraj.
2. The Surat split of the Indian National Congress in 1907 stemmed from disagreements over the strategy of participating in elections to legislative councils.
3.  The Morley-Minto Reforms of 1909, introduced to appease moderate nationalists, significantly increased the number of directly elected members in the Imperial Legislative Council.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) 2 and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect.  While Dadabhai Naoroji did declare the goal of Swaraj in his presidential address, this was at the 1906 Calcutta session, not the 1905 session. The 1905 session was presided over by Gopal Krishna Gokhale who condemned the Partition.

Statement 2 is correct. The Surat split in 1907 was a major division within the Congress, primarily caused by the fundamental differences in strategies between the Moderates and Extremists. The Extremists, including Tilak, advocated for more assertive and radical methods, while the Moderates favored working within the existing constitutional framework.  Council entry was a key point of contention.

Statement 3 is incorrect. The Morley-Minto Reforms did increase the number of elected members, but most were elected indirectly, through provincial councils or other bodies. The reforms also included provisions reserving seats for specific groups, including landlords and British capitalists, limiting the extent of direct representation.


**3. With reference to the Khilafat and Non-Cooperation Movement (1919-1922), consider the following statements:**

1.  The Rowlatt Act's passage directly triggered the Khilafat Movement.
2.  The Chauri Chaura incident, involving violence against police, led to the immediate suspension of the Non-Cooperation Movement by Gandhi.
3.  The Treaty of Sevres, signed in May 1920, significantly improved the conditions for the Ottoman Empire, thus diminishing the impetus for the Khilafat Movement.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. While the Rowlatt Act and the Jallianwala Bagh massacre fueled widespread discontent and contributed to the overall atmosphere of unrest, the Khilafat Movement's primary catalyst was the post-World War I treatment of the Ottoman Empire by the Allied powers, specifically the threat to the Caliphate.  The Rowlatt Act agitation did, however, create a climate of Hindu-Muslim unity, which was instrumental to the Khilafat movement's success.

Statement 2 is correct. The Chauri Chaura incident, where protestors set fire to a police station, resulting in the deaths of policemen, prompted Gandhi to call off the Non-Cooperation Movement due to his commitment to non-violence. This demonstrates his commitment to non-violent methods and his belief that violence would undermine the movement's effectiveness and legitimacy.

Statement 3 is incorrect. The Treaty of Sevres, far from improving conditions for the Ottoman Empire, severely curtailed its territories and power, directly fueling the Khilafat Movement's anger and demands. The treaty's harsh terms intensified Muslim resentment towards British policy and contributed to the widespread support for the movement.


**4.  With reference to the Swarajist movement, consider the following statements:**

1.  The Swarajist party was formed solely by C.R. Das and Motilal Nehru in December 1922.
2. The "No-Changers" within the Congress advocated for continued boycott of Legislative Councils, emphasizing constructive work instead of council politics.
3.  The Swarajists' participation in council elections was universally supported by all factions within the Congress.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. While C.R. Das and Motilal Nehru were the key figures in the formation of the Swarajist party, it was not formed solely by these two.  Other prominent leaders were involved in its creation and operations.

Statement 2 is correct. The "No-Changers" within the Congress opposed the Swarajists' strategy of entering legislative councils, arguing that it would divert attention from constructive work like promoting Khadi and Hindu-Muslim unity.  They believed that focusing on mass mobilization and non-cooperation was more effective.

Statement 3 is incorrect. The Swarajists participation in council elections caused a significant split within the Congress.  The "No-Changers" strongly opposed this strategy, leading to internal conflict and division within the nationalist movement. The text explicitly mentions the disagreements between the two groups.


**5. With reference to the Second Non-Cooperation Movement and the rise of socialist ideas, consider the following statements:**

1.  Jawaharlal Nehru and Subhas Chandra Bose were initially staunch supporters of Gandhian methods and opposed socialist ideology.
2. The Bardoli Satyagraha, led by Sardar Vallabhbhai Patel, was a major peasant movement focused on protesting against increased land revenue in Uttar Pradesh.
3.  The Kanpur Conspiracy Case primarily involved the prosecution of individuals accused of spreading socialist and communist ideas.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 3 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) 2 and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. While initially influenced by Gandhi, Jawaharlal Nehru and Subhas Chandra Bose later embraced socialist ideals and advocated for more radical approaches to achieving independence, moving away from purely Gandhian methods.  Their advocacy for socialism is clearly mentioned in the text.

Statement 2 is incorrect. While the Bardoli Satyagraha was indeed a significant peasant movement led by Sardar Vallabhbhai Patel, it took place in *Gujarat*, not Uttar Pradesh, and focused on protesting against increased land revenue in that region.


Statement 3 is correct. The Kanpur Conspiracy Case was a major trial during the 1920s where several individuals were prosecuted for spreading communist ideologies in India. The case highlights the British government's response to the growing influence of communist and socialist ideas within the nationalist movement.

**1. With reference to the socio-religious reform movements in 19th century India, consider the following statements:**

1. The Prarthana Samaj, founded in Bombay, primarily focused on religious reform, advocating monotheism as its central tenet.
2. The Satyashodhak Samaj, established in Maharashtra, aimed at social transformation by challenging the caste system and promoting education among marginalized communities.
3. The Arya Samaj, founded in Bombay, emphasized a return to Vedic principles, advocating for social reforms like widow remarriage and opposing idolatry.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
