(d) 2 only


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect because while the Prarthana Samaj did advocate monotheism, its focus was broader, encompassing significant social reform initiatives like women's education and widow remarriage.  It was deeply intertwined with the Bhakti movement of Maharashtra and used persuasion rather than confrontation.  Its primary concern was the upliftment of society through social reform, not solely religious reform.

Statement 2 is correct.  The Satyashodhak Samaj, founded by Jyotirao Phule, directly challenged the caste system and aimed for a more equitable society.  Education for women and lower castes was a central pillar of its ideology, advocating for social transformation beyond mere reform.

Statement 3 is partially correct. The Arya Samaj, founded by Dayananda Saraswati, did stress a return to Vedic principles and championed social reforms such as widow remarriage.  However, its crucial to note that its Bombay founding is debatable, with Lahore generally considered its headquarters.  It also actively opposed idolatry and polytheism, a significant religious reform aspect. Therefore, the statement is partially correct in its description of the Arya Samaj's goals but slightly inaccurate regarding its founding location.

Therefore, only statements 2 and 3 are largely accurate, making option (b) the correct answer.  The nuanced inaccuracies in statement 3 and the oversimplification of statement 1 highlight the need for precise understanding of these complex historical movements.




**2. With reference to the 19th-century social reform movements in India, consider the following statements:**

1. The Brahmo Samaj, initially established in Bengal, significantly influenced social reform movements in Maharashtra, notably the Prarthana Samaj.
2.  The Faraizi movement, primarily active in East Bengal, focused on the purification of Islamic practices and challenged the authority of Hindu Zamindars.
3. The Singh Sabha movement, originating in Punjab, aimed to reform Sikh religious practices and promote modern Western education among Sikhs.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The Brahmo Samaj's monotheistic ideals and emphasis on social reform had a demonstrable influence on the Prarthana Samaj in Maharashtra, showcasing the spread of reformist ideas across regional boundaries.  The Brahmo Samaj's emphasis on reason and rejection of idolatry resonated with similar reformist movements elsewhere in India.

Statement 2 is correct. The Faraizi movement, while focused on purifying Islamic practices, also directly challenged the authority of Zamindars, many of whom were Hindu. This highlights the inter-religious and socio-economic dimensions of the movement.  The movement's anti-landlord stance had significant social and economic implications.

Statement 3 is correct. The Singh Sabha movement's dual focus on religious reform within Sikhism and the promotion of modern Western education demonstrates its multifaceted approach to societal advancement.  The movement's success in establishing Khalsa schools underscores its commitment to education.

All three statements accurately reflect the core aims and influences of these distinct yet interconnected social reform movements.  Option (d) is thus the correct answer.  The diverse nature of the movements and their regional variations demonstrate the complex interplay of religious, social, and political factors shaping 19th-century India.



**3. With reference to the social and religious reform movements in British India, consider the following statements:**

1. The Dev Samaj, founded by Shiv Narayan Agnihotri, was a direct offshoot of the Arya Samaj, sharing its emphasis on Vedic principles and social reform.
2. The Aligarh Movement, spearheaded by Sir Syed Ahmed Khan, primarily focused on modernizing Muslim education and promoting loyalty to the British Raj.
3. The Self-Respect Movement, initiated by E.V. Ramaswamy Naicker, advocated for the rejection of Brahminical Hinduism and challenged traditional caste hierarchies.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 2 only


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. While Shiv Narayan Agnihotri was initially a follower of the Brahmo Samaj, the Dev Samaj, which he founded, had its own distinct tenets, although it shared some similarities with other reformist movements in its emphasis on social reform and rejection of certain orthodox practices. It did not directly stem from the Arya Samaj.

Statement 2 is largely correct. The Aligarh Movement, led by Sir Syed Ahmed Khan, prioritized the modernization of Muslim education through the establishment of the Mohammedan Anglo-Oriental College (later Aligarh Muslim University).  While it aimed for the upliftment of Muslims, its emphasis on loyalty to the British Raj is a significant aspect, often criticized for its potential contribution to the British policy of "divide and rule."

Statement 3 is correct.  E.V. Ramaswamy Naicker's Self-Respect Movement explicitly rejected Brahminical dominance and challenged the deeply entrenched caste system within Hinduism.  It aimed at social justice and self-respect for marginalized communities, advocating for social equality and challenging traditional religious practices.

Therefore, statements 2 and 3 accurately describe the primary goals and impact of the Aligarh and Self-Respect movements, making (b) the correct option. The incorrectness of statement 1, along with the nuanced complexities of statement 2 (the potential for misinterpreting the Aligarh movement's pro-British stance), creates a challenging question requiring accurate historical knowledge.


**4. With reference to the impact of Western education on Indian society in the 19th century, consider the following statements:**

1. The Young Bengal movement, inspired by Henry Vivian Derozio, promoted radical ideas like questioning authority and advocating for social equality, but lacked widespread mass appeal.
2. The introduction of Western education led to the immediate and widespread adoption of radical social reforms across all sections of Indian society, effectively dismantling traditional hierarchies.
3. The Brahmo Samaj and Arya Samaj, while advocating for social reform, demonstrated the capacity of Indian intellectuals to reconcile modern ideas with traditional religious beliefs.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 3 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The Young Bengal movement, under Derozio's influence, did indeed promote radical ideas and challenged traditional norms. However, its impact remained largely confined to the educated elite in Bengal. The movement's lack of significant outreach to the broader masses limited its transformative effect on the society at large.

Statement 2 is incorrect. The introduction of Western education did not lead to the immediate and widespread dismantling of traditional social hierarchies. While it fostered new ideas and spurred reform movements, the process of social change was gradual, complex, and faced considerable resistance from conservative elements in society.  The impact varied significantly across different regions and communities.

Statement 3 is correct. The Brahmo Samaj and Arya Samaj successfully demonstrated the possibility of integrating modern Western concepts of social reform with traditional religious beliefs and practices.  They showcased the capacity of Indian intellectuals to engage critically with both Western and Indian thought, leading to reformist movements that aimed to modernise Indian society within its existing cultural context.

Therefore, only statements 1 and 3 are accurate representations of the effects of Western education on Indian society during the 19th century, making (a) the correct answer.  The stark contrast between the partially true statement 1 and completely false statement 2, along with the more nuanced accuracy of statement 3, increases the question's difficulty and tests the candidate's detailed knowledge of the period.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple choice questions based on the provided target content, adhering to all specified criteria.  Each question includes the correct answer and a detailed explanation.

**1. With reference to 19th-century socio-religious reform movements in India, consider the following statements:**

1. The Arya Samaj, founded in Bombay, primarily focused on Vedic interpretations and challenged the caste system.
2. The Brahmo Samaj, originating in Bengal, advocated for widow remarriage and vehemently opposed idolatry, while considering Vedic scriptures infallible.
3. The Theosophical Society, initially established outside India, promoted the revival of ancient religions and the doctrine of transmigration of souls, while remaining silent on universal brotherhood.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is largely correct. The Arya Samaj, founded by Dayananda Saraswati in Bombay (not Lahore, which was its later headquarters), emphasized a return to Vedic principles and actively challenged the rigidities of the caste system.  It promoted social reform through a reinterpretation of Hindu scriptures.

Statement 2 is incorrect on multiple counts.  While the Brahmo Samaj, founded by Raja Ram Mohan Roy in Bengal, did advocate for widow remarriage and opposed idolatry, it did *not* consider Vedic scriptures infallible.  In fact, it critically examined and reinterpreted religious texts, rejecting many traditional practices.

Statement 3 is partially incorrect.  The Theosophical Society, founded by Helena Blavatsky, was indeed established outside India and promoted the revival of ancient religions and the doctrine of transmigration of souls. However, it explicitly advocated for universal brotherhood, a core tenet of its philosophy, and did not remain silent on this aspect.


**2. With reference to the 1857 Revolt, consider the following statements:**

1. The annexation of Awadh by Lord Dalhousie directly contributed to the discontent among sepoys, many of whom originated from that region, leading to their participation in the revolt.
2. The Revolt of 1857 was solely a product of sepoy discontent over the greased cartridges of the Enfield rifle, with minimal participation from other social groups.
3. The economic exploitation of India by the British, including the destruction of traditional economic structures and land revenue policies, played a significant role in fueling the widespread rebellion.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 3 only
(b) 3 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3
(d) 2 only


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 accurately reflects a key factor contributing to the 1857 Revolt. The annexation of Awadh, a region from which many sepoys hailed, created intense resentment and a sense of betrayal, significantly impacting their loyalty to the British East India Company. This regional grievance became a catalyst for their participation in the rebellion.

Statement 2 is fundamentally incorrect. While the greased cartridges were a triggering incident, the 1857 Revolt was a far more complex event rooted in deep-seated grievances across various social strata. Peasants, artisans, landowners, and princes all participated, driven by economic exploitation, administrative injustices, and the overall resentment towards British rule.  It was a multi-faceted rebellion, not merely a sepoy mutiny.

Statement 3 correctly identifies a crucial underlying cause. The British economic policies, including land revenue systems that dispossessed many peasants and the destruction of traditional industries, created widespread poverty and resentment, significantly contributing to the widespread participation in the revolt.  The economic hardship fueled the flames of rebellion.


**3. With reference to the social reform movements in 19th-century India, consider the following statements:**

1.  Jotiba Phule's contributions primarily focused on women's education and widow remarriage in Maharashtra, while ignoring the plight of untouchables.
2.  Gopal Hari Deshmukh (Lokahitawadi) advocated for social reorganization based on rational principles and secular values, but neglected the issue of caste discrimination.
3.  Dadabhai Naoroji, a prominent social reformer from Bombay, focused primarily on reforming the Zoroastrian religion and Parsi Law, while largely ignoring broader social issues.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) None
(b) 1 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 2 only


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. Jotiba Phule was a staunch advocate for the upliftment of both women and the untouchables in Maharashtra. His work encompassed both women's education and challenging the caste system's discriminatory practices.

Statement 2 is incorrect.  Gopal Hari Deshmukh (Lokahitawadi) was a comprehensive social reformer. His advocacy for rational principles and secular values explicitly included a critique of the caste system and its inherent inequalities. He actively worked towards social justice for all.

Statement 3 is incorrect. Dadabhai Naoroji's social reform efforts extended beyond religious reform within the Parsi community. He was involved in broader social reform movements, advocating for women's rights and other progressive causes. His commitment to social justice encompassed a wider spectrum of concerns than just Zoroastrian reform.  His work on economic exploitation was also widely recognized.


**4. Consider the following statements regarding the impact of British rule on Indian education:**

1. The Charter Act of 1813 allocated funds specifically for the promotion of Western science and technology in India, leading to a rapid expansion of modern educational institutions.
2. The "downward filtration theory," which aimed to educate the upper classes who would then disseminate knowledge to the masses, was a complete success in bridging the educational gap in India.
3.  Lord Macaulay's Minute of 1835 prioritized Western knowledge through the English medium, neglecting vernacular languages and mass education, creating a significant educational divide.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 3 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3
(d) 1 only


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. While the Charter Act of 1813 did allocate funds for education, the implementation was slow and controversial. The expansion of modern educational institutions was gradual and not a direct result of this act alone.

Statement 2 is incorrect.  The "downward filtration theory" was a flawed approach and ultimately failed to bridge the educational gap.  It did not effectively disseminate knowledge to the masses, perpetuating educational inequalities.

Statement 3 accurately describes the consequences of Lord Macaulay's Minute.  The emphasis on Western knowledge through English created an educational divide, neglecting vernacular languages and mass education, and ultimately serving colonial interests.  This policy profoundly shaped the Indian education system for decades to come.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided target content, adhering to all specified criteria.  Each question is followed by the correct answer and a detailed explanation.

**1. With reference to the socio-religious movements in British India, consider the following statements:**

1.  The Arya Samaj, initially headquartered in Bombay, later shifted its main base to Lahore.
2.  The Brahmo Samaj, while advocating for widow remarriage, explicitly rejected the infallibility of the Vedas.
3.  The Satyashodhak Samaj, founded by Jyotirao Phule in 1873, primarily focused on uplifting the Kunbi peasantry and promoting Maratha identity.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is partially incorrect. While the Arya Samaj was founded in Bombay, its *main* center of activity and influence shifted to Lahore.  The initial location is often overlooked, making this a good distractor. Statement 2 is correct. The Brahmo Samaj, a reformist movement within Hinduism, advocated for social reforms like widow remarriage and actively challenged traditional interpretations of the Vedas, rejecting their absolute infallibility.  This contrasts with the Arya Samaj's reverence for the Vedas. Statement 3 is largely correct.  The Satyashodhak Samaj, founded in 1873, did focus on the Kunbi peasantry, a significant social group in Maharashtra. However, while Phule's work touched upon Maratha identity, it wasn't the *primary* focus of the Satyashodhak Samaj.  The emphasis on the Kunbi peasantry and the nuanced relationship with Maratha identity make this a challenging statement to evaluate. Therefore, only statements 2 and 3 are entirely accurate.


**2. With reference to the Indian freedom struggle, consider the following statements:**

1.  The All India Khilafat Conference, held in Delhi in 1919, demanded the annulment of the Rowlatt Act as a precondition for cooperation with the British government.
2.  The Non-Cooperation Movement, launched in 1920, witnessed the establishment of national educational institutions like Jamia Millia Islamia and Kashi Vidyapith.
3.  The Nehru Report, drafted in 1928, proposed Dominion Status as the immediate political goal, while advocating for joint electorates with reserved seats for minorities for a decade.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. The All India Khilafat Conference in 1919 *did* advocate for the withdrawal of cooperation if their demands regarding the Ottoman Empire were not met, but this was not directly linked to the Rowlatt Act.  The Rowlatt Act was a separate issue that fueled the broader Non-Cooperation Movement.  This subtle difference makes it a strong distractor. Statement 2 is correct. The Non-Cooperation Movement saw the rise of national educational institutions as a direct response to the boycott of government-run schools and colleges. Statement 3 is correct. The Nehru Report, while proposing Dominion Status, also addressed the crucial issue of representation, suggesting joint electorates with temporary reservations for religious minorities. This demonstrates the complex political negotiations of the time. Thus, only statements 2 and 3 are accurate.


**3. With reference to the activities of the Awadh Kisan Sabha, consider the following statements:**

1.  The Awadh Kisan Sabha primarily focused on organizing industrial workers in the textile mills of Awadh.
2.  The Awadh Kisan Sabha's protests included urging peasants to refuse to cultivate 'Bedakhli' land and to resist forced labor ('hari' and 'begar').
3.  The Awadh Kisan Sabha actively collaborated with the British administration to implement land reforms in Awadh.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 2 and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. The Awadh Kisan Sabha was primarily a peasant organization, not focused on industrial workers. This is a significant factual difference, making it a good distractor. Statement 2 is correct. The Awadh Kisan Sabha played a crucial role in mobilizing peasants against unjust land practices and forced labor, urging them to resist cultivating 'Bedakhli' (illegally occupied) lands and to refuse 'hari' and 'begar'. Statement 3 is incorrect. The Awadh Kisan Sabha was actively involved in protests against the British administration, not in collaboration with it.  The contrast between active opposition and collaboration makes this a clear-cut distractor.  Therefore, only statement 2 accurately describes the Awadh Kisan Sabha's activities.


**4. With reference to the Shiromani Gurudwara Prabandhak Committee (SGPC), consider the following statements:**

1. The SGPC was formed in the late 19th century as a political offshoot of the Singh Sabhas.
2. The SGPC's primary objective was to secure control of Sikh shrines from government-controlled committees.
3. The Akali Dal emerged as a direct consequence of the SGPC's establishment, initially serving as its political arm.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 2 and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. The SGPC was formed in 1920, not in the late 19th century, as part of the Akali movement.  The difference in the timeframe is a key distractor. Statement 2 is correct. The SGPC's formation was a direct response to the need to wrest control of Sikh gurudwaras from committees seen as manipulated by the British government. Statement 3 is incorrect. While the SGPC did play a role in the Akali Dal's development, the Akali Dal wasn't initially its political arm; it evolved separately to coordinate the groups (Jathas) fighting for control of the shrines.  The nuanced relationship between the SGPC and the Akali Dal makes this a sophisticated distractor.  Therefore, only statement 2 is entirely correct.


**5.  With reference to the revolutionary movements in India, consider the following statements:**

1. The Hindustan Republican Association, later renamed the Hindustan Socialist Republican Association, was primarily active in Bengal.
2. Bhagat Singh and his associates threw a bomb in the Central Legislative Assembly in 1929 as a purely symbolic act, aiming to draw attention to their grievances rather than cause harm.
3. The Kakori Conspiracy case of 1925 resulted in the execution of all the accused, including Ramprasad Bismil and Ashfaqulla Khan.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) 2 and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. While the Hindustan Republican Association/Hindustan Socialist Republican Association had members across India, its core activities were concentrated in Uttar Pradesh and Punjab, not primarily in Bengal. This geographical inaccuracy serves as a strong distractor. Statement 2 is largely correct. The bomb thrown in the Central Legislative Assembly was intended to be a symbolic protest, designed to capture attention, not to inflict casualties.  The emphasis on the symbolic nature is a crucial point. Statement 3 is incorrect. While Ramprasad Bismil and Ashfaqulla Khan were executed, not *all* the accused in the Kakori Conspiracy case faced capital punishment; some received life imprisonment.  The detail about the number of executions versus life sentences forms a powerful distractor.  Therefore, only statement 2 is completely accurate.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple choice questions based on the provided target content, adhering to all specified criteria.  Each question is designed to be challenging and test a range of cognitive skills, primarily factual recall with elements of analysis and evaluation.


**1. With reference to the British presence in India, consider the following statements:**

1. Henry Lawrence's role as British Resident in Lucknow was preceded by his appointment through the Treaty of Bhairowal.
2. The English East India Company's expansion in India involved establishing factories in both Patna and Dacca.
3.  The English East India Company's initial trade interests in Bengal were later superseded by its pursuit of political dominance.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect.  While Henry Lawrence was involved with the Treaty of Bhairowal (as presiding officer of the regency council), his appointment as British Resident in Lucknow stemmed from the Treaty of Lahore.  The Treaty of Bhairowal dealt with the Sikh succession and did not directly lead to his Lucknow posting.

Statement 2 is correct. The English East India Company did establish factories in both Patna and Dacca as part of its expansion strategy in India. These were crucial trading posts.

Statement 3 is correct. The English East India Company began with primarily trade-focused objectives in Bengal, but its actions gradually shifted towards political control and the establishment of an empire, culminating in its dominance over large parts of India.  The commercial activities were a stepping stone to political power. The initial focus on trade morphed into a quest for power.


**2. With reference to the administration of Bengal, consider the following statements:**

1. The Permanent Settlement, implemented by the British, had a uniform impact across all regions of Bengal, leading to consistent socio-economic outcomes.
2.  The Sanyasi Revolt, a significant rebellion, unfolded entirely within the geographical boundaries of Bengal, without impacting neighboring regions.
3. The English East India Company's monopoly over Bengal's trade significantly contributed to its economic development, creating widespread prosperity.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 3 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. The Permanent Settlement's impact on Bengal was far from uniform.  Its effects varied significantly across different regions and social groups, leading to diverse socio-economic consequences.  It had uneven impact.

Statement 2 is incorrect. The Sanyasi Revolt, while originating in Bengal, spilled over into neighboring regions like Bihar, impacting a wider area than just Bengal. The rebellion was not confined to Bengal.

Statement 3 is incorrect. While the English East India Company's control over Bengal's trade boosted its own economic power, it did not automatically translate to widespread prosperity for Bengal. In fact, it led to exploitation and economic hardship for many.  The Company's actions primarily benefited its own interests.


**3. With reference to the early years of the English East India Company's operations, consider the following statements:**

1. The Company's establishment of factories in Surat and Bombay was facilitated by direct grants of land from the Mughal emperor, Jahangir.
2.  William Hawkins's role as a representative of the English East India Company was primarily focused on establishing trade relationships, not territorial control.
3.  The Company's early competition with Portuguese and Dutch entities involved primarily military conflicts, rather than economic rivalry.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 3 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. While Jahangir did grant permission for the Company's operations, the initial establishment of factories in Surat and Bombay involved a complex interplay of negotiations and permissions, not direct land grants from the Mughal Emperor.  The process was more nuanced than a simple grant.

Statement 2 is correct. William Hawkins's primary mission was to establish trade relations with the Mughal Empire.  Territorial ambitions were not the initial focus of the company.

Statement 3 is incorrect. While military clashes did occur, the early competition with the Portuguese and Dutch primarily centered on economic rivalry for control of trade routes and markets in India. Military conflicts were a consequence, not the primary driver, of the competition.


**4.  With reference to Warren Hastings's governorship of Bengal, consider the following statements:**

1. Hastings's "ring-fence policy" aimed to limit the territorial expansion of the English East India Company, focusing instead on consolidating existing power.
2. The Izaredari system, implemented under Hastings, was a completely novel land revenue system, unrelated to any pre-existing practices.
3. Hastings's conflict with the Marathas was primarily driven by territorial disputes, rather than economic competition for resources.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 1 and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. Hastings's ring-fence policy aimed to consolidate the Company's power in Bengal and avoid further costly territorial expansion. This aimed at stabilizing the situation and avoiding costly conflicts.

Statement 2 is incorrect. The Izaredari system, while modified and adapted by Hastings, was not entirely novel. It built upon existing practices of revenue collection. It was a modified version of pre-existing systems.

Statement 3 is incorrect.  While territorial disputes were a factor, Hastings's conflicts with the Marathas were also significantly influenced by economic factors, particularly the competition for resources and control of trade routes. Economic aspects were equally important.


**5. With reference to the annexation of Awadh, consider the following statements:**

1. The annexation of Awadh by Lord Dalhousie directly resulted in improved financial conditions for the sepoys of the British East India Company.
2. The Doctrine of Lapse, a key policy under Lord Dalhousie, played a significant role in the events leading to the annexation of Awadh.
3.  The annexation of Awadh was met with widespread support from the Awadh population, who saw it as a positive change in governance.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 2 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. The annexation of Awadh, rather than improving the sepoys' financial conditions, significantly contributed to their discontent, as it disrupted the existing system and created uncertainty. The annexation actually worsened their situation.

Statement 2 is correct. Though not directly applied, the Doctrine of Lapse, which provided a pretext for annexing territories with no clear heir, formed the basis of the accusations used to justify the annexation of Awadh.  It was the justification, not the direct cause.

Statement 3 is incorrect. The annexation of Awadh was widely opposed by the Awadh population, who viewed it as a violation of their autonomy and traditional governance. There was significant resistance to the annexation.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple choice questions based on the provided text, adhering to all specified criteria.  The questions are designed to be challenging and test a deep understanding of the subject matter, going beyond simple factual recall.


**1. With reference to Lord Dalhousie's administration in India, consider the following statements:**

1. The annexation of Awadh in 1856 was primarily driven by concerns about the Nawab's misgovernance and the need for administrative reforms, as publicly stated by Dalhousie.
2. The Doctrine of Lapse, a key instrument of Dalhousie's annexation policy, was applied consistently across all princely states regardless of the presence of adopted heirs.
3. Dalhousie's policies significantly impacted the economic conditions of sepoys, although not solely through increased land taxes in Awadh.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 3 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is partially correct. While Dalhousie did cite misgovernance as a reason for annexing Awadh, the underlying motive was significantly driven by the expansion of British economic interests and the desire to eliminate potential rivals. The stated justification served as a convenient pretext.

Statement 2 is incorrect. The Doctrine of Lapse was selectively applied.  While it led to the annexation of several states, it wasn't universally enforced; the presence of adopted heirs sometimes did not automatically lead to annexation if the British found it politically inexpedient.

Statement 3 is correct. Dalhousie's annexation policies, including the Doctrine of Lapse, had significant repercussions for sepoys, impacting their economic stability and livelihoods.  While increased land taxes in Awadh were a factor, the broader economic consequences arising from the disruption of established power structures and the displacement of populations played a much larger role.  The annexation of territories where sepoys' families resided directly affected their financial security.


**2. With reference to the economic policies of the British in 19th-century India, consider the following statements:**

1. The Permanent Settlement, introduced by Lord Cornwallis, aimed to improve land productivity by granting proprietary rights to zamindars, mirroring the English landlord system.
2. The Ryotwari system, primarily implemented in Madras and Bombay Presidencies, resulted in consistently higher revenue collection for the British compared to other systems due to its direct assessment of individual cultivators.
3.  The Mahalwari system, implemented across a large portion of northern India, led to the consistent enrichment of village communities due to its collective assessment approach.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is largely correct. Lord Cornwallis's intention behind the Permanent Settlement was to establish a stable system of revenue collection by granting proprietary rights to zamindars.  However, the intended parallel to the English landlord system was not fully realized, as the system's flaws led to unintended consequences such as absentee landlordism and the exploitation of ryots.

Statement 2 is incorrect. While the Ryotwari system aimed for direct revenue collection, it did not consistently yield higher revenue than other systems.  Over-assessment, coupled with the vulnerability of ryots to economic shocks, often resulted in revenue shortfalls.

Statement 3 is incorrect. The Mahalwari system, while aiming for a more community-based approach, did not consistently lead to the enrichment of village communities.  High revenue demands, coupled with administrative inefficiencies, often led to the impoverishment of villagers and their displacement.


**3.  With reference to the social and cultural policies of the British in India, consider the following statements:**

1. The British consistently supported social reforms in India, even when facing opposition from orthodox sections, demonstrating a commitment to improving the lives of Indians.
2. Post-1857, the British significantly curtailed their support for social reforms, aligning themselves with conservative elements to maintain social stability and control.
3. The Christian missionary activities in India were entirely independent of British administrative policies and had no impact on the social and cultural landscape.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. While the British supported certain social reforms earlier, their support was not consistent.  Their actions often reflected a pragmatic approach, balancing their commitment to reform with the need to maintain political stability and control.  They often retreated from supporting reforms when it caused social unrest.

Statement 2 is correct. Post-1857, the British shifted their stance, increasingly aligning with conservative social elements. This was a strategic move to consolidate their power and control, seeing social reform as potentially destabilizing.

Statement 3 is incorrect. Christian missionary activities were intertwined with British administrative policies. Missionaries played a role in advocating for certain social changes, sometimes aligning with the British administrations interests, and sometimes acting independently. Their activities significantly influenced the social and cultural transformation of India.


**4. With reference to the British annexation policy under Lord Dalhousie, consider the following statements:**

1. The annexation of Satara in 1848 was solely based on the application of the Doctrine of Lapse due to the absence of a natural heir to the throne.
2.  The annexation of Nagpur and Jhansi in 1854 was a direct consequence of the application of the Doctrine of Lapse.
3. Lord Dalhousie's annexation policy was primarily motivated by a genuine concern for the welfare and good governance of the annexed territories.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 3 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. While the absence of a natural heir was cited, other political considerations likely influenced the annexation of Satara. The Doctrine of Lapse provided a convenient justification for a pre-existing imperial ambition.

Statement 2 is correct. The annexations of Nagpur and Jhansi were directly attributed to the application of the Doctrine of Lapse, though the application of the doctrine itself was often politically motivated.

Statement 3 is incorrect. Lord Dalhousie's annexation policy was primarily driven by the expansion of British power and economic interests.  Concerns about the welfare of the annexed territories were secondary to these overriding imperial objectives. The stated reasons often served as pretexts for already-existing expansionist goals.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple choice questions based on the provided target content, adhering to all specified criteria.  Each question is designed to be challenging and requires detailed knowledge of Indian history and the figures mentioned.


**1. With reference to 19th-century Indian social reformers, consider the following statements:**

1. Savitribai Phule, a prominent figure from the Mali community, established the first girls' school in Pune in 1848.
2. Gopal Hari Deshmukh, known as "Lokahitwadi," championed the cause of widow remarriage and advocated for the reorganization of Indian society based on modern humanistic values.
3. Dadabhai Naoroji, a Parsi social reformer, co-founded an association to reform Zoroastrianism and played a significant role in advocating for legal status for women.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is partially incorrect. While Savitribai Phule was indeed a prominent figure from the Mali community and a pioneer of women's education, the year mentioned, 1848, is not entirely accurate according to most historical accounts. She and her husband, Jyotiba Phule, started a girls' school in Pune in 1851.  The precise date and year of the establishment of the first school is a matter of some scholarly debate.

Statement 2 is incorrect.  Gopal Hari Deshmukh, known as "Lokahitwadi," was indeed a champion of social reform in Maharashtra advocating for rational principles and modern values. However, his primary focus was not specifically on widow remarriage.  While he supported progressive social causes,  the widow remarriage movement was more directly spearheaded by others like Vishnu Shastri Pandit and Karsondas Mulji.

Statement 3 is correct. Dadabhai Naoroji, a prominent Parsi leader, was actively involved in social reform, co-founding associations focused on reforming Zoroastrianism and advocating for improved legal rights for women within the Parsi community. His contributions extended beyond social reform to encompass economic and political spheres.  His role as a leader of the Indian National Congress further underscores his importance in modern Indian history.


**2. With reference to the contributions of key figures in the Indian freedom struggle, consider the following statements:**

1. Annie Besant, known for her association with the Theosophical Society, actively collaborated with Bal Gangadhar Tilak in the Home Rule Movement and advocated for women's education.
2. Bal Gangadhar Tilak, a prominent leader from Maharashtra, founded the Home Rule League and championed the cause of Swaraj, utilizing Ganapati and Shivaji festivals to mobilize popular support.
3. Lala Lajpat Rai, a prominent figure from Punjab, is primarily remembered for his role in organizing the labor movement in India, particularly in Punjab and the Rawalpindi strike.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. Annie Besant, a prominent Theosophist, played a crucial role in the Indian independence movement, collaborating extensively with Bal Gangadhar Tilak in the Home Rule Movement. Her advocacy for women's education was also a significant aspect of her work.

Statement 2 is largely correct but requires clarification. While Bal Gangadhar Tilak was a key figure in the Indian freedom struggle, a leader of the Extremist faction within the Congress, and instrumental in the Home Rule Movement, the statement that he *founded* the Home Rule League is an oversimplification.  He was a crucial leader of the movement, but the Home Rule League had multiple branches and organizers.  His use of festivals to mobilize support is accurate.

Statement 3 is incorrect. While Lala Lajpat Rai was a significant figure in the Indian National Congress and associated with various nationalist movements,  he is not primarily known for organizing the labor movement in India.  That distinction is often attributed to figures like N.M. Lokhande.  Lala Lajpat Rai's contributions were primarily in the political arena, although he did involve himself with broader social reforms.


**3. With reference to the Revolt of 1857 and its aftermath, consider the following statements:**

1. The Revolt of 1857, while initially a sepoy mutiny, rapidly expanded to encompass widespread participation from peasants, artisans, and other sections of Indian society.
2. The economic exploitation under the East India Company, coupled with land revenue policies and administrative corruption, significantly contributed to the widespread discontent that fueled the revolt.
3.  The annexation of Awadh by Lord Dalhousie in 1856, while ostensibly aimed at improving governance, exacerbated existing grievances among sepoys and the populace, further inflaming tensions and contributing to the revolt.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

All three statements accurately reflect key aspects of the Revolt of 1857 and the socio-political context surrounding it.

Statement 1 correctly describes the evolution of the revolt.  It began as a mutiny within the East India Company's sepoy army but quickly escalated into a larger rebellion involving diverse sections of Indian society, demonstrating the widespread discontent with British rule.

Statement 2 accurately identifies the economic grievances that fueled the rebellion.  The East India Company's policies led to economic exploitation, land alienation, and administrative corruption, all of which contributed to widespread poverty and resentment among various segments of the population.  These economic factors were a significant underlying cause of the rebellion.

Statement 3 accurately highlights the role of the annexation of Awadh.  Lord Dalhousie's annexation of Awadh, despite its purported aim of improving governance, instead triggered widespread resentment and anger among the sepoys (many of whom were from Awadh) and the local population due to increased taxation and economic hardship. This action served as a significant catalyst for the rebellion.


**4. With reference to the pre-Congress nationalist organizations, consider the following statements:**

1. The British Indian Association, formed through the merger of the Landholders' Society and the Bengal British Indian Society, primarily focused on the interests of landlords and did not address wider public concerns.
2. The Poona Sarvajanik Sabha, established in the 1870s, played a significant role in shaping public opinion and intellectual discourse, particularly through its quarterly journal.
3. The Indian Association, founded in Calcutta in 1876, aimed to create a strong national public opinion and unify Indians across provincial boundaries, advocating for wider public interests and reforms.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 2 and 3 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is partially incorrect. The British Indian Association, while initially formed from groups with landlord interests, gradually broadened its scope to include wider public concerns.  It is not entirely accurate to say it *only* focused on landlord interests.  It did, however, start with a strong representation from the landed gentry.

Statement 2 is correct. The Poona Sarvajanik Sabha, under the guidance of Justice Ranade, was instrumental in shaping public opinion and intellectual discourse through its influential quarterly journal. This played a crucial role in the development of nationalist thought.

Statement 3 is correct.  The Indian Association, led by Surendranath Banerjea and Anandamohan Bose, explicitly aimed to cultivate a strong national public opinion, transcend provincial boundaries, and advocate for broader Indian interests beyond those of a specific class or region.  This made it a significant precursor to the Indian National Congress.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple choice questions based on the provided text, adhering to all specified criteria.  Note that the difficulty level is subjective and depends on the examinee's prior knowledge.  I've aimed for a challenging level by incorporating subtle inaccuracies and plausible distractors.


**1. With reference to the early phase of the Indian nationalist movement (1885-1905), consider the following statements:**

1.  The Moderates primarily employed constitutional methods, focusing on petitions and public opinion to influence the British government.
2.  Dadabhai Naoroji's "Poverty and Un-British Rule in India" significantly highlighted the economic exploitation of India by the British.
3.  The early nationalist movement effectively mobilized widespread peasant participation across India, leading to significant agrarian reforms.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The early phase of the Indian nationalist movement, led by the Moderates, primarily focused on constitutional methods like petitions, public meetings, and reasoned arguments to press for reforms within the existing political framework.  They believed in gradual progress through legal and peaceful means.

Statement 2 is also correct. Dadabhai Naoroji's work, "Poverty and Un-British Rule in India," was a seminal contribution to nationalist thought.  It systematically documented the economic drain of wealth from India to Britain, exposing the exploitative nature of British rule and significantly impacting the nationalist movement's agenda.

Statement 3 is incorrect.  While the nationalist movement aimed for mass mobilization, its early phase (1885-1905) largely remained confined to the urban educated elite.  Widespread peasant participation and substantial agrarian reforms were features of later phases of the movement, particularly under Gandhi's leadership.  The early nationalists did address peasant issues, but their impact was limited due to organizational constraints and the movement's predominantly urban character.  Therefore, this statement presents a misleading oversimplification of the historical reality.



**2. With reference to the Partition of Bengal in 1905 and the subsequent Swadeshi movement, consider the following statements:**

1.  The Partition was primarily intended to improve administrative efficiency by dividing a large and unwieldy province.
2.  The Swadeshi movement solely focused on boycotting British goods and promoting indigenous industries.
3.  Rabindranath Tagore's "Vande Mataram" became a powerful symbol of Bengali nationalism and later, Indian nationalism.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is partially correct but oversimplified. While Lord Curzon cited administrative efficiency as a justification, the Partition also had a political dimensionan attempt to weaken Bengali nationalism by dividing the province and fostering communal divisions.  The statement's simplicity obscures this crucial nuance.

Statement 2 is incorrect.  The Swadeshi movement encompassed more than just boycotting British goods and promoting Indian industries.  It also involved a cultural revival, promotion of vernacular education, and a broader push for self-reliance and national consciousness.  The statement presents an incomplete and narrow perspective.

Statement 3 is correct.  "Vande Mataram," composed by Rabindranath Tagore, became a powerful anthem of the Swadeshi movement and a potent symbol of both Bengali and later, Indian nationalism.  Its adoption as a national song played a crucial role in galvanizing the movement.



**3. With reference to the militant nationalists and revolutionary terrorism in early 20th-century India, consider the following statements:**

1.  The militant nationalists successfully established a unified and highly effective organization to coordinate their activities.
2.  Revolutionary terrorism primarily targeted high-ranking British officials and aimed to inspire mass uprisings.
3.  The activities of revolutionary groups like the Anushilan Samiti were entirely confined to Bengal.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 2 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect.  While militant nationalists played a vital role, their efforts to create a unified and effective organization were largely unsuccessful.  Internal divisions and lack of coordination hampered their overall effectiveness.

Statement 2 is partially correct but overstates the impact. While assassinations of British officials were a tactic, revolutionary terrorism did not consistently succeed in sparking widespread mass uprisings.  The movement remained largely confined to specific groups and regions.  The statement oversimplifies the complex relationship between terrorism and mass mobilization.

Statement 3 is incorrect.  Though Bengal was a major center of revolutionary activity,  terrorist groups and secret societies emerged and operated in other parts of India as well.  The statement presents a geographically limited and inaccurate picture.


**4.  Consider the following statements regarding the impact of the anti-Partition movement on the Indian National Congress:**

1. The 1905 Congress session, under Gopal Krishna Gokhales presidency, strongly condemned the Partition of Bengal and supported the Swadeshi movement.
2. The Surat split of 1907 marked a significant division within the Congress between the Moderates and the Extremists, impacting the movement's direction.
3. The Morley-Minto Reforms of 1909, introduced to appease the Moderates, granted substantial self-governance to India, effectively resolving the issues raised by the anti-Partition movement.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. While the 1905 Congress session did condemn the Partition and support the Swadeshi movement, it was presided over by Lord Curzon, not Gokhale. Gokhale was a prominent voice against the Partition, but the presidency of the session was held by someone else.

Statement 2 is correct. The Surat split of 1907 dramatically exposed the growing rift between the Moderates and Extremists within the Congress, significantly altering the movement's trajectory.

Statement 3 is incorrect. The Morley-Minto Reforms of 1909, while offering some limited constitutional concessions, did not grant substantial self-governance. They fell far short of the demands of the nationalist movement and did not resolve the core issues raised by the anti-Partition agitation.  The statement misrepresents the extent of the reforms and their impact on the nationalist movement.



These questions are designed to be challenging, requiring not only factual recall but also analytical skills to identify inaccuracies and subtle nuances within the statements.  They test the ability to critically evaluate information and avoid common misconceptions.

**1. With reference to the Indian National Movement, consider the following statements:**

1. Bal Gangadhar Tilak's newspaper, Kesari, primarily focused on promoting agrarian reforms in Maharashtra.
2. The Home Rule Movement, spearheaded by Tilak and Annie Besant, advocated for dominion status within the British Empire.
3.  The Ganapati and Shivaji festivals, organized by Tilak, aimed to foster a sense of Hindu unity and nationalist sentiment, indirectly challenging British rule.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statement 3 is correct.  Bal Gangadhar Tilak's organization of the Ganapati and Shivaji festivals was a crucial aspect of his strategy to mobilize mass support for the nationalist cause. These festivals, celebrating Hindu icons, served as platforms to promote nationalist sentiment and subtly challenge British authority. By reviving these festivals, Tilak successfully brought together diverse segments of Hindu society, strengthening the nationalist movement's base.

Statement 1 is incorrect. While Kesari, edited by Tilak, did address issues related to the agrarian sector in Maharashtra, its primary focus was broader, encompassing political commentary, social reform advocacy, and the promotion of militant nationalism.  It was not solely dedicated to agrarian reforms.

Statement 2 is incorrect.  The Home Rule Movement, a significant campaign within the Indian National Movement, advocated for Swaraj (self-rule), not dominion status.  The demand for complete independence intensified over time, and dominion status was never the central goal. The movement aimed to prepare India for self-governance and eventually complete independence.


**2. With reference to the early phase of the Indian National Movement (1885-1905), consider the following statements:**

1. The Moderate nationalists primarily employed constitutional methods, such as petitions and public meetings, to achieve their political goals, while completely rejecting any form of civil disobedience.
2. Dadabhai Naoroji's "Drain of Wealth" theory highlighted the economic exploitation of India by the British, significantly impacting nationalist discourse and shaping the movement's economic agenda.
3. The Indian National Congress, from its inception, unequivocally demanded complete independence from British rule.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 2 and 3 only

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 2 is correct. Dadabhai Naoroji's meticulous research and articulation of the "Drain of Wealth" theory exposed the economic exploitation of India under British rule.  This theory significantly influenced the nationalist movement, providing a concrete economic argument against British rule and shaping its future economic policy demands.  It became a cornerstone of the nationalist critique of British imperialism.

Statement 1 is incorrect.  While Moderate nationalists primarily focused on constitutional methods like petitions and public meetings, their approach was not entirely devoid of civil disobedience.  The methods employed were a mix of constitutional and non-violent means of protest, although they did not resort to large-scale civil disobedience that characterized later movements.

Statement 3 is incorrect.  The initial demands of the Indian National Congress were more moderate, focusing on reforms within the existing British framework rather than immediate complete independence. The demand for Swaraj (self-rule), while eventually becoming the central goal, emerged gradually and was not an immediate demand from the Congress's inception.


**3. With reference to the personalities involved in the Indian National Movement, consider the following statements:**

1.  Sarojini Naidu's primary contribution to the movement was through her work in organizing trade unions and leading labor movements.
2.  Jawaharlal Nehru's early political involvement was primarily focused on promoting religious harmony and interfaith dialogue.
3.  Gopal Krishna Gokhale, a prominent Moderate leader, advocated for gradual constitutional reforms within the British system, believing in a collaborative approach to achieving self-rule.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 1 and 2 only

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statement 3 is correct. Gopal Krishna Gokhale was a key figure among the Moderate nationalists. His approach emphasized gradual and constitutional methods to achieve India's self-rule.  He believed in working within the existing system to secure reforms and eventually lead to greater autonomy for India. His collaborative approach was a defining feature of the Moderate factions strategy.

Statement 1 is incorrect. While Sarojini Naidu was a prominent figure in the Indian National Movement and a powerful orator, her primary contributions were not in trade union organization.  Her strength lay in her poetic talent and her ability to connect with the masses through powerful speeches and mobilization efforts.

Statement 2 is incorrect.  While Nehru did advocate for communal harmony, his early political engagement was more focused on broader nationalist goals, including participation in the Non-Cooperation movement, advocacy for complete independence, and leading the Congress party in the fight against British rule. Religious harmony was part of his vision for independent India, but it was not his primary political focus in his early years.


**4.  With reference to the Quit India Movement, consider the following statements:**

1. The Quit India Resolution was passed by the Indian National Congress during a session held in Calcutta in August 1942.
2.  The movement saw widespread participation from diverse groups, including students, workers, and peasants, but notably lacked support from the princely states.
3.  Jayaprakash Narayan played a significant role in leading the movement in the eastern region, particularly in Bihar.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 2 and 3 are correct. The Quit India Movement was a mass movement with broad participation from various social strata.  The princely states, however, largely remained on the sidelines due to various factors including their own political interests and the British government's strategy of securing their loyalty. Jayaprakash Narayan's leadership in Bihar was instrumental in the movement's success in the eastern region.  His organizational capabilities and ability to mobilize support were vital.

Statement 1 is incorrect. The Quit India Resolution was indeed passed in August 1942, but the session was held in Bombay (Mumbai), not Calcutta (Kolkata). This is a key detail that differentiates the correct answer from the incorrect one.


**5. With reference to post-independence India, consider the following statements:**

1. The States Reorganisation Commission, appointed by Jawaharlal Nehru, primarily focused on reorganizing states based on geographical contiguity and administrative convenience.
2.  The nationalization of Air India was undertaken to enhance the country's international connectivity and to promote the growth of India's aviation sector by curbing private sector dominance.
3. The renaming of the Imperial Bank of India to the State Bank of India was initiated during the tenure of Lal Bahadur Shastri as Prime Minister.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) 2 and 3 only

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 2 is correct. The nationalization of Air India was a significant step in post-independence India.  It aimed to establish a national carrier with a strong international presence, enhancing India's global connectivity and promoting the country's aviation industry.  It was also intended to bring the aviation industry under state control and influence.

Statement 1 is incorrect. While geographical contiguity was a factor considered by the States Reorganisation Commission, the primary basis for reorganization was linguistic identity.  The commission aimed to create states that largely reflected the linguistic identities of their populations.

Statement 3 is incorrect. The renaming of the Imperial Bank of India to the State Bank of India occurred during Jawaharlal Nehru's tenure as Prime Minister, not under Lal Bahadur Shastri.  This is a significant chronological detail.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple choice questions based on the provided target content, adhering to all specified criteria.  Each question includes the correct answer and a detailed explanation.


**1. With reference to the historical context of Goa, consider the following statements:**

1.  The Vijayanagara Empire's influence extended to Goa, predating Portuguese arrival.
2.  The Bijapur Sultanate's control over Goa ended with the Portuguese conquest.
3.  Goa served as a crucial import point for horses from Iran and Iraq during certain periods.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

All three statements are historically accurate.  The Vijayanagara Empire indeed held sway over Goa before the Portuguese arrived, establishing its presence through military campaigns and political maneuvering in the region.  The Bijapur Sultanate's rule in Goa did conclude upon the successful Portuguese conquest led by Alfonso de Albuquerque.  The strategic location of Goa facilitated the import of horses, a crucial element of military power at that time, from both Iran and Iraq, reflecting Goa's importance in regional trade and power dynamics.  The other options fail to capture the full historical reality of Goa's multifaceted past.


**2. With reference to the Portuguese presence in Goa, consider the following statements:**

1.  Nino da Cunha significantly strengthened Goa's fortifications after capturing it.
2.  The Portuguese declared Goa their capital, shifting administrative power from Lisbon.
3.  The Portuguese archives in Goa contain extensive records of their colonial administration.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

While Alfonso de Albuquerque is credited with the initial capture of Goa, it was  Nino da Cunha who later implemented significant administrative and infrastructural changes, including strengthening fortifications.  The Portuguese indeed shifted their administrative centre to Goa, making it the hub of their Asian operations and not merely a trading post.  The Portuguese archives in Goa are a valuable primary source of information, containing detailed records of their colonial rule. Statement 1 is incorrect because it attributes the fortification work to the wrong person.  Option (b) correctly identifies the accurate statements.


**3. With reference to the history of Goa, consider the following statements:**

1.  The S Cathedral is a prominent example of Portuguese architecture in Goa.
2.  The Churches and Convents of Goa are a UNESCO World Heritage Site.
3.  The Maratha Empire never attempted to conquer Goa from the Portuguese.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 2 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

The S Cathedral in Old Goa stands as a significant testament to Portuguese architectural influence during their colonial rule.  The Churches and Convents of Goa are indeed recognized as a UNESCO World Heritage site, showcasing the region's rich history and cultural heritage.  However, the third statement is incorrect.  The Maratha Empire did, in fact, attempt to capture Goa, engaging in conflicts with the Portuguese, although their efforts did not lead to a successful conquest.


**4. Consider the following statements regarding the historical significance of Goa:**

1.  Goa's strategic importance diminished after Brazil became a major Portuguese colony.
2.  The Inquisition was introduced in Goa as a means of religious control by the Portuguese.
3.  The Deccan sultans signed several treaties with Goa, acknowledging its political autonomy.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 2 and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

The rise of Brazil as a major Portuguese colony did contribute to a relative decline in Goa's strategic importance in the Portuguese Empire's global trade and power structure.  The Portuguese implemented the Inquisition in Goa to suppress dissent and enforce religious conformity amongst the population.  However, the third statement is incorrect.  While the Deccan sultans interacted with Goa, they did not formally recognize its political autonomy; instead, their relationship was characterized by conflict and power struggles.


**5. With reference to the Indian National Congress, consider the following statements:**

1.  The Surat session of the Indian National Congress witnessed a major split within the organization.
2.  The Calcutta session of the Indian National Congress adopted the goal of Purna Swaraj.
3.  The Indian National Congress consistently supported the partition of Bengal.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 2 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

The Surat session of the Indian National Congress in 1907 is infamous for the major split between the Moderates and Extremists, marking a significant turning point in the organization's history. The Calcutta session of 1928 is indeed notable for the adoption of Purna Swaraj (complete independence) as the Congress's goal. However, the third statement is incorrect; the Indian National Congress actively opposed the partition of Bengal.



**6. With reference to the Home Rule Movement, consider the following statements:**

1.  Annie Besant was a key leader of the Home Rule Movement.
2.  Bal Gangadhar Tilak played a significant role in the Home Rule Movement.
3.  The Home Rule Movement aimed to achieve complete independence for India.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 2 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Both Annie Besant and Bal Gangadhar Tilak were instrumental figures in spearheading the Home Rule Movement, which aimed to establish self-governance in India. Although the movement was a stepping stone towards independence, its immediate goal was not complete independence, but rather significant strides towards self-rule within the British Empire.  The movement's objective was Dominion Status,  not complete independence.


**7. With reference to Shivaji's reign, consider the following statements:**

1.  Shivaji's military campaigns extended into Karnataka.
2.  Shivaji's administrative system borrowed elements from the Deccan sultanates.
3.  Shivaji's primary rivalry was with the Qutb Shahi dynasty of Golconda.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 2 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Shivaji's military expeditions did reach into Karnataka, showcasing his expansionist ambitions.  His administrative innovations drew inspiration from the established systems of the Deccan sultanates, demonstrating his pragmatic approach to governance.  However, while Shivaji did have conflicts with the Qutb Shahi dynasty, his primary rivalry was with the Mughal Empire, particularly under Aurangzeb.  Therefore, only statements 1 and 2 are accurate.


**8.  With reference to the activities of Shivaji Maharaj, consider the following statements:**

1.  The Treaty of Purandar marked a significant territorial concession to the Mughals.
2.  Shivaji's coronation took place at Raigarh.
3.  Shivaji's military tactics heavily relied on naval power.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

The Treaty of Purandar resulted in Shivaji ceding a significant portion of his territory to the Mughals.  His coronation ceremony did indeed take place at Raigarh, solidifying his claim to kingship.  However, while Shivaji did utilize naval forces, his military strategy predominantly focused on land warfare and guerrilla tactics, rather than naval dominance. Thus, only statements 1 and 2 are correct.


**9. With reference to the post-Civil Disobedience Movement debates within the Indian National Congress, consider the following statements:**

1.  Jawaharlal Nehru advocated for the immediate resumption of mass civil disobedience.
2.  Gandhi initially opposed office acceptance in the provincial elections.
3.  The Congress won a majority in all provincial assemblies in the 1937 elections.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 2 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Following the withdrawal of the Civil Disobedience Movement, Jawaharlal Nehru strongly argued for the immediate resumption of mass political action, contrasting with the more gradualist approach favored by other Congress leaders.  Gandhi initially expressed reservations about accepting office in the provincial legislatures, reflecting his concern about potential compromises with the British system.  However, the Congress did not win a majority in all provincial assemblies; it secured majorities in several but not all.  Therefore, only statements 1 and 2 are entirely accurate.


**10. With reference to the Government of India Act of 1935, consider the following statements:**

1.  The Act established an All-India Federation that included all princely states.
2.  The Act introduced provincial autonomy, replacing dyarchy.
3.  The Act granted universal adult suffrage throughout British India.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 2 and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

The proposed All-India Federation under the Government of India Act, 1935, never materialized due to the non-participation of many princely states. The Act did indeed replace dyarchy with provincial autonomy, granting provinces greater self-governance within the framework of British rule.  However, the Act did not grant universal adult suffrage; the franchise was extended but not to all adults in British India.  Therefore, only statement 2 is fully correct.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided target content, adhering to all specified criteria.  Each question includes the correct answer and a detailed explanation.


**1. Consider the following statements regarding the Partition of Bengal:**

1. The Partition of Bengal was primarily driven by linguistic differences between East and West Bengal.
2.  Lord Curzon's primary objective in partitioning Bengal was to weaken the burgeoning nationalist movement centered in Calcutta.
3. The Swadeshi Movement was a direct response to the economic hardships inflicted upon the Bengali population by the partition.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 2 and 3
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is partially correct but oversimplifies the complex motivations behind the partition. While linguistic differences existed, they were not the sole, or even primary, driver.  The partition was a multifaceted decision influenced by administrative concerns, a desire to control the politically active Bengali population, and to counter the growing nationalist sentiment.

Statement 2 is correct.  Lord Curzon's administration explicitly aimed to weaken the strength of Bengali nationalism, which was perceived as a significant threat to British rule.  Dividing Bengal into smaller, more manageable units was seen as a strategy to dilute the unified political force.

Statement 3 is also largely correct. The Partition of Bengal sparked widespread resentment and resistance, directly contributing to the rise of the Swadeshi Movement.  While economic grievances existed prior to the partition, the partition acted as a catalyst, intensifying existing frustrations and unifying opposition across social and economic strata.  The movement wasn't solely about economic hardship, but also about asserting Indian self-rule and resisting British administrative policies. Therefore, the combination of statements 2 and 3 provides the most accurate assessment.


**2. With reference to the Indian Civil Service (ICS), consider the following statements:**

1.  The ICS was initially created by Lord Wellesley during his tenure as Governor-General.
2. The Charter Act of 1853 formalized the structure and recruitment process of the ICS.
3.  Satyendra Nath Tagore was the first Indian to successfully qualify for the ICS.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 2 and 3
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. While Lord Wellesley expanded the civil service, the ICS as a distinct entity wasn't established until later.  The groundwork for the ICS was laid by Lord Cornwallis through his reforms, which established a more structured and standardized civil service system.

Statement 2 is correct. The Charter Act of 1853 is a pivotal point in the history of the ICS, marking its formal establishment, and outlining the procedures for selection and training.  This Act significantly shaped the future of the service.

Statement 3 is also correct. Satyendra Nath Tagore holds the distinction of being the first Indian to successfully clear the competitive examination for the ICS.  This marked a significant milestone in the struggle for Indian representation in the higher echelons of British administration.  Therefore, options 2 and 3 are the only correct statements.



**3. With reference to the Swadeshi Movement, consider the following statements:**

1. The Bengal School of Art was significantly influenced by the economic principles of Swadeshi.
2. The Swadeshi Movement was exclusively a Bengali phenomenon, confined to the Bengal region.
3. The Kukas actively propagated the Swadeshi economic policy through their religious and social networks.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 3 only
(c) 1 and 3
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The Swadeshi Movement, with its emphasis on supporting indigenous industries, had a profound impact on various sectors, including art. The Bengal School of Art, with its focus on Indian themes and styles, directly reflected the spirit of Swadeshi, promoting Indian artistic expression and challenging the dominance of Western art forms.

Statement 2 is incorrect.  While the movement originated in Bengal as a response to the Partition, its influence spread far beyond the region.  It became a pan-Indian movement, gaining support in various parts of India and involving diverse social groups and communities.

Statement 3 is correct.  The Kukas, a religious sect, actively supported the Swadeshi ideology and promoted self-reliance through their religious and social networks.  Their advocacy of Swadeshi demonstrated how the movement transcended purely political boundaries and integrated with socio-religious movements.  Therefore, statements 1 and 3 are correct.


**4. With reference to prominent figures of the Indian freedom struggle, consider the following statements:**

1.  Lal Bahadur Shastri translated Madame Curie's autobiography into Hindi.
2.  Rajendra Prasad was a teacher by profession before entering politics.
3.  J.B. Kripalani was a prominent Gandhian follower who held the position of Congress President.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?


(a) 1 only
(b) 3 only
(c) 2 and 3
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect.  While Lal Bahadur Shastri was a prominent figure in Indian politics, there's no record of him translating Madame Curie's autobiography.  The translator's identity would need further research to be confirmed.

Statement 2 is incorrect. Rajendra Prasad's primary profession was law, not teaching. He was a distinguished lawyer before he became involved in politics and eventually served as the first President of India.

Statement 3 is correct. J.B. Kripalani was a significant Gandhian and played a crucial role in the Indian National Congress, serving as its president.  His contributions to the freedom movement were substantial. Therefore, only statement 3 is accurate.


**5.  Consider the following statements about the Round Table Conferences:**

1.  The First Round Table Conference was boycotted by the Indian National Congress due to its lack of commitment to Purna Swaraj.
2.  The Gandhi-Irwin Pact paved the way for Gandhi's participation in the Second Round Table Conference as the sole representative of the Indian National Congress.
3. The Third Round Table Conference resulted in the immediate implementation of the Government of India Act 1935.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 2 and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The first Round Table Conference was indeed boycotted by the Congress, primarily due to its perceived inadequacy in addressing the demand for complete independence (Purna Swaraj). The Congress felt the conference didn't offer a genuine path towards self-rule.

Statement 2 is also correct. The Gandhi-Irwin Pact, a significant agreement between Mahatma Gandhi and Lord Irwin, led to the suspension of the Civil Disobedience Movement and facilitated Gandhi's participation in the Second Round Table Conference.  He represented the Congress's perspective on constitutional reforms.
