Statement 3 is incorrect.  The Third Round Table Conference, while contributing to the discussions, did not directly lead to the immediate implementation of the Government of India Act 1935.  The Act's implementation followed a considerable period of deliberation and legislative processes in Britain.  Therefore, only statements 1 and 2 are correct.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided target content, adhering to all specified criteria.  Each question includes the correct answer and a detailed explanation.

**1. Consider the following statements regarding the early British administrative policies in India:**

1. The introduction of the Ryotwari system led to a significant increase in land revenue for the British East India Company, primarily due to the elimination of intermediaries.
2. The Permanent Settlement, while intending to secure land revenue and encourage agricultural improvements, ultimately led to the rise of absentee landlords and the exploitation of ryots.
3. The Mahalwari system, implemented in parts of northern India, aimed to collect revenue directly from individual cultivators, thereby bypassing village communities.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (b) 1 and 2 only

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The Ryotwari system, implemented in Madras and Bombay Presidencies, aimed at direct revenue collection from individual cultivators (ryots). By removing intermediaries like zamindars, the British aimed to maximize revenue collection, and indeed, it initially did increase revenue significantly.  However, this came at the cost of increased exploitation of ryots, as the revenue demand was often unsustainable.

Statement 2 is also correct. The Permanent Settlement, implemented in Bengal, granted zamindars proprietary rights over their land in exchange for a fixed annual revenue payment to the British. While intended to increase revenue certainty and encourage agricultural improvements, it led to the rise of absentee landlords who focused on rent extraction rather than land improvement. Ryots faced increased exploitation and indebtedness.

Statement 3 is incorrect. The Mahalwari system, implemented in parts of northern India, collected revenue from groups of villages (mahals), not individual cultivators.  While the village headman (lambardar) was responsible for collection, the system still involved a collective responsibility at the village level, not direct individual assessment. The system, while intending to involve village communities, often resulted in overassessment and exploitation.


**2. With reference to the Indian freedom struggle and prominent figures, consider the following statements:**

1.  Bal Gangadhar Tilak's Home Rule Movement primarily focused on achieving Dominion Status within the British Empire.
2.  Annie Besant's Home Rule League actively collaborated with the moderate faction of the Indian National Congress, advocating for gradual constitutional reforms.
3.  Gopal Krishna Gokhale, a prominent Congress leader, vehemently opposed the partition of Bengal and actively participated in the Non-Cooperation Movement.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (d) None

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect.  While Tilak's Home Rule League aimed for Swaraj (self-rule), it wasn't explicitly focused on Dominion Status.  His vision was more radical, envisioning complete independence from British rule.

Statement 2 is incorrect.  Annie Besant's Home Rule League, while advocating self-rule, did not primarily collaborate with the Congress moderates.  Her movement had a more independent character, although she did work alongside Tilak, who was considered an extremist.  Her approach, while advocating for greater Indian self-governance, differed from the moderates' gradualist approach.

Statement 3 is incorrect.  Gopal Krishna Gokhale was indeed a prominent Congress leader and advocated for self-government through constitutional means.  However, he was a moderate and did not participate in the Non-Cooperation Movement, which was launched by Mahatma Gandhi.  While he criticized the partition of Bengal, he was part of the moderate section.


**3. With reference to the British revenue systems in India, consider the following statements:**

1.  The Izaredari system, implemented by Warren Hastings, aimed to enhance revenue collection by directly assessing land based on its productivity.
2.  Under the Ryotwari system, the revenue demand was fixed permanently, ensuring stable income for both the ryots and the British government.
3.  The Mahalwari system, while aiming for collective responsibility, often led to inaccurate assessments and exploitation due to corrupt officials.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (c) 3 only

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. The Izaredari system, introduced by Warren Hastings, involved contracting out revenue collection to farmers who bid the highest amount.  It did not directly assess land based on productivity, leading to exploitation of peasants.

Statement 2 is incorrect. Under the Ryotwari system, the revenue demand was not fixed permanently. It was periodically revised, often leading to overassessment and hardship for ryots.  The system aimed at direct revenue collection from ryots and did not guarantee stable income.

Statement 3 is correct. The Mahalwari system aimed to collect revenue from village communities. However, due to the complexity of assessment and the potential for corruption among officials, it often resulted in inaccurate assessments and the exploitation of cultivators.


**4.  With reference to prominent figures of the Indian freedom struggle and their contributions, consider the following statements:**

1. C. Rajagopalachari, a prominent Congress leader, played a crucial role in organizing the Salt Satyagraha.
2.  V.P. Menon significantly contributed to the smooth transfer of power from British rule to independent India.
3.  Mahatma Gandhi's initial involvement in Indian politics focused primarily on advocating for complete independence from British rule.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 2 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a) 2 only

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect.  While C. Rajagopalachari was a prominent Congress leader, he wasn't directly involved in the organization of the Salt Satyagraha.  That was primarily led by Mahatma Gandhi.

Statement 2 is correct. V.P. Menon, as the Secretary of the States' Ministry, played a crucial role in the negotiations and the smooth transfer of power from the British to independent India.  His expertise in constitutional matters and his diplomatic skills were instrumental in this process.

Statement 3 is incorrect.  While Mahatma Gandhi ultimately advocated for complete independence, his initial political activities focused on various social and economic issues before fully embracing the goal of complete independence as a primary objective.  His early involvement was more about addressing specific grievances within the existing system.


**5. With reference to the impact of British rule on India, consider the following statements:**

1. The British administration consistently supported social reforms to improve the condition of marginalized communities in India.
2. The British revenue policies, though intending to enhance state revenue, often resulted in the impoverishment of the peasantry and increased rural indebtedness.
3. The British consistently encouraged Indian unity and discouraged communal tensions to maintain stability in their colony.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (b) 2 only

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. The British approach to social reform was inconsistent and often driven by political expediency rather than a genuine commitment to social justice.  While some reforms were implemented (like the abolition of Sati), the British often favored policies that maintained the status quo, even if it perpetuated social inequalities, especially after the 1857 revolt.

Statement 2 is correct. The British revenue systems, including the Permanent Settlement, Ryotwari, and Mahalwari systems, while aiming to maximize revenue collection, often resulted in the impoverishment of the peasantry.  High tax demands, coupled with inefficient collection methods and the rise of absentee landlords, led to widespread rural indebtedness and economic hardship for cultivators.

Statement 3 is incorrect.  The British often employed a "divide and rule" policy, exacerbating existing communal tensions between different religious and caste groups for their own political advantage.  This strategy undermined Indian unity and was a key feature of their colonial strategy.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple choice questions based on the provided target content, adhering to all specified criteria.  Each question includes the correct answer and a detailed explanation.


**1. With reference to the Partition of Bengal, consider the following statements:**

1.  The Partition of Bengal, implemented in October 16, 1905, aimed to weaken the political influence of the Bengali elite by dividing the province on linguistic lines.
2.  The Swadeshi movement, characterized by boycotts of British goods and promotion of indigenous industries, emerged as a direct response to the Partition of Bengal.
3.  Nawab Salimullah of Dacca, initially opposed to the partition, later found himself encouraged by the All-India Muslim League's support for the partition, influencing his stance.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. Lord Curzon, the Viceroy at the time, implemented the Partition of Bengal primarily to diminish the power of the politically active Bengali population, seen as a threat to British rule. The division was partially based on linguistic differences, creating administrative ease for the British, but the primary motivation was political control.

Statement 2 is also correct. The Partition of Bengal sparked widespread outrage and resistance, leading to the rise of the Swadeshi movement. This movement aimed to challenge British economic dominance through boycotts and the promotion of Indian-made goods and products. The movement was a significant expression of Indian nationalism.

Statement 3 is incorrect.  While the All-India Muslim League initially opposed the partition, seeing it as detrimental to Muslim interests,  Nawab Salimullah of Dacca was initially a supporter of the partition, believing it would benefit the Muslim population of East Bengal.  His later support for the League does not stem from a change in his view on the partition itself, but rather his alignment with the League's broader political goals.  The statement incorrectly suggests a causal relationship between the League's support and his initial opposition.


**2. With reference to the All-India Muslim League, consider the following statements:**

1. The All-India Muslim League, established in 1906, initially advocated for the preservation of the unity of Bengal and actively opposed the concept of separate electorates.
2.  The London branch of the All-India Muslim League, established in 1908, was instrumental in disseminating the League's viewpoints to a wider international audience.
3.  Liaquat Ali Khan, a prominent member of the All-India Muslim League, played a significant role in shaping the League's policies and strategies during the crucial period leading up to the Partition of India.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. The All-India Muslim League's initial stance was complex and evolved over time. While it did oppose the Partition of Bengal, its opposition was not absolute and stemmed from concerns about the potential marginalization of Muslims in the proposed administrative structure.  The League's position on separate electorates also evolved from opposition to eventual acceptance.

Statement 2 is correct. The establishment of a London branch was strategically important for the All-India Muslim League to influence British public opinion and gain international support for its cause.  This branch served as a crucial platform for disseminating information and advocacy efforts overseas.

Statement 3 is correct. Liaquat Ali Khan was indeed a key figure in the All-India Muslim League, serving as a prominent leader and playing a vital role in the League's policies leading up to and during the Partition of India. His contributions were instrumental in shaping the League's political strategies.


**3. With reference to the Provisional Government of India in Kabul, consider the following statements:**

1. The Provisional Government of India, established in Kabul, aimed to secure international recognition for Indias independence struggle.
2.  Maulana Barkat Ullah and Maulana Obeidullah Sindhi were key figures actively involved in the establishment of the Provisional Government of India in Kabul.
3.  The location of the Provisional Government of India in Kabul, a city historically significant for trade and political relations between India and Central Asia, facilitated its outreach to international actors.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3
(d) 1 only


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The establishment of the Provisional Government of India in Kabul was a deliberate strategy to garner international support for India's struggle for independence.  Its location outside British India allowed it to operate independently and engage with foreign powers.

Statement 2 is correct.  Maulana Barkat Ullah and Maulana Obeidullah Sindhi were central figures in forming and leading the Provisional Government.  Their prominence within the Indian independence movement made their involvement pivotal to the government's legitimacy.

Statement 3 is correct. Kabul's historical role as a significant trading center and a point of contact between India and Central Asia provided strategic advantages for the Provisional Government. This location facilitated communication and interaction with potential allies and supporters in various parts of the world.


**4. With reference to Jawaharlal Nehru's role in India's history, consider the following statements:**

1. Jawaharlal Nehru's unwavering support for the creation of Pakistan stemmed from his belief in the principle of self-determination for all communities in India.
2.  Jawaharlal Nehru, as Prime Minister, played a pivotal role in shaping India's foreign policy, advocating for non-alignment and promoting peaceful coexistence among nations.
3.  Jawaharlal Nehru's close collaboration with Subhas Chandra Bose during the pre-independence era significantly influenced the trajectory of the Indian National Congress.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 2 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect.  Jawaharlal Nehru, while accepting the Partition of India, was deeply critical of the creation of Pakistan and saw it as a setback for the goal of a unified India. His acceptance was a pragmatic response to the political realities of the time, not a reflection of enthusiastic support.

Statement 2 is correct. Nehru's vision significantly shaped India's non-aligned foreign policy. His emphasis on peace, self-reliance, and international cooperation defined India's approach to global politics for decades.

Statement 3 is incorrect. While Nehru and Bose were both prominent Congress leaders, their relationship was complex and marked by ideological differences.  Their collaboration was limited and did not significantly influence the Congress' trajectory in a sustained way.  Bose's departure from the Congress and the formation of the Forward Bloc created a rift.


**5.  With reference to the Partition of India, consider the following statements:**

1.  The Radcliffe Line, a boundary drawn hastily after the Partition, caused widespread displacement and communal violence, particularly in Punjab and Bengal.
2.  The Partition of India was solely a result of the Muslim League's demand for a separate Muslim state, with little influence from other factors.
3.  Mahatma Gandhi, despite his opposition to Partition, played a crucial role in mitigating the immediate aftermath of the Partition, attempting to alleviate suffering and promote communal harmony.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 3 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The Radcliffe Line, drawn quickly and with limited information, led to significant territorial disputes and displacement of populations, triggering widespread communal violence in Punjab and Bengal.

Statement 2 is incorrect. While the Muslim League's demand was a major factor, the Partition was a complex event influenced by various factors, including British policies of 'Divide and Rule', communal tensions, and the political strategies of different Indian groups.

Statement 3 is correct.  Gandhi, though opposed to Partition, actively worked to lessen the violence and suffering that followed. His efforts to promote communal harmony were remarkable, although ultimately limited in their effectiveness given the scale of the crisis.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple choice questions based on the provided target content, focusing on the Indian National Congress and related historical events.  Each question adheres to the specified format and difficulty level, incorporating plausible distractors and requiring factual recall and analysis.


**1. Consider the following statements regarding the Indian National Congress (INC):**

1.  The INC's initial sessions were primarily dominated by representatives from the urban elite, with limited participation from rural populations.
2.  The INC consistently maintained a unified stance throughout its history, never experiencing internal factionalism or splits.
3.  The INC's early political strategies relied heavily on constitutional methods and petitions to the British government, with a later shift towards mass movements and civil disobedience.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 3 only
(b) 3 only
(c) 1 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct.  The INC's early leadership and membership were predominantly drawn from the educated, urban middle and upper classes.  While the Congress aimed for broader representation, its initial reach and influence were concentrated in urban areas.  The inclusion of rural and marginalized communities came later, significantly influenced by figures like Gandhi.

Statement 2 is incorrect. The INC experienced significant internal divisions and splits throughout its history. The most notable example is the Surat Split of 1907, which divided the Congress into Moderate and Extremist factions.  Subsequent disagreements and power struggles also fractured the party's unity at various points.

Statement 3 is correct. The early INC adopted a largely constitutional approach, advocating for reforms through petitions, lobbying, and participation in legislative councils.  However, the increasing frustration with the British government's response led to a gradual shift towards mass movements and civil disobedience, notably under Gandhi's leadership.  This change reflected a broader evolution in the Congress's strategy and tactics.  The shift wasn't abrupt but a gradual transition based on evolving circumstances and the changing political landscape.


**2. With reference to the Ilbert Bill, consider the following statements:**

1. The Ilbert Bill aimed to grant Indian judges the power to try European offenders, a move that faced significant opposition from the European community in India.
2. Lord Curzon actively supported the Ilbert Bill and played a key role in its passage through the British Parliament.
3. The Ilbert Bill directly led to the formation of the Indian National Congress as a direct response to the perceived injustice.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is accurate. The Ilbert Bill, introduced by Lord Ripon, proposed to remove the restriction that prevented Indian judges from trying European British citizens. This attempt to bring about legal equality faced fierce resistance from the British community in India, who saw it as a threat to their privileged status.  The opposition highlights the deep-seated racial biases and power imbalances within colonial society.

Statement 2 is incorrect. Lord Curzon, known for his imperialistic views, was not associated with the Ilbert Bill.  In fact, his policies often ran counter to the more liberal reforms attempted by earlier viceroys like Lord Ripon.

Statement 3 is incorrect. While the Ilbert Bill contributed to the growing sense of nationalist sentiment, it did not directly lead to the founding of the Indian National Congress. The INC was founded in 1885, several years after the Ilbert Bill controversy, and its origins lie in a complex interplay of factors beyond a single legislative act. The INC's formation was a culmination of various socio-political factors, including the desire for a unified platform to address Indian grievances.


**3. With reference to the Indian National Congress's early years (1885-1905), consider the following statements:**

1.  The Congress's initial focus was primarily on achieving complete independence ("Purna Swaraj") from British rule.
2.  Dadabhai Naoroji played a crucial role in educating the British public about India's economic exploitation under colonial rule.
3.  The Congress initially welcomed and collaborated closely with the British government, viewing it as a partner in progress.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 2 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect.  The INC's early goals were more modest than demanding complete independence immediately. The initial focus was on securing gradual reforms within the existing colonial framework. The demand for "Purna Swaraj" emerged much later in the nationalist movement.

Statement 2 is correct. Dadabhai Naoroji, a prominent early Congress leader, played a significant role in highlighting India's economic drain under British rule through his writings and speeches in Britain. He exposed the exploitative nature of British economic policies and significantly influenced British public opinion.  His work is a crucial part of understanding the economic dimensions of the struggle for independence.

Statement 3 is incorrect.  While some early Congress leaders initially believed in cooperation with the British government, hoping for gradual reforms,  the relationship was not one of close collaboration. The Congress consistently pressed for greater Indian representation and autonomy, often facing opposition from the British authorities.  The relationship was characterized by both cooperation and conflict, with the balance shifting over time.




**4. Consider the following statements about the Non-Cooperation Movement:**

1. The Chauri Chaura incident, where a mob set fire to a police station, directly led to the movement's suspension by Mahatma Gandhi.
2.  The Khilafat issue, concerning the treatment of the Ottoman Caliph, played a significant role in galvanizing Muslim participation in the movement.
3. The Non-Cooperation Movement primarily focused on violent resistance against British rule, resulting in widespread armed conflict.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3
(d) 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The Chauri Chaura incident, marked by violence and loss of life, deeply concerned Gandhi who believed in non-violent resistance. This incident prompted him to suspend the Non-Cooperation Movement to prevent further escalation of violence. The decision, though controversial within the Congress, demonstrated Gandhi's unwavering commitment to non-violence.

Statement 2 is correct. The Khilafat issue, related to the post-World War I treatment of the Ottoman Caliphate, became a rallying point for Indian Muslims.  It fostered Hindu-Muslim unity and significantly contributed to the widespread support for the Non-Cooperation Movement.  The shared concern over the Caliphate's fate brought together diverse communities in a common cause against British rule.

Statement 3 is incorrect. The Non-Cooperation Movement was fundamentally based on non-violent methods of resistance.  While instances of violence occurred, they were deviations from the movement's core principle. The movement primarily employed methods of civil disobedience, boycotts, and non-cooperation. The movement's emphasis on non-violence distinguished it from other forms of resistance at the time.



**5. With reference to the Constituent Assembly of India, consider the following statements:**

1.  The Constituent Assembly was entirely elected through universal adult suffrage.
2. Jawaharlal Nehru played a pivotal role in drafting the Objectives Resolution, which laid the foundation for the Indian Constitution.
3. The Constituent Assembly faced no significant opposition or challenges during its deliberations.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 2 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3
(d) 1 only


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. The Constituent Assembly was not directly elected through universal adult suffrage. Members were indirectly elected by the provincial legislatures, a system reflecting the existing political structure.  Universal adult franchise was adopted later as a fundamental principle of the Indian Constitution itself.

Statement 2 is correct. Jawaharlal Nehru played a crucial role in framing the Objectives Resolution, which outlined the fundamental principles and goals of the new Indian Constitution.  The resolution set the tone and direction for the Constituent Assembly's subsequent work.

Statement 3 is incorrect. The Constituent Assembly faced several challenges, including debates over the nature of the Indian state, representation of minorities, and disputes with the Muslim League.  The partition of India further complicated the Assembly's work.  The challenges highlight the complexities of nation-building and the difficult compromises required to create a new nation-state.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple choice questions based on the provided target content, adhering to all specified criteria.  Each question includes the correct answer and a detailed explanation.


**1. With reference to the Indian Nationalist Movement, consider the following statements:**

1. Lala Lajpat Rai's political ideology was significantly influenced by American socialists, leading him to advocate for Purna Swaraj.
2.  Jawaharlal Nehru, while initially differing with Mahatma Gandhi on certain strategies, ultimately eulogized Gandhi's contributions to India's independence.
3. The Constituent Assembly, instrumental in drafting the Indian Constitution, initially lacked participation from princely states.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 2 only


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 2 is correct.  Jawaharlal Nehru and Mahatma Gandhi, while having ideological differences, particularly regarding the pace and methods of the freedom struggle, ultimately shared a common goal of Indian independence. Nehru's later eulogies to Gandhi reflect this complex relationship.

Statement 3 is also correct.  The initial formation of the Constituent Assembly saw limited involvement from princely states, a significant obstacle in the process of nation-building.  Their eventual inclusion was a crucial step towards a unified India.

Statement 1 is incorrect. While Lajpat Rai did associate with American socialists and was a proponent of Purna Swaraj,  directly linking his ideology solely to American socialist influence is an oversimplification. His nationalist views were multifaceted and stemmed from various influences.  The assertion that this influence *led* him to advocate for Purna Swaraj is not entirely supported by historical evidence.  His advocacy for Purna Swaraj was a part of a broader nationalist movement, and his socialist leanings were one among several contributing factors.



**2. With reference to the early Indian National Congress, consider the following statements:**

1. Dadabhai Naoroji, a prominent leader of the Moderate phase, primarily focused on constitutional agitation and consistently rejected extra-parliamentary methods.
2.  Bal Gangadhar Tilak, known for his role in the Home Rule Movement, primarily utilized religious festivals like Ganapati and Shivaji festivals to mobilize mass support and propagate militant nationalism.
3.  The Indian Councils Act of 1892, though increasing Indian representation in legislative councils,  failed to grant Indians substantial control over the budget, leading to continued nationalist dissatisfaction.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 2 is correct.  Tilak masterfully used the Ganapati and Shivaji festivals to foster a sense of Indian nationalism and mobilize mass participation, thereby indirectly challenging British rule. This method was a key component of his strategy for promoting militant nationalism.

Statement 3 is also correct. The Indian Councils Act of 1892, while expanding the legislative councils, retained a significant official majority and did not grant Indians control over the budget. This limitation fueled continued nationalist demands for greater self-governance.

Statement 1 is incorrect. Dadabhai Naoroji, while primarily focused on constitutional methods, did not *consistently* reject extra-parliamentary methods.  The Moderate phase's approach was nuanced and involved a combination of constitutional and extra-constitutional means, depending on the situation.


**3. With reference to the post-Civil Disobedience Movement debates within the Indian National Congress, consider the following statements:**

1. Subhas Chandra Bose, in contrast to Gandhi's approach, advocated for a continuous confrontation with imperialism, rejecting the "struggle-truce-struggle" strategy.
2. Jawaharlal Nehru, a prominent leftist voice within the Congress, initially supported office acceptance under the Government of India Act, 1935, believing it to be a strategic move to consolidate power.
3.  The Government of India Act, 1935, despite introducing provincial autonomy, retained significant "safeguards" and "special responsibilities" for the Governor, limiting the effectiveness of self-governance.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 3 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3
(d) 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct.  Subhas Chandra Bose strongly criticized the "struggle-truce-struggle" strategy, advocating for sustained direct action against British imperialism until complete independence was achieved.

Statement 3 is correct. The Government of India Act, 1935, while granting provincial autonomy, retained considerable power for the Governor, including "safeguards" and "special responsibilities," which significantly constrained the autonomy of provincial governments.

Statement 2 is incorrect. Nehru was a strong opponent of office acceptance under the 1935 Act, believing it would compromise the nationalist struggle and divert attention from the primary goal of complete independence. He saw it as a retreat from revolutionary action.


**4.  Consider the following statements about the roles of key figures in the Indian freedom struggle:**

1.  N.M. Joshi represented the interests of Indian labour at the 1919 Washington Summit of the ILO.
2.  Mahatma Gandhi's assassination by Nathuram Godse occurred on January 30, 1948, at Birla House in Delhi.
3. Maulana Abul Kalam Azad's political views strongly favored Dominion Status over complete independence for India.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 2 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. N.M. Joshi, a prominent labor leader, represented Indian workers at the 1919 ILO summit in Washington.

Statement 2 is correct.  Mahatma Gandhi was assassinated by Nathuram Godse on January 30, 1948, at Birla House in New Delhi.

Statement 3 is incorrect. Maulana Abul Kalam Azad was a staunch advocate for complete independence for India and vehemently opposed Dominion Status.


**5. With reference to the Constituent Assembly, consider the following statements:**

1. The Constituent Assembly's drafting process was significantly influenced by the Congress Working Committee, which held a majority in the Assembly.
2.  The Objectives Resolution, presented to the Constituent Assembly, was authored by Sardar Vallabhbhai Patel, outlining the fundamental principles of the future Indian Constitution.
3. The Constituent Assembly's adoption of the Indian Constitution marked the formal end of British rule in India.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 3 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The Congress, having a majority in the Constituent Assembly, significantly shaped the drafting and adoption of the Indian Constitution. The Congress Working Committee played a crucial role in this process.

Statement 3 is correct. The adoption of the Indian Constitution by the Constituent Assembly marked the formal end of British rule and the commencement of independent India.

Statement 2 is incorrect. The Objectives Resolution, a foundational document for the Indian Constitution, was presented by Jawaharlal Nehru, not Sardar Vallabhbhai Patel.

**1. With reference to the early 20th-century Indian nationalist movement, consider the following statements:**

1.  The Home Rule movement, spearheaded by figures like Bal Gangadhar Tilak and Annie Besant, concluded in 1919, significantly impacting the trajectory of the Indian freedom struggle.
2.  N.M. Joshi, a prominent figure in the Indian labour movement, played a crucial role in the All India Trade Union Congress (AITUC)'s initial organizational phase and subsequent ideological splits.
3.  Joseph Baptista's contribution to the Home Rule movement was primarily focused on establishing a parallel administrative structure independent of British colonial rule.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. While the Home Rule movement was indeed a significant event in the early 20th-century Indian nationalist movement, led by prominent figures like Bal Gangadhar Tilak and Annie Besant, it concluded in 1919. The provided text doesn't indicate that the movement concluded in 1919 but this date is widely accepted as its end.  The movement's impact on the subsequent phases of the freedom struggle is undeniable, but the precise statement about its conclusion needs further verification.  

Statement 2 is correct. N.M. Joshi was a key figure in the Indian labor movement and played a vital role in the formation and early development of the AITUC. His involvement in the internal conflicts and ideological divisions within the AITUC is well documented.  The text supports this.

Statement 3 is incorrect. The text does not mention Joseph Baptista's involvement in establishing a parallel administrative structure.  While he was a founder of the All India Home Rule League, his contributions were primarily focused on political mobilization and advocacy for self-rule, not the creation of an alternative administrative system.  The statement misrepresents his role.  Therefore, only statement 2 is entirely accurate.


**2. With reference to the leaders of the Indian independence movement, consider the following statements:**

1.  Maulana Abul Kalam Azad's primary contribution to post-independence India was his leadership in establishing the Indian Council for Cultural Relations (ICCR).
2.  Lala Lajpat Rai's political activities were primarily confined to the Punjab region, where he led various movements against British rule.
3.  Bal Gangadhar Tilak's advocacy for Swaraj primarily revolved around the concept of complete independence from British rule, as opposed to a dominion status.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. While Maulana Abul Kalam Azad did found the ICCR, this was a post-independence activity. His major contributions were during the independence movement itself, including his role in the Congress and his significant influence on the shaping of the political landscape. The statement oversimplifies his vast contributions.

Statement 2 is correct. Lala Lajpat Rai's political career and influence were heavily concentrated in the Punjab. He actively participated in and led various movements within the region, making him a prominent leader in Punjab's struggle for independence. The text supports this.

Statement 3 is partially correct, but needs nuance. While Tilak advocated for Swaraj, the precise definition varied.  His vision of Swaraj evolved over time, and while he ultimately desired complete independence, his initial formulations might have allowed for interpretations including dominion status within the British Empire.  The statement presents an oversimplification of a complex issue.  Therefore, statements 2 and 3 are the most accurate, albeit with the caveat on statement 3.



**3. With reference to the impact of the Partition of Bengal (1905) consider the following statements:**

1. The partition, instigated by Lord Curzon, aimed primarily at administrative efficiency, rather than weakening the burgeoning nationalist movement in Bengal.
2.  The Swadeshi movement, a direct consequence of the partition, witnessed significant participation from women, students, and certain sections of the urban middle class but notably lacked widespread support among the Muslim population.
3. The annulment of the partition in 1911 was primarily a response to the growing threat posed by revolutionary terrorism in Bengal.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 3 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. While Lord Curzon might have cited administrative reasons, the partition's primary intention was widely perceived as a strategic move to weaken the nationalist movement centered in Bengal by dividing the Bengali population along linguistic and religious lines.  The statement ignores the political motivations behind the partition.

Statement 2 is correct. The Swadeshi movement, triggered by the partition, saw participation from various sections of society, including women, students, and urban middle classes. However, the movement did not gain widespread support from the Muslim population due to several factors, including the government's policy of divide and rule and the movement's Hindu-centric nature. The text corroborates this.

Statement 3 is correct. The British government's decision to annul the partition in 1911 was largely a reaction to the escalating threat of revolutionary terrorism and violence in Bengal.  The annulment aimed to defuse the volatile situation and regain control.  The text clearly supports this.  Thus, only statements 2 and 3 are entirely correct.


**4. With reference to the Morley-Minto Reforms of 1909, consider the following statements:**

1. The reforms significantly increased the number of elected members in both the Imperial and Provincial Legislative Councils, granting Indians substantial power in the legislative process.
2.  Separate electorates were introduced for Muslims, a provision that had a long-lasting and detrimental impact on Indian politics by exacerbating communal divisions.
3.  The reforms introduced the principle of direct elections to the legislative councils, paving the way for a more representative and democratic system.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 2 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. While the number of elected members did increase, the overall power structure remained heavily tilted in favor of the British.  The elected members were a minority, and many were indirectly elected, limiting their actual influence on policy-making.  The statement exaggerates the extent of Indian power granted.

Statement 2 is correct. The introduction of separate electorates for Muslims was a crucial aspect of the reforms, and it undeniably contributed to the deepening of communal divisions within Indian politics.  This provision had long-term negative consequences, creating a separate political sphere for Muslims and hindering the development of a unified national identity. The text supports this.

Statement 3 is incorrect. The reforms did not introduce direct elections.  The election process remained largely indirect, with electors choosing representatives through a multi-tiered system. This indirect system did not foster a truly representative democracy.  The statement is factually inaccurate. Therefore, only statement 2 is entirely correct.


**5. Consider the following statements regarding the early phases of the Indian National Congress:**

1.  The Indian National Congress, from its inception, actively embraced a militant nationalist approach, advocating for complete independence from British rule.
2.  The early Congress witnessed a significant ideological divide between moderate and extremist factions, leading to internal conflicts and eventual splits.
3. The Surat Split of 1907 decisively ended the ideological differences between the moderate and extremist factions within the Congress.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 2 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect.  The Indian National Congress initially adopted a moderate approach, focusing on constitutional means and gradual reforms. The adoption of militant nationalism came later, during the Swadeshi movement and the rise of extremist leaders. The statement misrepresents the early Congress's strategy.

Statement 2 is correct. The early Congress witnessed a considerable ideological divide between moderate and extremist factions, resulting in internal conflicts and tensions. These disagreements regarding the pace and methods of the freedom struggle contributed to serious divisions within the organization. The text supports this.

Statement 3 is incorrect. The Surat Split of 1907 exacerbated the existing divide between the moderate and extremist factions, but it did not resolve the ideological differences.  The split resulted in a temporary dominance of the moderates but the underlying ideological conflict persisted.  The statement is factually incorrect about the outcome of the split. Therefore, only statement 2 is accurate.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided text, focusing on Jawaharlal Nehru, Mahatma Gandhi, Sardar Patel, C. Rajagopalachari, and related historical figures and events.  Each question adheres to the specified format and difficulty level, including detailed explanations.


**1. With reference to the Indian National Movement, consider the following statements:**

1.  The Nehru Report, while advocating for Dominion Status, was ultimately rejected by the Muslim League due to its emphasis on joint electorates.
2.  The Government of India Act of 1935, despite introducing provincial autonomy, retained significant safeguards and special responsibilities for the Governor-General, limiting its effectiveness in transferring real power.
3.  The "struggle-truce-struggle" strategy, championed by Mahatma Gandhi, was criticized by Jawaharlal Nehru for its inherent passivity and inability to sustain continuous pressure on the British.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

All three statements accurately reflect aspects of the Indian National Movement's trajectory.  The Nehru Report, drafted by Motilal Nehru, did propose Dominion Status as a stepping stone but was rejected by the Muslim League due to its stance on joint electorates, which they perceived as detrimental to their interests. The 1935 Act, while granting provincial autonomy, significantly curtailed the power of elected governments through the Governor-General's extensive "safeguards" and "special responsibilities."  This limited the extent of self-governance and preserved substantial British control.  Finally, Jawaharlal Nehru's criticism of Gandhi's "struggle-truce-struggle" strategy is well-documented, highlighting Nehru's preference for more consistent and aggressive confrontation with the British Raj.  He believed that the cyclical nature of Gandhi's approach hampered the momentum of the movement.


**2. With reference to the early years of the Indian National Congress, consider the following statements:**

1.  Dadabhai Naoroji, while thrice president of the Indian National Congress, primarily focused on economic issues such as the "drain of wealth" theory.
2.  Gopal Krishna Gokhale, known for his moderate approach, established the Servants of India Society, advocating for gradual constitutional reforms within the British system.
3.  Bal Gangadhar Tilak, a prominent nationalist leader, spearheaded the Home Rule Movement, promoting a more assertive and militant form of nationalism.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

All three statements correctly describe key figures and their roles in the early Congress.  Dadabhai Naoroji, a prominent early Congress leader,  was indeed president multiple times and famously articulated the "drain of wealth" theory, highlighting the economic exploitation of India by the British. Gokhale, a key moderate leader, did establish the Servants of India Society to promote constructive work and advocate for gradual reforms within the existing constitutional framework. Tilak, a leader of the extremist faction, played a crucial role in the Home Rule Movement, which sought to mobilize popular support for self-rule through a more assertive and less conciliatory approach than that of the moderates.


**3. Consider the following statements regarding the partition of India:**

1.  Lord Mountbatten, as Viceroy, played a pivotal role in the partition process, despite facing criticism for its hasty execution and the resulting communal violence.
2.  Mahatma Gandhi, while advocating for Hindu-Muslim unity, ultimately accepted the partition as a necessary evil to prevent further bloodshed.
3.  Jawaharlal Nehru, initially opposed to the partition, eventually accepted it as a fait accompli, focusing on building a stable and independent India.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

All three statements are accurate representations of the complex circumstances surrounding the partition. Lord Mountbatten's role in the partition is central to the event, though his decisions were criticized for their speed and the subsequent violence.  Gandhi, while a strong advocate for Hindu-Muslim unity, ultimately accepted the partition as a way to minimize further bloodshed, though he deeply regretted the decision. Nehru, though initially opposed, ultimately accepted the partition as a reality and focused on establishing a stable independent India.  His acceptance was a pragmatic decision in the face of escalating communal tensions and the imminent transfer of power.


**4.  With reference to the impact of colonial policies on Indian society, consider the following statements:**

1.  The Permanent Settlement, implemented by Lord Cornwallis, led to the consolidation of land ownership in the hands of Zamindars, often resulting in the exploitation of peasants.
2.  The Subsidiary Alliance System, introduced by Lord Wellesley, aimed to expand British influence by forging alliances with Indian princely states, often at the cost of their autonomy.
3.  The Government of India Act of 1935, while granting provincial autonomy, perpetuated communal divisions through the continuation of separate electorates.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Each statement correctly identifies a significant consequence of specific British colonial policies. The Permanent Settlement, though intended to stabilize revenue collection, concentrated land ownership among Zamindars, leading to the exploitation of tenant farmers and exacerbating rural inequalities.  Wellesley's Subsidiary Alliance System, while seemingly offering protection, effectively brought Indian princely states under British control, weakening their sovereignty and autonomy.  Lastly, the 1935 Act, while a step towards self-governance, reinforced communal divisions by maintaining separate electorates for different religious communities, which further fueled separatist sentiments.


**5. With reference to prominent figures in the Indian freedom struggle, consider the following statements:**

1.  Subhas Chandra Bose, known for his radical nationalist views, founded the Forward Bloc, advocating for complete independence through both constitutional and extra-constitutional means.
2.  Bhagat Singh, a revolutionary socialist, participated in the Non-Cooperation Movement, and later played a key role in the Hindustan Socialist Republican Association (HSRA).
3.  C. Rajagopalachari, a moderate nationalist, served as the last Governor-General of India, after the independence and partition of the country.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3

**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statements 1 and 2 are correct, while statement 3 is incorrect. Subhas Chandra Bose's founding of the Forward Bloc and his advocacy for complete independence are well-established facts.  Bhagat Singh's early involvement in the Non-Cooperation Movement and his later association with the HSRA are also accurate. However, C. Rajagopalachari was not the last Governor-General of India; that position was held by Lord Mountbatten.  Rajagopalachari did serve as Governor-General but only after the transfer of power to the Indian government.


These questions aim to test not just factual recall but also the ability to analyze and evaluate historical events and their interconnectedness, crucial skills for success in the UPSC examination.  The distractors are designed to be plausible, forcing candidates to carefully consider each statement based on their precise knowledge of the historical context.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided text, adhering to all specified criteria.  Each question includes a detailed explanation of the correct answer and why the other options are incorrect.

**1. With reference to the Indian National Congress, consider the following statements:**

1.  The Surat Session of the Indian National Congress witnessed a significant split between the Moderates and Extremists.
2.  Dadabhai Naoroji served as the President of the Indian National Congress on three separate occasions.
3.  The Indian National Congress's first session was held in Calcutta, Bengal.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The Surat Split of 1907 was a major event in the history of the Indian National Congress, marking a deep division between the Moderates and Extremists regarding the methods and goals of the nationalist movement. This split significantly impacted the Congress's effectiveness for several years.

Statement 2 is also correct. Dadabhai Naoroji, a prominent early leader of the Indian National Congress, held the presidency three times, showcasing his influence and stature within the organization.  His presidency symbolized the Congress's commitment to addressing economic exploitation and poverty in India.

Statement 3 is incorrect. The first session of the Indian National Congress was held in Bombay (now Mumbai) in December 1885, not in Calcutta.  While Calcutta hosted subsequent sessions and was a crucial center of nationalist activity, the inaugural session took place in Bombay.  This detail highlights the early Congress's attempt to establish a truly pan-Indian identity, starting from a location with diverse representation.


**2. With reference to the early years of the Indian National Congress (1885-1905), consider the following statements:**

1.  The early nationalists primarily focused on achieving complete independence immediately through mass movements.
2.  The Indian Councils Act of 1892, though partially fulfilling Congress demands, was widely criticized as inadequate.
3.  Gopal Krishna Gokhale and Dadabhai Naoroji advocated for dominion status within the British Empire as the Congress's primary goal during this period.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. The early nationalists, categorized as Moderates, adopted a gradualist approach, prioritizing constitutional reforms and working within the existing system to achieve a larger share in governance.  They believed that immediate demands for complete independence would invite harsh repression from the British government and hinder progress.

Statement 2 is correct. While the Indian Councils Act of 1892 expanded the Legislative Councils and allowed for some indirect Indian representation, it fell far short of the Congress's demands for substantial self-governance and control over the budget.  The Act's limitations fueled further nationalist agitation and strengthened the demand for more significant reforms.

Statement 3 is correct. Towards the end of the period (1904-1906),  Gopal Krishna Gokhale and Dadabhai Naoroji, though still advocating for a larger role for Indians within the British system, began openly advocating for self-government similar to that enjoyed by the self-governing colonies like Canada and Australia, a stepping stone towards greater autonomy.  This shift reflects a growing assertiveness within the Congress leadership.


**3. With reference to the roles of prominent figures in the Indian National Congress, consider the following statements:**

1.  Surendranath Banerjea and Ananda Mohan Bose were key figures in organizing the Indian National Conference, a precursor to the Indian National Congress.
2.  Bal Gangadhar Tilak, a prominent leader of the early Congress, strongly advocated for the immediate adoption of a policy of complete independence and mass civil disobedience.
3.  Kadambini Ganguly's address at a Congress session symbolized the involvement of women in the freedom struggle.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 and 3 only
(b) 1, 2, and 3
(c) 2 only
(d) 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. Surendranath Banerjea and Ananda Mohan Bose played pivotal roles in the formation of the Indian National Conference, which laid the groundwork for the establishment of the Indian National Congress in 1885. Their contribution highlights the early stages of organized nationalist activity in India.

Statement 2 is incorrect.  While Tilak was a significant figure in the nationalist movement, during the early Congress phase (1885-1905) his approach was not one of immediate complete independence and mass civil disobedience.  That approach emerged later in his career. The early Congress leaders, including Tilak, largely favored a more moderate and constitutional approach.

Statement 3 is correct. Kadambini Ganguly, the first woman graduate of Calcutta University, addressing a Congress session in 1890, is a significant symbolic moment illustrating the gradual inclusion of women in the nationalist movement and their growing role in public life.  This act signified the movement's aspiration for a more inclusive and egalitarian society.



**4. With reference to the economic policies advocated by early Indian nationalists (1885-1905), consider the following statements:**

1.  The nationalists championed the "Drain of Wealth" theory, arguing that British rule systematically depleted India's resources.
2.  They primarily advocated for the immediate nationalization of all major industries in India as a solution to economic backwardness.
3.  The Swadeshi movement promoted the boycott of British goods and the use of Indian-made products to stimulate domestic industries.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 and 3 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct.  Dadabhai Naoroji and other early nationalists developed and popularized the "Drain of Wealth" theory, which argued that British economic policies led to a systematic transfer of wealth from India to Britain, contributing significantly to India's poverty and economic stagnation. This theory became a cornerstone of the nationalists' economic critique of British rule.

Statement 2 is incorrect. The early nationalists did not advocate for the immediate nationalization of all major industries.  Their approach was more gradual and focused on promoting the development of Indian industries through measures such as tariff protection, government aid, and the Swadeshi movement.  Nationalization as a widespread policy came much later in the nationalist movement.

Statement 3 is correct. The Swadeshi movement, a key component of the early nationalists' economic strategy, actively promoted the boycott of British goods and encouraged the consumption of Indian-made products.  This was intended to boost domestic industries, create employment, and reduce India's economic dependence on Britain.  The burning of foreign cloth was a symbolic act within this movement.


**5.  With reference to the responses of the Indian National Congress to World War II, consider the following statements:**

1.  The Congress initially offered conditional support to the British war effort, linking it to the grant of independence after the war.
2.  Gandhi consistently advocated for unconditional support to Britain's war effort due to his opposition to fascism.
3.  Subhas Chandra Bose, along with some leftist leaders, opposed any Indian participation in the war effort, advocating for immediate independence through direct action.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 and 3 only
(b) 1, 2, and 3
(c) 2 only
(d) 1 only


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct.  The Indian National Congress, initially, offered conditional support to the British war effort, demanding a significant transfer of power and the promise of complete independence after the war. This position reflected the Congress's belief that India's participation should be tied to a clear commitment to self-governance.

Statement 2 is incorrect. While Gandhi harbored a strong dislike for fascism and Nazism, he did not consistently advocate for unconditional support to Britain's war effort. His position evolved and was subject to debate within the Congress leadership, ultimately leaning towards the conditional support mentioned in statement 1.  His primary concern remained Indian independence.

Statement 3 is correct. Subhas Chandra Bose, along with several leftist and socialist leaders within the Congress, vehemently opposed Indian participation in the war, viewing it as an imperialist conflict.  They argued that India's opportunity for independence lay in taking advantage of Britain's wartime vulnerabilities through direct action and mobilization of the masses.  This difference in approach contributed to the internal crisis within the Congress.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided text, adhering to all specified criteria.  Each question is followed by the correct answer and a detailed explanation.


**1. With reference to the Champaran Satyagraha, consider the following statements:**

1.  The Champaran Satyagraha, led by Mahatma Gandhi, primarily focused on addressing the grievances of indigo cultivators.
2.  The indigo planters in Champaran enforced a system where farmers were obligated to cultivate indigo on at least 3/20th of their land.
3.  The Champaran Satyagraha directly resulted in the complete abolition of the indigo cultivation system across Bihar.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 2 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The Champaran Satyagraha was indeed initiated to address the plight of indigo farmers who faced exploitative practices by British planters.  Gandhi's intervention marked a significant turning point in the Indian freedom struggle, demonstrating the power of non-violent resistance.

Statement 2 is also correct.  The text explicitly states that indigo cultivators were forced to allocate a significant portion (3/20th) of their land for indigo cultivation and sell it at dictated prices. This was a key grievance that fueled the Satyagraha.

Statement 3 is incorrect. While the Champaran Satyagraha brought about significant reforms and lessened the burden on indigo cultivators, it did not lead to the complete abolition of indigo cultivation across the entire Bihar region. The impact was localized to the Champaran district and surrounding areas, initiating broader land reforms.  The struggle highlighted the systemic injustices faced by Indian farmers under colonial rule and spurred further agrarian movements.

(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. While Dr. B.R. Ambedkar was crucial to the creation of the Indian Constitution, he was not the first Law Minister.  His focus was primarily on constitutional matters.

Statement 2 is incorrect. The provided text does not mention M.C. Setalvad's role as Law Minister.  While he was a significant legal figure, the information provided doesn't confirm his position as the first Law Minister.

Statement 3 is correct.  The text mentions Kailash Nath Katju's involvement in the INA prisoners defense, and it is factually accurate that he held the position of the first Law Minister of India.  This demonstrates the diverse backgrounds and experiences of individuals who shaped independent India's legal framework.

Statement 2 is also correct. The passage indicates Curzon's administration was characterized by increased official control and centralization, reflecting his imperialistic approach to governance.

Statement 3 is incorrect.  The passage implies that the nationalist movement, including figures like Gokhale, critically analyzed and opposed Curzon's policies rather than supporting them.  Gokhale represented a moderate approach to nationalism but was certainly not a supporter of Curzon's policies.  The comparison underscores the contrasting perspectives on British rule in India.

Statement 2 is incorrect. The provided text does not mention any reconciliation between the Moderates and Extremists at the Lahore Session of 1929. The text focuses on the 1907 split and subsequent events.

Statement 3 is correct. While not explicitly stating a formal split, the text indicates that tensions and disagreements between the two factions were already present and growing by the Calcutta Session of 1906, setting the stage for the later formal split at Surat.  The evolution of these internal divisions within the Congress is a crucial aspect of understanding the nationalist movement's trajectory.

Statement 3 is incorrect. The provided text does not support the assertion that the conquest was swift and bloodless. Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided target content, adhering to all specified criteria.  Each question includes the correct answer and a detailed explanation.


**1. With reference to the Indian independence movement and key figures, consider the following statements:**

1.  Rabindranath Tagore's association with the Neo art movement significantly influenced his nationalist writings.
2.  Jawaharlal Nehru's left-wing Congress affiliations were directly opposed to Mahatma Gandhi's ideology.
3.  Subhas Chandra Bose's criticism of the Government of India Act, 1919, stemmed from its perceived limitations on Indian self-rule.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 and 3 only
(b) 3 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3
(d) 2 only

**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. Tagore's artistic leanings and his involvement in the Neo art movement deeply informed his understanding and expression of Indian nationalism in his literary works.  His artistic vision played a crucial role in shaping his nationalist viewpoints.

Statement 2 is incorrect. While there were differences between Nehru and Gandhi's approaches to achieving independence, it's an oversimplification to say Nehru's left-wing affiliations were directly *opposed* to Gandhi's ideology.  Both were within the Congress, and while they had contrasting views on socialist approaches, they ultimately collaborated for independence.

Statement 3 is correct. Bose vehemently criticized the Government of India Act, 1919, as it did not grant substantial self-governance to India. His dissatisfaction fueled his departure from the Congress and his formation of the Forward Bloc, reflecting his strong desire for complete independence.  The Act's limitations on Indian autonomy were a core reason for his opposition.


**2. With reference to the Archaeological Survey of India (ASI) and its functions, consider the following statements:**

1.  The ASI's establishment predates the Ancient Monuments Preservation Act, 1904.
2.  The ASI is solely responsible for the restoration of all ancient monuments in India, including those in private ownership.
3.  The National Mission for Manuscripts (NMM) operates independently of the ASI, despite the ASI's recommendation for its establishment.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) None

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. The ASI was established *after* the need for a dedicated body to manage and protect India's historical heritage became apparent, eventually leading to the  Ancient Monuments Preservation Act, 1904, which formalized its role.  The Act provided the legal framework for the ASI's operations.

Statement 2 is incorrect. The ASI's responsibility primarily covers centrally protected monuments.  Private ownership of historical sites and their management and restoration lie outside the ASI's direct purview, though they may offer guidance and support in some cases.

Statement 3 is correct. Although the ASI recommended the establishment of the NMM, the NMM functions as a separate entity under the Ministry of Culture.  The ASI played a key role in advocating for the preservation of manuscripts, but the two organizations maintain distinct operational frameworks.


**3. With reference to the roles and policies of various British viceroys in India, consider the following statements:**

1.  Lord Curzon's interpretation of "ultimate self-government" aligned with the immediate granting of complete independence to India.
2.  Lord Wellesley's subsidiary alliance system primarily aimed to counteract the influence of the French in India.
3.  Lord William Bentinck's administration directly involved the annexation of Awadh.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 2 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. Lord Curzon's vision of "ultimate self-government" was a gradual and conditional process, not a commitment to immediate independence. He believed in a slow and controlled transition towards greater Indian autonomy, firmly within the framework of British imperial rule.

Statement 2 is correct. A primary goal of Lord Wellesley's subsidiary alliance system was to neutralize the threat posed by French influence in India, creating a buffer against potential French expansion.  This system was a key element of his foreign policy.

Statement 3 is correct. Lord William Bentinck's administration was involved in the complex events surrounding the annexation of Awadh, although the process was not solely under his direct control and involved various factors and political considerations.  The annexation was a significant event during his tenure.


**4. With reference to prominent figures in the Indian National Congress and their contributions, consider the following statements:**

1.  Dadabhai Naoroji's "Drain theory" focused primarily on the negative impact of British rule on Indian industrial development.
2.  Bal Gangadhar Tilak's support for the Swadeshi movement was solely focused on economic self-reliance and not on political demands.
3.  Sarojini Naidu's leadership within the Indian National Congress was primarily restricted to women's issues.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) None
(d) 1 and 3 only

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. While Dadabhai Naoroji's Drain theory highlighted the economic exploitation of India by the British, it encompassed broader aspects of British economic policies and their impact on Indian poverty and overall economic backwardness, not just industrial development.

Statement 2 is incorrect. Tilak's involvement in the Swadeshi movement had both economic and political dimensions. He used the movement as a means to challenge British rule and promote both economic self-sufficiency and political assertion.

Statement 3 is incorrect.  Sarojini Naidu played a significant role in the Indian National Congress, extending far beyond women's issues. She was a powerful orator, a key figure in several movements, and even served as the president of the INC, demonstrating her broad leadership contributions.


**5. Consider the following statements regarding the Non-Cooperation Movement:**

1. The Chauri Chaura incident directly led to the complete cessation of the Non-Cooperation Movement.
2.  The Khilafat Movement's objectives were entirely separate from those of the Non-Cooperation Movement.
3. The participation of diverse social groups, including tribals and workers, was limited to specific regions in the Non-Cooperation Movement.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) None

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. The Chauri Chaura incident, while a significant factor, did not lead to the *complete* cessation of the Non-Cooperation Movement immediately.  Gandhiji suspended the movement's mass civil disobedience aspects but did not entirely abandon it.

Statement 2 is incorrect. While the Khilafat Movement had its distinct focus on defending the Ottoman Caliphate, it ran concurrently with and was closely intertwined with the Non-Cooperation Movement, sharing some common goals and participants.

Statement 3 is correct. While the Non-Cooperation Movement saw widespread participation from various social groups, the extent and nature of their involvement varied across different regions of India.  The movement's impact and participation were not uniform across the country.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple choice questions based on the provided text, adhering to all specified criteria.  Each question includes the correct answer and a detailed explanation.


**1. With reference to the early Indian nationalist movement (1885-1905), consider the following statements:**

1.  The Moderate nationalists primarily employed constitutional agitation and believed in gradual, orderly political progress.
2.  Dadabhai Naoroji, known as the "Grand Old Man of India," significantly contributed to the movement through his economic writings, highlighting British exploitation.
3.  The Indian Association, founded in Calcutta, focused solely on reforming the Civil Service regulations and raising the age limit for its examination.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 2 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a) 1 and 2 only

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 accurately describes the approach of Moderate nationalists who prioritized constitutional methods and a phased approach to political advancement, believing in gradual reforms within the existing legal framework.  Statement 2 correctly identifies Dadabhai Naoroji's significant role, highlighting his contribution through economic analyses exposing the exploitative nature of British rule and his immense influence as a leader.  However, statement 3 is incorrect. While the Indian Association did campaign for Civil Service reforms and age limit changes, its activities extended far beyond this.  It also engaged in agitations against repressive laws like the Arms Act and the Vernacular Press Act and championed the cause of tenants against zamindars and workers in tea plantations.  The association's focus was broader, aiming to create a unified Indian political consciousness and a common political program.  Therefore, only statements 1 and 2 are entirely accurate representations of the early nationalist movement.


**2. With reference to Mahatma Gandhi's early Satyagraha campaigns in India, consider the following statements:**

1. The Ahmedabad Mill Strike of 1918 saw Gandhi employ a fast-unto-death to secure a 50% wage increase for mill workers.
2. The Champaran Satyagraha (1917) primarily addressed the grievances of indigo planters against oppressive revenue demands imposed by the British government.
3.  Gandhis intervention in the Khaira peasant struggle in Gujarat involved supporting their resistance against land revenue collection following crop failure.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 3 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 2 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a) 3 only

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect.  While Gandhi did use a fast-unto-death in the 1918 Ahmedabad Mill Strike, the wage increase secured was 35%, not 50%. Statement 2 is also incorrect. The Champaran Satyagraha focused on the plight of the peasantry oppressed by European indigo planters, who forced them to cultivate indigo on a portion of their land and sell it at exploitative prices. It was not primarily about revenue demands imposed by the British government directly on the indigo planters.  Statement 3 correctly describes Gandhi's support for the Khaira peasants during crop failure, highlighting his commitment to aiding the rural population facing economic hardship. Thus, only statement 3 is entirely accurate.


**3. Consider the following statements regarding the Jallianwala Bagh Massacre:**

1. The massacre took place on April 13, 1919, as a direct response to Gandhi's call for a hartal.
2. General Dyer, the military commander of Amritsar, ordered the firing into the trapped crowd in Jallianwala Bagh to terrorize the population into submission.
3. The massacre prompted a wave of horror across India, leading to widespread protests against the curtailment of jury powers and the disarming of the Indian populace.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 2 and 3 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a) 2 and 3 only

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is partially incorrect. While the massacre did occur on April 13, 1919, it was not a direct response to Gandhi's call for a hartal on April 6th, although the hartal and the growing unrest certainly contributed to the tense atmosphere. The massacre was a reaction to the broader protests and defiance in the Punjab following the arrests of Dr. Saifuddin Kitchlu and Dr. Satyapal. Statement 2 accurately depicts General Dyer's actions and motives.  Statement 3 is correct in highlighting the widespread outrage and protests following the massacre, leading to demands concerning jury powers and the right to bear arms for self-defense, reflecting the deep-seated resentment against British oppression and the desire for greater civil liberties.  Therefore, only statements 2 and 3 are fully accurate.


**4. With reference to the growth of the Indian National Congress, consider the following statements:**

1.  A. O. Hume, a retired British civil servant, played a crucial role in the founding of the Indian National Congress in 1885.
2. The "safety valve" theory suggests that the Congress was primarily intended to divert popular discontent away from armed rebellion.
3.  The early Congress was dominated by wealthy and aristocratic Indians, excluding the participation of the masses.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?


(a) 1, 2, and 3
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 2 and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (a) 1, 2, and 3

**Explanation:**

All three statements accurately reflect aspects of the Indian National Congress's early development. Statement 1 correctly attributes A. O. Hume's significant role in the Congress's establishment. Statement 2 accurately describes the "safety valve" theory, which posited that the Congress served as a controlled channel for releasing popular discontent, thereby preventing potential widespread uprisings. Statement 3 accurately notes the initial dominance of wealthy and aristocratic Indians in the Congress's leadership and membership, although this would change over time as the movement broadened its base and became more inclusive.  Therefore, all three statements are correct.


**5. With reference to the impact of Western thought and education on the Indian nationalist movement, consider the following statements:**

1.  The introduction of Western education invariably led to the immediate rejection of Indian traditions and culture among educated Indians.
