Here are some UPSC-style multiple choice questions based on the provided text, adhering to all specified criteria.  Remember, the difficulty is designed to be high, reflecting the challenging nature of the UPSC exam.

**1. Consider the following statements regarding the Non-Cooperation Movement:**

1.  The movement's widespread participation included significant contributions from urban Muslim communities, alongside other social groups.
2.  The Chauri Chaura incident, marked by violence, directly led to the movement's abrupt termination.
3.  The movement's primary objective was the attainment of "Purna Swaraj," or complete self-rule.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The Non-Cooperation Movement saw substantial participation from urban Muslim communities, fueled by the Khilafat movement and broader anti-imperialist sentiments.  This diverse participation extended beyond urban centers, involving various social groups across India.

Statement 2 is incorrect. While the Chauri Chaura incident, characterized by violence against police, was a significant factor, it did not directly cause the immediate and complete termination of the movement.  Gandhi's decision to suspend the movement was a complex response to the incident, reflecting his commitment to non-violence and concerns about the movement's direction.  The movement gradually lost steam after this incident and was not abruptly ended.

Statement 3 is correct.  The ultimate goal of the Non-Cooperation Movement was the achievement of "Purna Swaraj," or complete self-rule for India. This overarching aim guided the movement's strategies and actions, even though the methods employed were largely non-violent.

Therefore, only statements 1 and 3 are accurate.


**2. With reference to the Swadeshi Movement, consider the following statements:**

1.  The movement's economic impact primarily included a significant reduction in foreign cloth imports, a key objective.
2.  The movement's ideological spectrum encompassed both conservative moderation and political extremism, reflecting internal divisions.
3.  The Partition of Bengal directly triggered the Swadeshi Movement, serving as its immediate cause.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 2 and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. While the Swadeshi Movement did promote the boycott of foreign goods and encouraged the use of Indian-made products,  a significant *reduction* in foreign cloth imports is an oversimplification.  The movement's economic impact was multifaceted and its success in reducing imports varied regionally.

Statement 2 is correct. The Swadeshi Movement was characterized by a wide range of ideologies and approaches.  It encompassed both the more moderate, reformist views and the more radical, extremist factions within the Indian nationalist movement.  This internal diversity shaped the movement's strategies and actions.

Statement 3 is correct. The Partition of Bengal directly sparked the Swadeshi Movement as a form of organized resistance against British policies. The partition was a key catalyst, uniting diverse groups in opposition to British rule.

Therefore, only statements 2 and 3 are accurate.


**3. With reference to the Quit India Movement, consider the following statements:**

1.  The movement's leadership, including Gandhi, was arrested in early August 1942, leading to widespread spontaneous uprisings.
2. The Muslim League actively participated in and supported the Quit India Movement's objectives.
3.  The movement witnessed the establishment of several "parallel governments" in different regions of India, challenging British authority.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 3 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The mass arrests of Congress leaders, including Gandhi, on August 9, 1942, triggered widespread spontaneous protests and civil disobedience across India, demonstrating the depth of nationalist sentiment.  The lack of organized leadership fueled the movement's often decentralized and sometimes violent nature.


Statement 2 is incorrect. The Muslim League actively *opposed* the Quit India Movement, fearing that the British withdrawal might leave the Muslim minority vulnerable to the Hindu majority. The League's position reflected its distinct political goals and concerns about the future of India.


Statement 3 is correct.  The Quit India Movement did lead to the formation of several underground "parallel governments" in various regions of India. These temporary administrations, often operating in rural areas, aimed to demonstrate the potential for self-governance and to challenge British control at the local level.


Therefore, only statements 1 and 3 are accurate.


**4. With reference to the Cripps Mission, consider the following statements:**

1.  The mission proposed the creation of a Constituent Assembly to draft a new constitution for India after the war.
2.  The mission offered full independence to India immediately upon its conclusion.
3.  Winston Churchill, the British Prime Minister at the time, strongly supported and endorsed the Cripps Mission's proposals.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. A key proposal of the Cripps Mission was the creation of a Constituent Assembly to frame a new constitution for India. This was a significant element of the mission's attempt to address Indian demands for self-governance and constitutional reform.

Statement 2 is incorrect. The Cripps Mission did *not* offer full independence to India immediately. Instead, it proposed a path towards dominion status after the Second World War, a proposal that was ultimately rejected by the Indian National Congress.

Statement 3 is incorrect. Winston Churchill was deeply skeptical of the Cripps Mission and its concessions to Indian nationalists. He opposed the proposals, believing they would weaken British authority and undermine the war effort.  His opposition highlights the internal divisions within the British government regarding India's future.

Therefore, only statement 1 is accurate.


**5.  With reference to the Individual Satyagraha, consider the following statements:**

1.  Vinoba Bhave was the first Satyagrahi selected for the campaign, initiating the movement.
2.  Sardar Vallabhbhai Patel was the second Satyagrahi chosen to participate in the campaign.
3.  The Individual Satyagraha was launched by the Indian National Congress as a direct response to the failure of the Cripps Mission.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 2 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct.  Vinoba Bhave was indeed the first Satyagrahi selected for the Individual Satyagraha campaign, launched by the Congress. His participation marked the beginning of this phase of non-violent resistance.

Statement 2 is incorrect.  The second Satyagrahi was Jawaharlal Nehru, not Sardar Vallabhbhai Patel.  This sequence of participants is a significant detail in understanding the strategic choices of the Congress.

Statement 3 is correct. The Individual Satyagraha was a direct response to the failure of the Cripps Mission to address Indian demands for self-governance and independence.  It was a carefully planned strategy by the Congress to maintain pressure on the British government.

Therefore, only statements 1 and 3 are accurate.


**6. With reference to the Shimla Conference, consider the following statements:**

1. Lord Mountbatten was the Viceroy when the Shimla Conference took place.
2. The conference aimed to reconstruct the Viceroy's Executive Council, with a significant increase in Indian representation.
3.  The conference successfully resulted in the formation of an interim government with a balanced representation of Congress and Muslim League members.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 2 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect.  Lord Wavell, not Lord Mountbatten, was the Viceroy during the Shimla Conference.  This distinction is crucial in understanding the historical context of the conference and its outcomes.

Statement 2 is correct. The central objective of the Shimla Conference was to reconstruct the Viceroy's Executive Council, substantially increasing the number of Indian members. This was an attempt to address Indian demands for greater participation in governance.

Statement 3 is incorrect. The Shimla Conference ultimately *failed* to achieve its goal of forming an interim government with balanced representation.  The disagreements between the Congress and the Muslim League regarding the allocation of seats prevented a successful resolution.

Therefore, only statement 2 is accurate.


**7. With reference to the Interim Government formed in 1946, consider the following statements:**

1.  Jawaharlal Nehru held the portfolio of Defence in the Interim Government.
2.  The Interim Government included representatives from both the Indian National Congress and the Muslim League.
3. Dr. Rajendra Prasad held the portfolio of Food and Agriculture in the Interim Government.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 2 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. Jawaharlal Nehru was the Prime Minister of the Interim Government, but he did *not* hold the Defence portfolio.  This portfolio was held by another prominent leader.

Statement 2 is correct. The Interim Government was a significant step towards power transfer and included members from both the Congress and the Muslim League, though the League later withdrew.

Statement 3 is incorrect. Dr. Rajendra Prasad was the President of the Constituent Assembly, not a member of the Interim Government. He did not hold any portfolio in this government.

Therefore, only statement 2 is accurate.


**8. With reference to the resolution of 'Purna Swaraj', consider the following statements:**

1.  The resolution was passed at the Lahore session of the Indian National Congress.
2.  Jawaharlal Nehru was the President of the Indian National Congress when the resolution was passed.
3.  The resolution unequivocally demanded complete independence for India.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 3 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The Lahore session of the Indian National Congress in 1929 is where the 'Purna Swaraj' resolution was adopted. This session marks a significant turning point in the Indian independence movement.

Statement 2 is incorrect. Jawaharlal Nehru was not the President of the Indian National Congress at the Lahore session.  Another prominent leader held the presidency during this crucial session.

Statement 3 is correct. The 'Purna Swaraj' resolution explicitly and unequivocally demanded complete independence for India, marking a shift towards a more assertive and radical approach to the struggle against British rule.

Therefore, only statements 1 and 3 are accurate.



**9. Consider the following statements about the activities associated with prominent figures during the Indian freedom struggle:**

1.  Rajendra Prasad was prominently associated with the Champaran Satyagraha.
2.  Morarji Desai was prominently associated with the Ahmedabad Mill Workers' Satyagraha.
3.  Vallabhbhai Patel was prominently associated with the Kheda Satyagraha.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. Rajendra Prasad played a significant role in the Champaran Satyagraha, supporting Gandhi's efforts to address the grievances of the indigo farmers.  His involvement highlights the collaborative nature of the movement.

Statement 2 is correct.  Morarji Desai's participation in the Ahmedabad Mill Workers' Satyagraha is well documented.  His contributions demonstrate his early involvement in the Indian freedom struggle and his commitment to workers' rights.

Statement 3 is correct.  Vallabhbhai Patel's leadership in the Kheda Satyagraha is a well-known event in Indian history. His organizational skills and political acumen were crucial to the success of this movement.

Therefore, all three statements are accurate.


**10. With reference to the Congress Ministries in the provinces, consider the following statements:**

1.  The Congress Ministries resigned in 1939 primarily due to the Viceroy's decision to involve India in the Second World War without consulting the Congress.
2.  The Congress Ministries implemented several measures to ease restrictions on the press and restore civil liberties.
3.  The resignation of the Congress Ministries significantly weakened the Indian nationalist movement's overall strength and influence.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The Congress Ministries' resignation in 1939 was a direct consequence of the Viceroy's decision to declare war on Germany without seeking the consent of the elected provincial governments. This action highlighted the lack of self-governance and fueled nationalist resentment.

Statement 2 is correct. During their tenure, the Congress Ministries implemented several progressive measures to ease restrictions on the press and to restore civil liberties, showcasing their commitment to democratic principles.

Statement 3 is incorrect. The resignation of the Congress Ministries did not weaken the Indian nationalist movement.  Rather, it solidified the Congress's opposition to British rule and created the conditions for future mass movements.  The period after the resignation saw continued growth in the strength and influence of the Congress.

Therefore, only statements 1 and 2 are accurate.

**55. With reference to the Indian National Congress's strategies during the pre-independence era, consider the following statements:**

1.  The Congress Working Committee's authorization to launch Civil Disobedience was formally decided at the Lahore Session.
2.  The Gandhi-Irwin Pact resulted in the temporary suspension of the Civil Disobedience Movement and Congress participation in the Second Round Table Conference.
3.  The Nehru Report, adopted at the Calcutta Session, unequivocally demanded complete independence (Purna Swaraj) as the Congress's primary goal.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a) 1 and 2 only

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct.  The Lahore Session of the Indian National Congress in 1929 is indeed where the Working Committee received the mandate to launch a program of Civil Disobedience, including non-payment of taxes.  This marked a significant shift towards a more assertive approach to achieving independence.

Statement 2 is also correct. The Gandhi-Irwin Pact of 1931, a significant agreement between Mahatma Gandhi and Lord Irwin, led to the temporary suspension of the Civil Disobedience Movement.  A key element of this pact was the Congress's agreement to participate in the Second Round Table Conference to discuss constitutional reforms. This represented a strategic decision by the Congress to engage in negotiations while retaining its ultimate goal of independence.

Statement 3 is incorrect. While the Nehru Report, approved at the Calcutta Session of 1928, did advocate for dominion status, it did *not* unequivocally demand complete independence (Purna Swaraj) as its primary goal.  The demand for Purna Swaraj was a later development, gaining momentum among younger Congress leaders and eventually adopted at the Lahore Session in 1929.  The Calcutta Session's emphasis was on dominion status within a reasonable timeframe, reflecting a more gradualist approach at that stage. The younger leaders' dissatisfaction with this more moderate stance is a key aspect of the historical context.  This difference in the timeline and the ultimate goal of the Nehru Report versus the later Purna Swaraj resolution demonstrates the evolving strategies within the Congress.


**56. With reference to the political landscape of India during the 1930s, consider the following statements:**

1. The Government of India Act of 1935 introduced provincial autonomy, replacing the earlier diarchy system.
2.  The Poona Pact, signed in 1932, abolished separate electorates for the depressed classes, but increased their reserved seats in legislative bodies.
3. The Congress ministries formed in several provinces after the 1937 elections fully cooperated with the provisions of the Government of India Act of 1935, aiming for a smooth transition to dominion status.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a) 1 and 2 only

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is accurate. The Government of India Act of 1935 is a landmark legislation that significantly altered the governance structure in British India. A key feature was the introduction of provincial autonomy, replacing the earlier diarchy system which involved a division of power between Indian ministers and British officials. This marked a step towards greater self-governance at the provincial level.

Statement 2 is also correct. The Poona Pact, a crucial agreement reached between Mahatma Gandhi and B.R. Ambedkar in 1932, directly addressed the issue of representation for the depressed classes (Dalits).  A key outcome was the abandonment of the separate electorates proposed in the Communal Award, which would have created separate voting systems for different religious and caste groups.  While separate electorates were abolished, the Poona Pact did result in an increase in the number of reserved seats for the depressed classes in legislative assemblies, aiming for more inclusive representation.

Statement 3 is incorrect. While the Congress did win a majority in several provincial assemblies in the 1937 elections and formed ministries, they did *not* fully cooperate with the provisions of the Government of India Act of 1935.  The Congress remained fundamentally opposed to the Act, viewing it as a tool of continued British control despite the introduction of autonomy.  The Congress ministries used their positions to advance their own agenda of self-governance and social reform, often clashing with the Governor's reserved powers and the limitations imposed by the Act.  The Congress's ultimate goal remained complete independence, not dominion status under the British Crown.  The Congress's ambivalent relationship with the Act and its eventual resignation from provincial governments highlight the complex political dynamics of the era.


**57. With reference to the Quit India Movement, consider the following statements:**

1. The movement was launched immediately following the failure of the Cripps Mission.
2.  Mahatma Gandhi's call for the movement involved urging government servants to resign from their posts.
3.  The movement saw significant participation from various groups, including socialists, communists, and members of the Forward Bloc, although with varying degrees of commitment and coordination.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3
(d) 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (b) 2 and 3 only

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. While the failure of the Cripps Mission in 1942 certainly contributed to the atmosphere of discontent and heightened the demand for independence, the Quit India Movement was not launched immediately *after* the mission's failure. There was a period of deliberation and strategic planning within the Congress before the launch of the movement on August 8, 1942.

Statement 2 is correct. A key aspect of Mahatma Gandhi's call for the Quit India Movement was his appeal to government servants to resign from their positions. This was a significant element of the movement's strategy, aiming to disrupt the administrative machinery of the British Raj and demonstrate widespread opposition to colonial rule.

Statement 3 is also correct. The Quit India Movement saw participation from a broad spectrum of groups within the Indian nationalist movement.  Socialists, communists, and members of the Forward Bloc were among those involved, though their participation was not always fully coordinated or aligned with the Congress's overall strategy.  The differing ideologies and approaches within the movement contributed to its decentralized and often spontaneous nature.  The involvement of these diverse groups reflects the broader anti-colonial sentiment prevalent at the time.


**58. With reference to the pre-independence era in India, consider the following statements:**

1. Subhas Chandra Bose's Forward Bloc was formed after he broke away from the Indian National Congress in 1939 following disagreements over the strategy of the freedom movement.
2.  The All India Federation, envisioned under the Government of India Act of 1935, was successfully established, incorporating both British Indian provinces and princely states.
3. The Simon Commission's report, published in 1930, strongly recommended the immediate grant of dominion status to India.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a) 1 only

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct.  Subhas Chandra Bose's departure from the Indian National Congress in 1939 and the subsequent formation of the Forward Bloc is a well-documented event in Indian history.  The split resulted from fundamental disagreements with Mahatma Gandhi and other Congress leaders regarding the strategy for achieving independence. Bose advocated for a more aggressive and potentially less non-violent approach.

Statement 2 is incorrect. The All India Federation, a key component of the Government of India Act of 1935, was *never* successfully established.  The Act's provisions for the federation were conditional upon the accession of a significant number of princely states, which did not materialize due to various political factors and the reluctance of many princely rulers to join a federal structure under the British Raj.

Statement 3 is incorrect. The Simon Commission's report, published in 1930, did *not* recommend the immediate grant of dominion status to India.  In fact, the report was widely criticized for its lack of Indian representation in its drafting and for its failure to adequately address the issue of dominion status.  The report's conservative recommendations fueled further nationalist agitation and contributed to the growing demand for complete independence.  The report's shortcomings are a crucial element in understanding the trajectory of the Indian independence movement.

**1. With reference to Jawaharlal Nehru's role in India's independence and early years, consider the following statements:**

1.  Jawaharlal Nehru, while a key figure in the Constituent Assembly,  initially advocated for dominion status rather than complete independence.
2.  Nehru's vision for India's foreign policy, as articulated after independence, strongly emphasized non-alignment and peaceful co-existence, diverging significantly from the policies of some other prominent leaders.
3.  The Nehru-Liaquat Pact, signed in 1950, primarily focused on resolving the issue of princely states' integration into the Indian Union, showcasing his pragmatic approach to national unity.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect.  While Nehru initially engaged with the idea of Dominion Status within the British Commonwealth,  his ultimate goal and the position he championed within the Congress was Purna Swaraj (complete independence).  His advocacy for complete independence is well documented throughout the Indian freedom struggle. The statement misrepresents his evolving stance, suggesting a preference for dominion status which is inaccurate.

Statement 2 is correct.  Nehru's vision for India's foreign policy, which he significantly shaped, was rooted in non-alignment. This policy aimed at maintaining independence from both the US-led Western bloc and the Soviet-led Eastern bloc during the Cold War.  This approach, however, was not universally accepted by all leaders within India, reflecting differing geopolitical perspectives.  His emphasis on peaceful co-existence and international cooperation is a core tenet of his foreign policy legacy, contrasting with more assertive or regionally focused approaches.

Statement 3 is incorrect. The Nehru-Liaquat Pact, signed between Jawaharlal Nehru and Liaquat Ali Khan in 1950, primarily aimed at protecting the rights of minorities in both India and Pakistan.  It addressed issues such as the security and welfare of minority communities in the aftermath of the Partition, not the integration of princely states.  The integration of princely states was largely achieved through Sardar Vallabhbhai Patel's efforts as the Home Minister.  This statement confuses the focus and subject matter of the pact.


**2. With reference to the Cripps Mission of 1942, consider the following statements:**

1. The Cripps Mission explicitly guaranteed complete independence to India immediately upon the conclusion of World War II, aiming to secure India's full cooperation in the war effort.
2. A key proposal of the Cripps Mission was the formation of a Constituent Assembly to draft a new constitution for India, with the proviso that any province could opt out and form a separate independent state.
3.  The Cripps Mission's failure was primarily due to the unwavering opposition of Mahatma Gandhi, who vehemently rejected any compromise with the British government.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 2 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. The Cripps Mission offered dominion status, not immediate complete independence.  While the aim was to secure Indian support for the war effort, the offer fell short of the Congress's demand for immediate independence. The mission's proposal of dominion status after the war was a significant point of contention.

Statement 2 is correct. The Cripps Mission did indeed propose a Constituent Assembly to frame a new constitution for India.  Crucially, the plan included a provision allowing provinces to opt out of the Indian Union and forge their own independent paths, a clause that directly contributed to the partition of India.  This option for secession was a major point of contention and a key factor in the mission's ultimate failure.

Statement 3 is incorrect. While Gandhi was critical of the Cripps Mission's proposals, it was not solely his opposition that led to its failure.  The Muslim League also voiced significant objections, primarily concerning the lack of a clear commitment to the creation of Pakistan.  Furthermore, the British government's own reservations and the lack of a commitment to immediate power transfer also significantly hindered the mission's success.  Attributing the failure solely to Gandhi's opposition is an oversimplification of a complex political situation.


**3. With reference to the Partition of India in 1947, consider the following statements:**

1. The Radcliffe Line, the boundary dividing India and Pakistan, was meticulously drawn based on detailed demographic data and pre-existing administrative boundaries, minimizing displacement and conflict.
2. The division of assets and personnel of the Indian Civil Service (ICS) and the armed forces was a smooth and orderly process, ensuring minimal disruption to governance and national security.
3.  The assassination of Mahatma Gandhi was directly caused by the failure of the Nehru-Liaquat Pact to adequately address the grievances of Hindu refugees from Pakistan.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) None
(b) 1 only
(c) 2 only
(d) 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. The Radcliffe Line was drawn hastily and with limited information, leading to significant displacement and communal violence.  It did not accurately reflect demographic realities or existing administrative boundaries in many areas, causing considerable unrest and conflict along the border regions.

Statement 2 is incorrect. The division of assets and personnel was far from smooth.  It was a chaotic process that led to considerable confusion and conflict, particularly within the armed forces.  The hasty nature of the partition meant that many decisions were made under immense pressure, contributing to the widespread violence.  The allocation of resources and personnel was a major source of tension between India and Pakistan.

Statement 3 is incorrect. While the assassination of Gandhi was influenced by the political climate of the time, including the refugee crisis, it was not directly caused by the failure of the Nehru-Liaquat Pact.  Nathuram Godse, Gandhi's assassin, had a complex set of motivations, including his opposition to Gandhi's perceived appeasement of Muslims. The pact aimed to improve relations and address minority concerns but was unable to prevent the political turmoil that ultimately led to Gandhi's death.  The statement presents a simplistic and inaccurate causal link.


**4.  With reference to the Indian National Congress's internal debates and strategies during the 1930s, consider the following statements:**

1. Subhas Chandra Bose's election as Congress President in 1938 marked a significant shift towards a more radical and militant approach to the freedom struggle, leading to a major split within the Congress.
2. Jawaharlal Nehru consistently advocated for a complete abandonment of constitutional politics and a complete shift to non-violent mass movements, even during periods of relative political calm.
3.  The Government of India Act of 1935, while introducing provincial autonomy, included significant safeguards that limited Indian self-governance and ultimately failed to satisfy nationalist aspirations.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 3 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is largely correct.  Bose's election did represent a shift towards a more assertive and potentially more militant approach.  While not leading to an immediate, complete split, it exacerbated existing tensions within the Congress between those favoring a more gradual, constitutional approach and those who preferred a more radical and possibly violent struggle for independence. The differences in ideology and strategy between Bose and Gandhi contributed to internal conflict.

Statement 2 is incorrect.  While Nehru was critical of relying solely on constitutional methods and advocated for mass movements, he didn't consistently call for a complete abandonment of constitutional politics. His approach was more nuanced, recognizing the potential value of participation in legislatures as a tool for political engagement and mobilization, even while pushing for more direct action when necessary.

Statement 3 is correct. The Government of India Act of 1935 did grant provincial autonomy.  However, the Act retained significant safeguards and "special responsibilities" for the Governor-General and Governors, limiting the extent of self-governance and leaving ultimate power in British hands.  These limitations ultimately failed to appease nationalist demands for complete self-determination.  The Acts provisions were widely criticized as inadequate.
